Apostate's Authority Over Children's Property
Explaining the ruling on apostate and harbi's agency over children's property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on an apostate's transaction regarding his children's property, distinguish the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the condition of unity of religion (ittihad al-millah) to determine validity.

Core Idea
An apostate's authority over children's property is suspended due to lack of unity of religion.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah tackles a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: does an apostate (murtad) or a harbi (enemy non-Muslim) retain authority over their Muslim children's property? The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that such authority is suspended (mawquf) because guardianship of consideration (wilayah nazariyyah) requires unity of religion between guardian and ward. The ruling pivots on the apostate's eventual fate—return to Islam versus death in apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling for the Apostate's Own Property
According to Sahibayn, the apostate's transaction in his own property is valid (nafidh). This forms the baseline: apostasy does not strip all capacity.
Imam Abu Hanifa reportedly agrees on this point.
2
State the Ruling for Children's Property
The apostate's transaction regarding his children's (or parents') property is suspended (mawquf), not immediately valid or invalid. This suspension is by consensus (ijma') among the Hanafi school.
The suspension means the transaction awaits a condition: return to Islam or death.
3
Analyze the Basis: Wilayah Nazariyyah and Ittihad al-Millah
A father's authority over his children is a guardianship of consideration (wilayah nazariyyah), rooted in natural affection. But affection presumes shared religion; since the apostate's religion wavers, the unity (ittihad al-millah) is absent, precluding valid authority.
This reasoning is unique to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may emphasize blood relation alone.
4
Determine the Outcome Based on the Apostate's Fate
If the apostate returns to Islam, his Islam is considered continuous, so the transaction becomes valid. If he is killed on apostasy, dies, or flees to dar al-harb, the severance of authority is confirmed retroactively, rendering the transaction invalid.
This conditional retroactivity is a key Hanafi principle.
5
Extend to the Harbi by Analogy
The harbi is even further from Islam than a dhimmī (who already lacks authority over Muslims), so the same suspension applies to his transactions over Muslim children's property.
The analogy (qiyas) strengthens the argument for stripping authority.

Source Text

دارالحرب میں چلا گیا تو اس کا تصرف نافذ نہ ہوگا کیونکہ باپ کی ولایت اولاد اور مال اولاد پر نظری ہے یعنی باپ کو اپنی اولاد اور اولاد کے مال پر ولایت اس لئے حاصل ہوتی ہے کہ باپ اولاد کے حق میں مشفق ہوتا اسکو اسلام کی توفیق نہ ہو ۔ حال جب مرتد کو بحالت ردت قتل کر دیا گیا تو باپ اور اولاد کے درمیان اتحادیلت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی ولایت کا منقطع ہونا ہو گیا اور جب اسکی ولایت کا منقطع ہونا محقق ہو گیا تو اس کا تصرف بھی باطل ہو جائے گا اور اگر مرتد نے اسلام قبول کر لیا تو اسلام قبول کرنے کی وجہ سے ایسا ہو گیا گویا وہ برابر مسلمان چلا آرہا ہے اور جب اس صورت میں مسلمان چلا آ رہا ہے تو اتحاد ملت کی وجہ اسکی ولایت منقطع نہ ہوگی اور جب ولایت منقطع نہیں ہوتی تو اس کا تصرف بھی جائز اور نافذ ہوگا۔
Book of Agency. So when a slave and a mukatab lack ability and a dhimmī kafir lacks affection, they will not have authority, and when they have no authority, their transactions are not valid. When an apostate is killed in his apostasy, his transaction regarding his own property is valid, but it is suspended regarding the property of his father and son; the same ruling applies to the harbi. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The apostate when killed on his apostasy, and the harbi likewise, because the harbi is further from the dhimmī, so he is more deserving of having authority stripped. As for the apostate, his transaction in his own property is valid according to them, but it is suspended regarding his son and his son's property by consensus, because it is a guardianship of consideration, and that depends on agreement of religion, and it is wavering. Then the aspect of severance becomes established when he is killed on apostasy, and Islam makes it as if he never ceased being a Muslim. Commentary: Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said that when the apostate is killed on his apostasy, and the harbi similarly, because the harbi, even if he is a musta'min, is further from the dhimmī, meaning the dhimmī is closer to Muslims compared to the harbi, and it has passed that a dhimmī has no authority over a Muslim, so the harbi is more deserving of having no authority over a Muslim. As for the apostate, his transaction in his own property is valid according to them, but his transaction regarding his children and their property is suspended by consensus. That is, if the apostate becomes Muslim, his transaction is valid, but if he does not become Muslim but is killed or dies or goes to dar al-harb, his transaction is not valid, because a father's authority over his children and their property is based on consideration, i.e., a father has authority over his children and their property because he is affectionate towards them, but consideration and affection between father and son exist only when both have the same religion, while here the apostate's religion is wavering; it is possible he will accept Islam again or not. When the apostate is killed in apostasy, due to lack of unity of religion between father and children, his authority is severed, and when his authority is confirmed severed, his transaction becomes invalid. If the apostate accepts Islam, due to Islam it becomes as if he has been a Muslim continuously, so unity of religion exists, his authority is not severed, and his transaction is valid and effective.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of an apostate (murtad) and a harbi (non-Muslim from dar al-harb) regarding their authority (wilayah) over their children and their children's property. The text begins by stating the general principle: a slave and a mukatab lack power (qudrah), and a dhimmī kafir lacks affection (shafqah), so they have no authority; consequently, their transactions are invalid. Similarly, an apostate killed on apostasy and a harbi have their own rulings. The core issue is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad). According to the Sahibayn, an apostate's transaction in his own property is valid, but his transaction regarding his father's and son's property is suspended (mawquf) by consensus. This is because the father's authority over his children is a guardianship of consideration (wilayah nazariyyah), which depends on unity of religion (ittihad al-millah) for affection to exist. Since the apostate's religion is wavering (mutaraddid), the unity is absent. If he is killed on apostasy, the severance of authority becomes established retroactively, and his transaction becomes invalid. This is based on the principle that the apostate's Islam is considered as if he never left, but only if he returns to Islam; if he is killed, the severance is confirmed. The Sahibayn also liken the harbi to the apostate, as the harbi is even further from the dhimmī, who already has no authority over a Muslim. Imam Abu Hanifa's view is implied in the earlier statement that the apostate's transaction in his own property is valid and in the father's property is suspended; the commentary elaborates the Sahibayn's reasoning. The passage emphasizes that the ruling is nuanced and depends on the outcome of the apostate's status.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtad): An apostate; a Muslim who renounces Islam. The text discusses his legal capacity regarding transactions during apostasy.
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim from dar al-harb (territory at war with Muslims). The text considers him as lacking authority over Muslim children.
ولاية نظرية (wilayah nazariyyah): Guardianship of consideration; authority based on affection and care for the ward's welfare.
اتحاد الملة (ittihad al-millah): Unity of religion between the guardian and the ward; necessary for wilayah nazariyyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), what happens to an apostate's transaction regarding his child's property if he is killed on apostasy?
A) It becomes valid because he died as a Muslim.
B) It becomes invalid because the aspect of severance is confirmed.
C) It remains suspended indefinitely.
D) It is valid only if the child consents.

Key Takeaway
An apostate's transaction over a Muslim child's property is suspended until the apostate either returns to Islam (making it valid) or dies in apostasy (making it invalid).

Agency for Litigation and Taking Possession: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Fatwa Change
Intra-Hanafi dispute with fatwa change due to custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi fatwa changed from the original position that an agent for litigation is also an agent for possession, and apply the principle of custom (urf) in ruling on agency.

Core Idea
The original Hanafi ruling grants litigation agents possession authority, but changed custom now restricts it due to prevalent dishonesty.

This lesson explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute: does an agent appointed to litigate also have the right to take possession of the adjudicated property? The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) said yes, based on the principle that ownership of a thing includes its completion. But Imam Zufar said no, distinguishing litigation (verbal) from possession (physical). Over time, due to widespread treachery among agents, the fatwa shifted to Zufar's view, showing how custom can override even a well-established ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the issue and the two positions: the Hanafi majority (including Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) versus Imam Zufar.
Note that Zufar's view is now mufta bihi.
2
Analyze the Hanafi majority proof
Examine the principle 'man malaka shay'an malaka itmāmah' (whoever owns something owns its completion) and how it applies to litigation culminating in possession.
This proof is from the original narration.
3
Analyze Zufar's argument
Understand the distinction between litigation (speech) and possession (physical act), and why consent to one does not imply consent to the other.
Supported by other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali).
4
Understand the fatwa change
Recognize the role of custom (urf) and prevalent treachery in shifting the operative ruling to Zufar's view.
Custom can override literal positions in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Extend to analogous case
Apply the same reasoning to the agent for debt collection (wakīl bil-taqāḍī): originally had possession authority, but now custom restricts it.
Reinforces the impact of urf over time.

Source Text

كتاب الوكالة
باب الوكالة بالخصومة والقبض
ترجمہ یہ باب خصومت کرنے اور قبضہ کرنے کی وکالت کے بیان میں ہے وکیل بالخصومت وکیل بالقبض ہے یا نہیں
قال الوكيل بالخصومة وكيل بالقبض عندنا خلافا لزفر هو يقول انه رضى بخصومة والقبض غير الخصومة ولم يرض به ولنا ان من ملک شیئا ملک اتمامه و تمام الخصومة وانتهاؤها بالقبض والفتوى اليوم على قول زفر لظهور الخيانة فى الوكلاء وقد يؤتمن على الخصومة من لايؤتمن على المال ونظيره الوكيل بالتقاضي يملك القبض على اصل الرواية لانه في معناه وضعاً الا ان العرف بخلافه وهو قاض على الوضع فالفتوى على ان لا يملك
ترجمہ صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ ہمارے نزدیک وکیل بالخصومت وکیل بالقبض بھی ہوتا ہے امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے امام زفر کہتے ہیں که موکل خصومت پر راضی ہوا ہے اور قبضہ، خصومت کے علاوہ ہے اور موکل اس پر راضی نہیں ہوا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو شخص کسی چیز کا مالک ہوا وہ اس کو پورا کرنے کا مالک ہو گیا۔ اور خصومت کو پورا کرنا اوراس و انبار تک پہنچانا قبضہ سے ہوتا ہے اور آج کل امام زفر کے قول پر توئی ہے۔ کیونکہ وکیلوں میں خیانت ظاہر کو ہوگئی اور کبھی اس شخص کی خصومت پر اطمینان ہوتا ہے جس کے مال وصول کرنے پر اطمینان نہیں ہوتا اس کی نظیر قرضہ طلب کرنے کا وکیل اصل روایت کے مطابق قبضہ کرنے کا مالک بھی ہوتا ہے کیونکہ افت میں نقاضی قبضہ کے معنی میں ہے مگر یہ کہ عرف اس کیخلاف ہے اور عرف ، وضع پر حاکم ہوتا ہے لیکن فتویٰ اس پر ہے کہ تقاضی کا وکیل قبضہ کا بالک نہ ہو گا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے ایک شخص نے دوسرے شخص پر قرضہ کا دعوی کیا اور مدعی نے خصومت اور مقدمہ کی پیروی کے لئے کسی کو وکیل کیا پس اگر مدعی علیہ پر قرضہ ثابت ہو گیا تو وکیل بالخصومت اس قرضہ کو وصول کرنے اور اس پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل ہوگا یا نہیں اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے احناف میں سے امام زفر کے نزدیک وکیل بالخصومت وکیل بالقبض نہیں ہوگا امام شافعی کا ظاہری قول بھی یہی ہے۔ امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ذ ہب بھی یہی ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کا ایک قول وہ ہے جو امام صاحب اور صاحبین کا ہے۔ امام ز فر فر ماتے ہیں کہ خصومت اور قبضہ میں تغایر ہے کیونکہ خصومت وہ قول ہے جو اظہار حقوق کے لئے بولا جاتا ہے اور قبضہ فعل حسی ہے اور موکل وکیل کے خصومت کرنے پر راضی ہو ا ہے اس کے قبضہ کرنے پر راضی نہیں ہوا کیونکہ خصومت کے لئے ایسا آدمی منتخب کیا جاتا ہے جو تیز طراز اور چالاک ہوا اور قبضہ کے لئے امانتدار آدمی کا انتخاب کیا جاتا ہے۔
پس جو آدمی خصومت کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے لوگ عادہ اسکی امانت و دیانت پر راضی نہیں ہوتے لہذا ثابت ہوا کہ مؤکل وکیل کی خصومت پر تو راضی ہے لیکن اس کے قبضہ کرنے پر راضی نہیں اور جب مؤکل ، وکیل بالخصومت کے قبضہ پر راضی نہیں ہے تو وکیل بالقبض بھی نہ ہو گا۔
Book of Agency. Chapter on Agency for Litigation and Taking Possession. Translation: This chapter explains agency for litigation and taking possession; whether the agent for litigation is also agent for taking possession. He (al-Quduri) said: The agent for litigation is agent for taking possession in our school, contrary to Zufar. He says: The principal consented to litigation, and possession is different from litigation, and he did not consent to it. And our proof is that whoever owns something owns its completion, and the completion of litigation and its ending is by possession. And the fatwa today is on Zufar's statement due to the appearance of treachery among agents, and sometimes one is trusted with litigation who is not trusted with money. Its analogy is the agent for debt collection: he possesses the right of taking possession according to the original narration because it is in its meaning by convention, except that custom is contrary to it, and custom overrides the literal position, so the fatwa is that he does not possess it. Commentary: The scenario: A person claimed a debt against another, and the plaintiff appointed someone as agent for litigation and pursuing the case. If the debt is proven against the defendant, will the agent for litigation also be the agent for collecting and taking possession of that debt? There is a dispute. Among the Hanafis, Imam Zufar says the agent for litigation is not agent for taking possession. Imam al-Shafi'i's apparent saying is the same, and Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad's school is also the same. Imam al-Shafi'i has another saying which is that of our Imam (Abu Hanifa) and the two Sahibayn. Imam Zufar says there is a difference between litigation and possession because litigation is speech used to manifest rights, while possession is a physical act. The principal consented to the agent's litigation, not to his possession, because for litigation a sharp and clever person is chosen, while for possession a trustworthy person is chosen. Therefore, the person who has the ability for litigation, people are usually not satisfied with his trustworthiness and honesty. Hence it is established that the principal consented to the agent's litigation but not to his possession, and since the principal did not consent to the agent's possession, he is not an agent for taking possession.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage addresses the chapter 'Agency for Litigation and Taking Possession', focusing on whether an agent authorized for litigation (wakīl bil-khusūmah) is also authorized to take possession (qabḍ) of the subject matter after winning the case. The Hanafi school's position, as stated by al-Quduri, is that such an agent is also an agent for possession, based on the principle 'whoever owns something owns its completion' (man malaka shay'an malaka itmāmah). The completion of litigation is possession. However, Imam Zufar (a Hanafi imam) disagreed, arguing that litigation and possession are distinct: litigation is verbal, possession is physical; a principal may choose a skilled litigator who may not be trustworthy for handling money. The text notes that today's fatwa follows Zufar's view due to the prevalence of treachery (khiyānah) among agents. An analogy is drawn to the agent for debt collection (wakīl bil-taqāḍī), who originally also had the right to take possession according to the original narration (aṣl al-riwāyah), but custom (urf) overrides that, so fatwa is that he does not possess that right. The commentary elaborates the scenario and the reasoning of both sides, concluding that due to the different capacities required for litigation vs. possession, the principal's consent for one does not imply consent for the other, especially given current circumstances.

Key Terms
وکیل بالخصومة (wakīl bil-khusūmah): An agent authorized to litigate on behalf of the principal in a legal case.
وکیل بالقبض (wakīl bil-qabd): An agent authorized to take physical possession of property, such as collecting a debt.
تمام الخصومة (tamām al-khusūmah): The completion or culmination of litigation, which is achieved by taking possession of the adjudicated property.
عرف (urf): Custom; prevalent practice among people that can override the literal meaning of a contract or rule.

Checkpoint

A) The agent for litigation is also the agent for possession.
B) The agent for litigation is not the agent for possession due to prevalent treachery.

Litigation Agent and Taking Possession: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Shift in Fatwa
Intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of agency for litigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the original Hanafi ruling on a litigation agent's authority to take possession, explain Zufar's objection, and apply the current fatwa (mufta bihi) based on changed circumstances.

Core Idea
The completion of litigation is taking possession, but the fatwa today restricts the agent due to prevalent dishonesty.

In Hanafi agency law, a person appointed to litigate (wakil bil-khusumah) was originally also authorized to take possession of the recovered property. However, Imam Zufar dissented, arguing that litigation and possession are distinct acts requiring different qualities. Due to increased dishonesty among agents, later Hanafi authorities adopted Zufar's view as the operative fatwa. This lesson examines the proof of the majority, Zufar's counterargument, and the rationale for the shift.

Guided Path
1
State the original Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn: the litigation agent is also an agent for taking possession. The principal's consent to litigation implies consent to its completion.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the rational principle 'man malaka shayan malaka itmamah' (whoever owns a thing owns its completion). The completion of litigation is taking possession, so the agent must have that right.
3
Examine Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that litigation (speech) and possession (physical act) are distinct and require different qualities (eloquence vs. trustworthiness). The principal's consent to one does not extend to the other.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the original ruling, the litigation agent can take possession without separate authorization. Under Zufar's view, he cannot. This affects whether the principal must appoint a separate agent for collection.
5
Understand the fatwa shift
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Marghinani) adopted Zufar's view due to widespread dishonesty among agents, making it the mufta bihi for contemporary practice.
This illustrates how Hanafi fatwa can adapt to changing social conditions (taghayyur al-ahkam bi taghayyur al-zaman).

صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اس مسئلہ کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ تقاضی یعنی قرضہ کی ادائیگی کے مطالبہ کا وکیل مبسوط کی روایت کے مطابق اس پر قبضہ کا وکیل بھی ہوگا یعنی جس شخص کو قرضدار کے قرضہ کے مطالبہ کرنے کا وکیل کیا گیا ہے وہی اس قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل بھی ہوگا یعنی یہ وکیل مطالبہ بھی کرے گا اور اس پر قبضہ بھی کرے گا کیونکہ لفظ تقاضی لغت کے اعتبار سے قبضہ کے ہم معنی ہے پس جب یہ لفظ قبضہ کے ہم معنی ہے تو اس لفظ تقاضی کے ذریعہ وہ شخص مطالبہ اور قبضہ دونوں کا وکیل ہوگا۔ لیکن عرف لغت کے برخلاف ہے کیونکہ عرف میں لفظ تقاضی سے صرف مطالبہ کے معنی سمجھے جاتے ہیں اور قبضہ کے معنی نہیں سمجھے جاتے اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ عرف لغت سے راجح ہوتا ہے یعنی عرف اور لغت میں تعارض کے وقت عرف کو ترجیح دی جائے گی اور جب یہاں عرف راج ہے تو فتوی اسی پر ہوگا کہ تقاضی اور مطالبہ کا وکیل دین پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل نہیں ہو گا اور اس وکیل کو قرضہ پر قبضہ کا اختیار حاصل نہیں ہوتا۔
Book of Agency. Chapter on Agency for Litigation and Taking Possession. He (al-Quduri) said: The agent for litigation is also agent for taking possession according to us, contrary to Zufar. He (Zufar) says: He (the principal) consented to litigation, and taking possession is other than litigation, and he did not consent to it. Our proof: Whoever owns a thing owns its completion, and the completion and conclusion of litigation is by taking possession. And the fatwa today is according to Zufar's statement due to the appearance of betrayal among agents. Sometimes one is trusted with litigation who is not trusted with property. Its analogy is that the agent for demanding payment (taqadi) has the right to take possession according to the original narration, because it is in its meaning according to the linguistic usage, except that custom is contrary to it, and custom prevails over linguistic usage. So the fatwa is that he does not have the right.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether an agent appointed for litigation (wakil bil-khusumah) is also authorized to take possession (qabd) of the property recovered. The original Hanafi position, held by Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), is that the litigation agent does have the authority to take possession. Their proof is rational: whoever owns a thing (here, the right to litigate) owns its completion, and the completion of litigation is taking possession of the claimed property. Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that litigation and taking possession are distinct acts; the principal's consent to one does not imply consent to the other. He noted that litigation requires eloquence and sharpness, while taking possession requires trustworthiness, and the two qualities often do not coexist. The text then states that the current fatwa (fatwa al-yawm) follows Zufar's view due to increased dishonesty among agents. The commentator further explains that this ruling is analogous to the case of an agent for demanding payment (taqadi): originally, such an agent could take possession because the word 'taqadi' linguistically implies taking possession, but custom uses it only for demanding, so the fatwa follows custom. Thus, the practical ruling today is that a litigation agent cannot take possession unless explicitly authorized.

Key Terms
وكيل بالخصومة (wakīl bil-khuṣūmah): An agent appointed to represent the principal in litigation, i.e., to plead and conduct a court case.
وكيل بالقبض (wakīl bil-qabḍ): An agent authorized to take physical possession of property (e.g., receiving a debt).
الفتوى اليوم (al-fatwā al-yawm): The fatwa that is operative in the present time, taking into account current circumstances (e.g., prevalence of dishonesty).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the current fatwa, if a person is appointed only as a wakil bil-khusumah (agent for litigation), can he take possession of the debt recovered?
A) Yes, because the completion of litigation requires taking possession.
B) No, because litigation and taking possession are distinct acts and the principal did not consent to the latter.
C) Yes, but only if the agent is also trustworthy.
D) No, unless the principal explicitly authorized him in writing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab allows fatwa to shift based on changing social conditions, even within the school, as seen in the dispute over the litigation agent's authority.

Joint Litigation Agents: Requirement for Collective Possession
Ruling on two joint litigation agents jointly taking possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on two joint litigation agents taking possession and explain the ratio legis (the principal's trust in both agents together).

Core Idea
Two joint litigation agents must take possession together because the principal relied on both of their trustworthiness.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a critical nuance in joint agency. While co-agents may act independently in litigation, taking possession of the recovered property requires their collective action. The reason lies in the nature of the principal's trust: he reposed confidence in both agents as a pair, not in each individually. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of agency in commercial and legal transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal actors
Two agents appointed jointly for litigation (wakīlayn bil-khuṣūmah). They are co-agents, not independent agents.
Joint agency means both are named together in the appointment.
2
Pinpoint the specific action
Taking possession (qabḍ) of the debt recovered through litigation. This is a physical act of receiving payment.
Distinguish from litigation itself, which may not require joint presence.
3
Identify the ruling
The agents must take possession together; one alone cannot validly do so.
The ruling is conditional: if they take possession together, it is valid; if singly, it is invalid.
4
Extract the dalil (proof)
The principal consented to the trustworthiness of both agents together, not to one individually. Therefore, the act must involve both.
This is a rational proof (dalīl ‘aqlī): the principal’s intent is determined by the wording of the appointment.
5
Note the contrast with litigation
In litigation, joint presence may not be required due to procedural feasibility; here, joint possession is possible and thus required.
The author refers to an earlier passage where joint presence for litigation was not mandated.

Source Text

قال فان كانا وكيلين بالخصومة لا يقبضان الامعالانه رضى باما نتهما لا بامانة احدهما واجتماعهما ممكن بخلاف الخصومة على مامر
ترجمہ اور اگر خصومت کے دو وکیل ہوں تو قرضہ پر دونوں ایک ساتھ قبضہ کر سکتے ہیں اس لئے کہ مؤکل ان دونوں کی امانت پر راضی ہوا ہے نہ کہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کی امانت پر اور ان دونوں کا جمع ہو ناممکن بھی ہے برخلاف خصومت کے چنانچہ گذر چکا۔ تشریح مسئلہ: اگر دو آدمی خصومت کے وکیل ہوں اور مال پر قبضہ کرنے کی نوبت آجائے تو یہ دونوں ملکر قبضہ کر سکتے ہیں صرف ایک کا قبضہ معتبر نہ ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ موکل دونوں وکیلوں کی امانت پر راضی ہوا ہے نہ کہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کی امانت پر۔ لہذا دونوں کا قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے اور ان دونوں کا اجتماع شرعا ممکن بھی ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ دونوں وکیل ایک ساتھ جمع ہو کر قبضہ کر لیں ۔ اس کے برخلاف خصومت کے دو وکیل کہ ان دونوں کا اجتماع چونکہ شرعاً
He said: If they are two agents for litigation, they may not take possession except together, because he (the principal) consented to the trustworthiness of both, not to the trustworthiness of one of them, and their coming together is possible, unlike litigation as has passed.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where two people are appointed as joint agents for litigation (wakilani bil-khusumah). When it comes to taking possession of the property (e.g., receiving a debt), both agents must act together. The reason is that the principal has placed his trust in both agents collectively, not in each individually. Therefore, taking possession by only one of them is not valid; they must both be present and jointly take possession. This is possible to arrange, unlike the act of litigation itself, where joint presence may not be required or feasible (as explained earlier in the text: due to the nature of court proceedings). The commentator emphasizes that the joint action is necessary because the trust is placed in the pair, and it is physically possible for them to meet and take possession together.

Key Terms
وكيلين بالخصومة (wakīlayn bil-khuṣūmah): Two agents jointly appointed to conduct litigation; they must act together in taking possession.
قبض (qabḍ): Taking physical possession of property (e.g., receiving a debt).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two people are appointed as joint agents for litigation (wakilani bil-khusumah), can one of them alone take possession of the debt recovered?
A) Yes, because each agent has full authority.
B) No, because the principal trusted both together, so both must be present.
C) Yes, but only if the other agent is unavailable.
D) No, because taking possession requires a separate agency.

Key Takeaway
Two joint litigation agents must jointly take possession because the principal's trust is in their collective trustworthiness, not individually.

Wakil for Litigation and Possession: The Fatwa Shift to Imam Zufar
Intra-Hanafi dispute with analogy to custom ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a wakil for litigation is automatically a wakil for possession, and state the mufta bihi position and its rationale based on custom and necessity.

Core Idea
The fatwa shifted: a litigation agent today is not automatically an agent for collecting the debt — custom and necessity override the original analogy.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: if a principal appoints an agent to litigate a debt claim, does that appointment automatically authorize the agent to take possession of the debt upon winning? The original Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) said yes, because the purpose of litigation is possession. However, Imam Zufar disagreed, and later authorities like Sahib al-Hidayah adopted his view due to increased dishonesty among agents. We will trace the reasoning, the shift, and an analogous case of 'taqadi' (demanding payment) that illustrates how custom ('urf) can modify legal interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What is the specific question: does a wakil for litigation (وكيل بالخصومة) automatically have the authority to take possession (قبض) of the debt? Recognize that this is an intra-Hanafi disagreement.
The dispute is about the scope of an agent's authority derived from the principal's appointment.
2
State the original Hanafi view and its proof
The original view holds that the agent for litigation is also agent for possession. The proof is rational: whoever is made owner of a task is owner of its completion; litigation of a debt is not complete until possession is taken. Trace this argument in the text.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the nature of agency.
3
Present Imam Zufar's opposing view
Imam Zufar argues that the agent for litigation is not automatically agent for possession. The basis is practical: increased betrayal among agents; a principal may trust an agent's legal skills but not his integrity in handling money.
Zufar's view is based on changed social circumstances and the need to protect principals.
4
Explain the fatwa shift
Sahib al-Hidayah explicitly states that the fatwa now follows Zufar. Identify the two reasons: widespread betrayal and the possibility that a principal trusts one's litigation but not money collection. Understand that the mufta bihi is Zufar's view.
The shift illustrates the principle that rulings can change with changing conditions (taghayyur al-ahkam bi taghayyur al-zaman).
5
Analyze the analogy with taqadi and the rule of custom
The passage draws an analogy: a wakil for demanding payment (taqadi) was originally considered wakil for possession because linguistically 'taqadi' means possession. But custom restricted it to mere demand, and custom prevails over language. This supports Zufar's view by showing that custom can limit apparent authority.
The rule 'al-ʿurfu muḥakkam' (custom is authoritative) applies here.

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص کو کسی چیز کا مالک بنایا گیا تو وہ اس کو مکمل کرنے اور اس کو انتہاء تک پہنچانے کا مالک ہو گا لہذا خصومت کا وکیل خصومت کو مکمل کرنے اور اس کو انتہا تک پہنچانے کا وکیل ہوگا اور خصومت کی تکمیل قبضہ سے ہوتی ہے یعنی قرضہ کے سلسلہ میں خصومت کا وکیل جب تک قرضہ پر قبضہ نہیں کرے گا اس وقت تک اس کی خصومت مکمل نہ ہوگی اور جب قرضہ کی خصومت بغیر قبضہ کے مکمل نہیں ہوتی تو جو شخص خصومت کا وکیل ہوگا وہ قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل بھی ضرور ہوگا خواہ مؤکل نے اس کو قبضہ کا وکیل کیا ہو یا نہ کیا ہو۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ آج کل فتویٰ امام زفر کے قول پر ہی دیا جائے گا کیونکہ آج کل وکیلوں میں خیانت زیادہ ہوگئی ۔ اور بسا اوقات ایسا ہوتا ہے کہ ایک وکیل کی خصومت پر تو اعتماد و اطمینان ہوتا ہے لیکن اس کے مال وصول کرنے پر اطمینان نہیں ہوتا پس ایسی صورت میں اس کو خصومت کا وکیل تو کیا جا سکتا ہے لیکن قبضہ کا وکیل نہیں کیا جاسکتا بہر حال جب یہ بات ہے تو فتوی یہی ہو گا کہ خصومت کا وکیل خصومت ہی کا وکیل رہے گا اور قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اس مسئلہ کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ تقاضی یعنی قرضہ کی ادائیگی کے مطالبہ کا وکیل مبسوط کی روایت کے مطابق اس پر قبضہ کا وکیل بھی ہوگا یعنی جس شخص کو قرضدار کے قرضہ کے مطالبہ کرنے کا وکیل کیا گیا ہے وہی اس قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل بھی ہوگا یعنی یہ وکیل مطالبہ بھی کرے گا اور اس پر قبضہ بھی کرے گا کیونکہ لفظ تقاضی لغت کے اعتبار سے قبضہ کے ہم معنی ہے پس جب یہ لفظ قبضہ کے ہم معنی ہے تو اس لفظ نقاضی کے ذریعہ وہ شخص مطالبہ اور قبضہ دونوں کا وکیل ہوگا۔ لیکن عرف لغت کے برخلاف ہے کیونکہ عرف میں لفظ تقاضی سے صرف مطالبہ کے معنی سمجھے جاتے ہیں اور قبضہ کے معنی نہیں سمجھے جاتے اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ عرف لغت سے راجح ہوتا ہے یعنی عرف اور لغت میں تعارض کے وقت عرف کو ترجیح دی جائے گی اور جب یہاں عرف راج ہے تو فتوی اسی پر ہوگا کہ تقاضی اور مطالبہ کا وکیل دین پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل نہیں ہو گا اور اس وکیل کو قرضہ پر قبضہ کا اختیار حاصل نہیں ہوتا۔
Our proof is that if a person is made owner of something, he becomes owner of completing it and bringing it to its end. Therefore, the wakil for litigation is the wakil for completing the litigation and bringing it to its end. And the completion of litigation occurs through possession (qabd), meaning that in matters of debt, the wakil for litigation's litigation is not complete until he takes possession of the debt. And when the litigation of debt is not completed without possession, then whoever is wakil for litigation is necessarily also wakil for taking possession of the debt, whether the principal appointed him as wakil for possession or not. Sahib Hidayah says that nowadays fatwa is given only on the view of Imam Zufar because nowadays betrayal by agents has increased. And sometimes it happens that there is confidence and trust in an agent's litigation but not in his collection of money; in such a case, he can be appointed wakil for litigation but cannot be appointed wakil for possession. In any case, since this is so, the fatwa is that the wakil for litigation remains only wakil for litigation and will not be wakil for taking possession of the debt.
Sahib Hidayah said that the analogy for this issue is that the wakil for demanding payment (taqadi) according to the narration of al-Mabsut is also wakil for possession, meaning that the person appointed as wakil for demanding payment from the debtor is also wakil for taking possession of that debt; this wakil will both demand and take possession because the word taqadi in language is synonymous with possession. So when this word is synonymous with possession, then by this word taqadi, that person will be wakil for both demanding and possession. But custom ('urf) contradicts language because in custom the word taqadi conveys only the meaning of demanding, not possession. And the rule is that custom prevails over language, meaning that when custom and language conflict, custom is given preference. And since here custom prevails, the fatwa is accordingly that the wakil for demanding payment (taqadi) and claiming is not wakil for taking possession of the debt, and this wakil does not have the authority to take possession.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah begins by presenting the original Hanafi proof that a wakil for litigation (وکیل بالخصومة) is automatically also a wakil for taking possession (وکیل بالقبض) of the debt, because the goal of litigation is to obtain the debt, which requires possession. However, the author then cites Sahib al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) who states that the fatwa has shifted to Imam Zufar's view: due to widespread betrayal among agents, a wakil for litigation is not automatically a wakil for possession; a principal may trust someone's legal skill but not their financial trustworthiness. The passage then draws an analogy with taqadi (demanding payment): according to al-Mabsut, a wakil for taqadi is also wakil for possession because linguistically taqadi means possession; but this is overridden by custom ('urf), which restricts taqadi to mere demanding. Since custom prevails over language, a wakil for demanding payment is not a wakil for possession. This establishes a consistent principle that custom can modify legal interpretations.

Key Terms
وكالة (wakālah): Agency; the delegation of authority from one person (principal) to another (agent) to perform a specific task.
خصومة (khuṣūmah): Litigation; the legal proceedings to establish a right or claim before a judge.
قبض (qabḍ): Taking possession; physical or constructive control over the subject matter (e.g., receiving payment of a debt).
تقاضی (taqāḍī): Demanding payment of a debt; the act of asking the debtor to fulfill the obligation.
عرف (ʿurf): Custom; prevalent practice in a particular society that can influence legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Sahib al-Hidayah shift the fatwa to Imam Zufar's view?
A) Because Imam Zufar provided a stronger Quranic proof.
B) Because agents became more trustworthy, making the original ruling unnecessary.
C) Because betrayal by agents increased, and principals need protection.
D) Because the majority of Hanafi scholars always followed Zufar.

Key Takeaway
The fatwa in the Hanafi school has shifted from the original view that a litigation wakil is automatically a possession wakil to Imam Zufar's view that explicit authorization is required, due to increased dishonesty and the principle that custom can override literal reasoning.

Joint Possession by Two Litigation Wakils
Ruling that two litigation agents must act together to collect debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that two litigation wakils must jointly take possession of a debt and explain the underlying rationale based on the principal's consent and feasibility of joint action.

Core Idea
Two litigation wakils must take possession together – joint trust requires joint action when possible.

This lesson examines a specific Hanafi rule: when two persons are appointed as agents for litigation (wakīlān bi-al-khuṣūmah), any subsequent taking of possession of the debt must be done jointly. The passage contrasts this with the litigation itself, where one agent can appear alone. The key insight is that the principal's consent was given to the combined trustworthiness of both agents, and since joint physical action is possible, it is obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the taking of possession (qabḍ) of a debt by two wakils for litigation. The ruling: both must take possession together; one alone cannot.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the principal's consent: 'because the principal consented to the trustworthiness of both, not the trustworthiness of one of them.'
This is a rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī) from the nature of agency.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Since the principal trusted both agents collectively, each action requiring their trust must involve both together. The possibility of joint action (ijtimāʿ mumkin) makes this requirement binding.
4
Compare the contrasting case
For litigation itself, joint appearance is not required because it is often impossible for both to attend court simultaneously; here the ijtimaʿ is not possible, so the rule is relaxed.
The passage refers to 'unlike litigation, as has passed'.
5
Understand the underlying principle
The ruling is based on two elements: the principal's intent (the type of trust) and the feasibility of joint action. Where feasibility exists, the principal's intent must be honored fully.
This principle can be extended to other joint agencies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خصومت کے دو وکیل ہوں تو قرضہ پر دونوں ایک ساتھ قبضہ کر سکتے ہیں
قال فان كانا وكيلين بالخصومة لا يقبضان الامعالانه رضى باما نتهما لا بامانة احدهما واجتماعهما ممكن بخلاف الخصومة على مامر
ترجمہ اور اگر خصومت کے دو وکیل ہوں تو قرضہ پر دونوں ایک ساتھ قبضہ کر سکتے ہیں اس لئے کہ مؤکل ان دونوں کی امانت پر راضی ہوا ہے نہ کہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کی امانت پر اور ان دونوں کا جمع ہو ناممکن بھی ہے برخلاف خصومت کے چنانچہ گذر چکا۔ تشریح مسئلہ: اگر دو آدمی خصومت کے وکیل ہوں اور مال پر قبضہ کرنے کی نوبت آجائے تو یہ دونوں ملکر قبضہ کر سکتے ہیں صرف ایک کا قبضہ معتبر نہ ہوگا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ موکل دونوں وکیلوں کی امانت پر راضی ہوا ہے نہ کہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کی امانت پر۔ لہذا دونوں کا قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے اور ان دونوں کا اجتماع شرعا ممکن بھی ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ دونوں وکیل ایک ساتھ جمع ہو کر قبضہ کر لیں ۔ اس کے برخلاف خصومت کے دو وکیل کہ ان دونوں کا اجتماع چونکہ شرعاً ناممکن اور معذ رہے جیسا کہ پہلے گذر چکا ہے۔ اس لئے خصومت کے لئے وکیلوں کیلئے مجلس قاضی میں اجتماع ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ اگر ایک وکیل بھی مقدمہ پیش کر دے گا تو درست ہوگا۔
If there are two wakils for litigation, they can take possession of the debt only together [both]. Because the principal was satisfied with the trustworthiness of both, not the trustworthiness of one of them, and their meeting together is possible, unlike litigation as has passed.
Translation: And if there are two wakils for litigation, then both can take possession of the debt together, because the principal consented to the trust of both, not the trust of one of them, and their joining together is not impossible, unlike litigation as has passed. Explanation of the issue: If two persons are wakils for litigation and the occasion for taking possession of the property arises, then both can take possession jointly; the possession of only one will not be valid.
The proof is that the principal consented to the trust of both wakils, not to the trust of one of them. Therefore, it is necessary for both to take possession, and their meeting together is legally possible, in the sense that both wakils can gather together and take possession. In contrast, for two wakils for litigation, their meeting together is legally impossible and excused, as has passed. Therefore, for litigation, it is not necessary for the wakils to meet in the court; rather, if even one wakil presents the case, it will be valid.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling: when two persons are appointed as agents for litigation concerning a debt, they must act jointly to take possession of that debt. The reasoning is that the principal's consent was given to the combined trustworthiness of both agents, not to either individually. Since joint action is physically possible (they can both be present together to receive the money), this is required. This contrasts with the rule for litigation itself, where two wakils need not appear together; one may present the case because it is often impractical for both to attend court simultaneously. The proof (dalīl) is based on the principal's presumed intent (رضا) and the capacity for joint performance.

Key Terms
وكيلان بالخصومة (wakīlān bi-al-khuṣūmah): Two agents specifically appointed to handle litigation (court proceedings) for a debt.
أمانة (amānah): Trustworthiness or fiduciary responsibility; the quality that the principal relies upon in the agent.
اجتماع (ijtimāʿ): The meeting or joint presence of the two agents for a particular action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two persons are appointed as wakils for litigation, how must they take possession of the debt?
A) Either one can take possession alone.
B) Both must take possession together.
C) The principal must designate one of them for possession.
D) They cannot take possession at all.

Key Takeaway
Two litigation wakils must take possession of the debt jointly because the principal trusted both, and joint action is possible; payment to one alone does not discharge the debt.

Wakil for Possession: Does It Imply Litigation Authority?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agent's litigation authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on whether a wakil for possession of a debt is also a wakil for litigation, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Consent to possession does not imply consent to litigation.

This passage examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: when a principal appoints an agent solely to take possession of a debt, does that appointment automatically include authority to litigate? Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the underlying purpose (tamlīk) necessitates litigation authority, drawing analogies from other agency contexts. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) counter that possession and litigation are distinct competences, and consent to one does not imply consent to the other. Understanding this dispute clarifies the importance of explicit authorization in agency appointments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the legal question? Determine whether the wakil for possession is also a wakil for litigation (khasm).
The issue centers on the scope of the agent's implied authority.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the wakil is also a wakil for litigation. His evidence: the principal appointed him for tamlīk (ownership), which includes the right to sue if needed. He uses qiyas to the wakil for shuf'a, who becomes a litigant before possession.
The analogy is based on the similarity that both involve securing a property right.
3
State Sahibayn's position and their proof
Sahibayn hold that the wakil for possession is not a wakil for litigation. Their proof: possession and litigation require different skills; trust in one does not imply competence in the other. The principal's consent to possession does not extend to litigation.
They also cite a narration from Hasan b. Ziyad from Abu Hanifa that supports their view.
4
Analyze the analogy with shuf'a
Examine the qiyas: Why does Abu Hanifa analogize the wakil for possession to the wakil for shuf'a? In shuf'a, the wakil must be a litigant to enforce the right before taking possession. Abu Hanifa argues that the wakil for possession similarly has a right to the debt that may require litigation.
The Sahibayn might not accept this analogy because the right in shuf'a is conditional on litigation, whereas debt possession is typically a pure receipt.
5
Identify the practical consequence
What is the thamarah al-khilaf? If Abu Hanifa's view is followed, the debtor can sue the wakil directly; if Sahibayn's view is followed, the debtor must sue the principal.
This affects procedural strategy and the principal's exposure to litigation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام ابوحنیفہ کے نقطہ نظر میں قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل خصومت کا بھی وکیل ہے
قال والوكيل بقبض الدين يكون وكيلا بالخصومة عند ابي حنيفة لو أقيمت عليه البيئة على استيفل المؤكل او ابرائه تقبل عنده وقالا لا يكون خصماً وهو رواية الحسن عن ابي حنيفةً لان القبض غير الخصومة وليس كل من يؤتمن على المال يهتدى فى الخصومات فلم يكن الرضاء بالقبض رضابها ولا بى حنيفة انه وكله بالتملك لان الديون تقضى بأمثالها اذ قبض الدين نفسه لا يتصور الا انه جعل استيفاء لعين حقه من وجه فاشبه الوكيل بأخذ الشفعة والرجوع فى الهبة والوكيل بالشراء والقسمة والرد بالعيب وهذه اشبه باخذ الشفعة حتى يكون خصماً قبل القبض كما يكون خصماً قبل الاخذهنا لك والوكيل بالشراء لا يكون خصماً قبل مباشرة بالشراء هذا لان المبادلة تقتضى حقوقا وهو اصيل فيها فيكون خصمافيها
ترجمہ اور قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک خصومت کا وکیل بھی گاھتی کہ اگر وکیل پر بینہ کیا گیا کہ متوکل قرضہ وصول کر چکا ہے یا موکل نے قرضدار کو بری کر دیا ہے تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ بینہ قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ وکیل مدی عالیہ نہیں ہوگا یہی ایک روایت امام ابوحنیفہ سے حسن کی ہے اس لئے کہ قبضہ، خصومت کا غیر ہے اور یہ بات ضروری نہیں کہ جو شخص مال سلسلہ میں قابل اطمینان ہو وہ مقدمات کی پیروی بھی کر سکے لہذا موکل کا وکیل کے قبضہ پر راضی ہونا ، اس کی خصومت راضی ہونا نہیں ہوگا اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ موکل نے اس کو مالک بننے کا وکیل کیا ہے اس لئے کہ دیون با مثالہا ادا کئے جاتے ہیں کیونکہ عین دین پر قبضہ کرنا متصور نہیں ہے مگر اس کو من وجہ عین حق کا وصول کرنا قرار دیا گیا ہے پس قبضہ کا وکیل اس وکیل کے مشابہ ہو گیا جو شفعہ لینے واپس لینے خریدنے کے واسطے، ہوارہ کے واسطے اور عیب کی وجہ سے واپس کرنے کے واسطے وکیل کیا گیا ہو اور وکالت بالقبض ، شفعہ لینے ، کی وکالت سے زیادہ مشابہ ہے حتی کہ وکیل بالقبض قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے قرضدار کے مقابلہ میں خصم ہو گا جیسا کہ وکیل شفعہ ، شفعہ لینے سے پہلے ہی خصم ہو جاتا ہے اور وکیل بالشراء خریداری کرنے سے پہلے خصم نہیں ہوتا ہے یہ اس لئے کہ مبادلہ حقوق کو چاہتا ہے اور وکیل مبادلہ کے حقوق میں اصیل ہوتا ہے لہذا وہ ان حقوق کے بارے میں خصم ہو گا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا جوشخص وکیل ہوگا۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک وہ شخص خصومت کا وکیل بھی ہو گاتی کہ اگر قرض دار نے اس وکیل کا بالقبض کے خلاف اس بات پر مبینہ قائم کر دیا کہ متوکل قرضہ وصول کر چکا ہے یا متوکل نے قرضدار کو قرضہ سے بری کر دیا ہے تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک یہ بعینہ قبول کر لیا جائے گا۔
اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل خصومت کا وکیل نہیں ہوتا اور جب وکیل بالقبض خصومت کا وکیل نہیں ہوتا تو یہ وکیل قرضدار کا خصم اور مدعی علیہ بھی نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب یہ وکیل خصم اور مدعی علیہ نہیں ہو گا تو اس کے خلاف قرضدار کی طرف سے پیش کر
In the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, the wakil for taking possession of the debt is also a wakil for litigation. He said: The wakil for taking possession of a debt is a wakil for litigation according to Abu Hanifa. If evidence is brought against him that the principal has taken possession or has discharged [the debtor], it is accepted according to him (Abu Hanifa). But the two (Sahibayn) said: He is not a litigant (khasm), and this is a narration from Hasan from Abu Hanifa. Because possession is not litigation, and not everyone who is trusted with money is skilled in litigation; thus, being satisfied with possession is not being satisfied with litigation. And the proof of Abu Hanifa is that he appointed him for ownership (tamlik) because debts are paid with their like, as taking possession of the very debt is not conceivable except that it is considered a kind of collection of the very right. So the wakil for possession resembles the wakil for taking pre-emption (shuf'a), returning a gift, wakil for purchase, division, and return due to defect. And this (wakil for possession) is more similar to taking pre-emption, so that he becomes a litigant before taking possession, just as the wakil for pre-emption becomes a litigant before taking it. And the wakil for purchase does not become a litigant before directly purchasing. This is because exchange entails rights, and he is an agent (asil) in them, so he becomes a litigant in them.
Translation: The wakil for taking possession of the debt, in the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, is also a wakil for litigation. If evidence is brought against the wakil that the principal has collected the debt or has discharged the debtor, this evidence is accepted according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said: The wakil is not a litigant (khasm), and this is one narration from Imam Abu Hanifa from Hasan. Because possession is other than litigation, and it is not necessary that a person who is trustworthy in matters of money can also pursue litigation. Therefore, the principal's consent to the wakil's possession does not imply consent to his litigation. Abu Hanifa's proof is that the principal appointed him for ownership, because debts are paid with their like; since taking possession of the very debt is not conceivable, it is considered, from one aspect, as collection of the very right. Thus, the wakil for possession resembles the wakil for taking pre-emption, returning a gift, wakil for purchase, division, and return due to defect. And agency for possession is more similar to agency for taking pre-emption, so that the wakil for possession becomes a litigant against the debtor before taking possession, just as the wakil for pre-emption becomes a litigant before taking the property. And the wakil for purchase does not become a litigant before purchasing. This is because exchange entails rights, and the wakil is an agent (asil) in them, so he becomes a litigant concerning those rights. Explanation: The issue is that the person who is appointed wakil for taking possession of the debt, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, is also a wakil for litigation. If the debtor brings evidence against this wakil for possession that the principal has already collected the debt or discharged the debtor, Imam Abu Hanifa accepts that evidence. And the Sahibayn said: The wakil for taking possession is not a wakil for litigation, and when the wakil for possession is not a wakil for litigation, then this wakil is not a litigant (khasm) or defendant (mudda'a 'alayh) against the debtor. And when he is not a litigant or defendant, then the debtor's presenting [evidence] against him...
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a person appointed specifically to take possession of a debt (وكيل بقبض الدين) is also by that appointment authorized to engage in litigation (خصومة) concerning that debt. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that he is, because the essence of taking possession implies ownership rights, and these rights may require litigation. He draws an analogy with other types of agency (shuf'a, return of gift, etc.) where the agent becomes a litigant. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, arguing that possession and litigation are distinct skills; trust in one does not imply competence in the other. A separate narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad attributes the same view to Abu Hanifa. The passage begins with the Arabic text from the Hidayah, then provides Urdu translation and explanation. The text cuts off mid-sentence but the core dispute is complete.

Key Terms
وكيل بقبض الدين (wakīl bi-qabḍ al-dayn): An agent appointed specifically to take physical or constructive possession of a debt (i.e., to receive the payment).
خصم (khaṣm): A litigant; a party in a lawsuit who can be sued or can sue.
شفعة (shufʿah): Pre-emption; the right of a co-owner to purchase the share of a selling partner before it is sold to a third party.
تمليك (tamlīk): Making someone owner; transferring ownership. Abu Hanifa argues that possession agent is appointed for tamlīk.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the implication of a wakil for possession not being a wakil for litigation?
A) The wakil can still be sued by the debtor.
B) The wakil is not a litigant (khasm) and cannot be sued for the debt.
C) The wakil can delegate litigation to another person.
D) The wakil automatically becomes a wakil for litigation after taking possession.

Key Takeaway
The scope of an agent's authority is determined by the principal's consent; possession authority does not automatically include litigation authority in the view of the Sahibayn.

Agent for Debt Collection: Is He Also an Agent for Litigation?
Dispute on whether agent collecting debt is also litigation agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that an agent for debt collection is also an agent for litigation, and evaluate the counter-argument of the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Debt collection is an exchange (mubadala), making the agent a principal who must be able to litigate.

When a creditor appoints an agent to collect a debt, a natural question arises: can that agent also represent the creditor in court if the debtor disputes the debt? The Hanafi school, led by Imam Abu Hanifa, answers yes, while his two main disciples (Sahibayn) disagree. This lesson walks through the reasoning on both sides and traces the practical consequences of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Clearly state the legal question: Is an agent appointed to take possession of a debt (wakil bi qabd al-dayn) also an agent for litigation (wakil bil khusuma)? This is a dispute within the Hanafi school.
2
State the Sahibayn's Position and Their Proofs
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani argue that taking possession of a debt and litigation are fundamentally different. Trustworthiness does not imply litigation skill, and consent to possession does not imply consent to litigation.
Their two proofs: (1) difference in nature, (2) trust does not equal litigation ability.
3
State Imam Abu Hanifa's Position and His Proof
Abu Hanifa argues that debts are paid by their like (mithl), not the specific item. Therefore, taking possession of a debt is an exchange (mubadala) where the agent becomes owner of the like. This makes the agent a principal in the rights of exchange, which necessarily includes the right to litigate.
The exchange element is key: mubadala entails rights of delivery and receipt.
4
Trace the Analogies (Qiyas) Used by Abu Hanifa
The passage cites several analogies: the agent for pre-emption (shuf'a), the agent for revoking a gift, and the agent for purchase. In each case, the agent becomes a litigant because the agency involves exchange. Note the author of Hidayah's preference for the pre-emption analogy as more similar.
These analogies reinforce the principle that agency involving exchange makes the agent a principal in litigation.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
If the debtor presents evidence (e.g., that the principal already received payment), under Abu Hanifa, that evidence is accepted because the agent is a litigant. Under the Sahibayn, the evidence would not be accepted; the principal must be present.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, as the author indicates.

كتاب الوكالة
اشرف الہدایہ جلد دہم حتی کہ اگر بائع نے بعینہ قائم کیا کہ وکیل بالشراء نے شمن ادا نہیں کیا تو یہ بینہ قبول ہوگا۔ اور جیسے مشترک چیز میں ہوارہ کیلئے کسی نے کسی کو وکیل بنا کر بھیجا پس شریک نے بعینہ قائم کیا کہ اسکے موکل نے اپنا حصہ وصول کر لیا ہے تو یہ بینہ قبول ہوگا اور جیسے مشتری نے عیب کی وجہ سے بیچ واپس کرنے کا وکیل کیا اور بائع نے بینہ قائم کیا کہ اس کا موکل اس عیب پر راضی ہو چکا ہے تو یہ بینہ قبول ہوگا یہی حال قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کے وکیل کا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ وکیل بقبض الدین وکیل باخذ الشفعہ سے زیادہ مشابہ ہے بہ نسبت وکیل بالشراء کے ۔ کیونکہ قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل قبضہ سے پہلے ہی قرضدار کے مقابلہ میں خصم قرار دیا جاتا ہے۔ اور ر باوکیل بالشراء تو وہ خریداری کرنے سے پہلے بائع کے مقابلہ میں خصم نہیں ہوتا بلکہ شراء اور خریداری کے بعد خصم ہو گا۔
هذا لان المبادلة تقتضى ..... الخ سے امام ابو حنیفہ کی طرف سے اصل مسئلہ پر ایک نکتہ : ۔ کیا گیا ہے نکتہ یہ ہے کہ موکل نے جب کسی کو مالک بناتے ہوئے قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل کیا اور قرضہ میں وکیل کو اصل قرضہ کی مثل پر مالک ہونے کا حق حاصل ہوتا ہے تو قرضہ کی مثل کا وصول کرنا مبادلہ ہوا اور مبادلہ کچھ حقوق کا تقاضہ کرتا ہے یعنی تسلیم اور تسلم کا۔
اور مبادلہ کا وکیل حقوق مبادلہ میں اصیل ہوتا ہے یعنی حقوق مبادلہ اسی کی طرف راجع ہوتے ہیں اور جب مبادلہ کا وکیل حقوق مبادلہ میں اصیل ہے تو وہ وکیل ان حقوق کے بارے میں خصم بھی ہوگا پس ثابت ہو گیا قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل ، قرضدار کا خصم بھی ہو گا یعنی وہ خصومت کا وکیل بھی ہوگا۔
The evidence will also not be accepted. From Imam Abu Hanifa, a narration by Hasan ibn Ziyad is also the same, and Imam Shafi'i's most correct opinion is also this, and according to Zahir al-Riwayah, Imam Ahmad also holds this. The proof of the two companions (Sahibayn) is that between taking possession of debt and litigation there is a difference. And when there is a difference between them, then the agent for possession is not an agent for litigation. A second proof is that a person whose honesty and trustworthiness is reliable, it is not necessary that he can pursue a lawsuit, i.e., many people are satisfactory in trustworthiness and honesty but are completely inept in litigation. So in such a case, if the principal agreed to the agent taking possession of the debt, then from that it does not necessitate that he agreed to the agent's litigation and pursuing the case. And when that is the case, then the agent for possession is not an agent for litigation. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the principal appointed the agent as an agent for the matter that the agent will take possession of something in exchange for the debt that is in the debtor's liability, and will become the owner of that possessed item. And this is said because debts are paid by their like (mithl) and not by their specific identity ('ayn), because the debt is an attribute established in the liability of the debtor, and taking possession of an attribute is impossible. Therefore, taking possession of the specific debt is also impossible. An example: Khalid loaned Shahid one hundred rupees. Then Shahid the debtor spent that money. So now the specific money cannot be recovered. And when this money cannot be recovered, then inevitably the debtor will pay its like. And when the debtor pays the like of the debt, then it is known that the agent will obtain ownership of the like instead of the original debt. So it is as if the principal appointed him as an agent to obtain ownership. But there could be an objection: when the specific debt cannot be recovered, how can it be correct to say that the creditor has recovered his debt, even though it is said? The answer is that the thing given as the like of the debt, due to being a like, is equal and equivalent to the actual right. And when the received thing is equal to the actual right, then it is considered, from one aspect, as receiving the actual right. And when it is considered as receiving the actual right, then it is correct to say that the creditor has recovered his debt. And when it is established that the agent for taking possession of debt has the right to own the like of the original debt, then that agent also has the right to litigation. He will be a litigant and defendant against the debtor. And when the agent for possession is a litigant and defendant against the debtor, then the evidence presented by the debtor will also be accepted. Just as the agent for taking pre-emption (shuf'a) can be a litigant against the buyer. So if the buyer presents evidence to the agent for taking pre-emption that the principal has surrendered the pre-emption right to the buyer, i.e., the principal has relinquished the right of pre-emption in favor of the buyer, then this evidence will be accepted. Similarly, the agent for possession can be an agent for litigation. And just as an agent for taking back a gift can be an agent for litigation. For example, the principal made a gift to someone, then sent an agent to take back the gift from the donee. Then the donee established evidence against the agent that the donor had taken compensation from him for the gifted item. Then this evidence of the donee will be accepted. And just as an agent for purchase (wakil bil-shira) is a litigant. Thus, the rights of the contract are demanded from him, not from the principal. So much so that if the seller establishes [evidence] specifically that the agent for purchase did not pay the price, then this evidence will be accepted. And just as, for division of a joint property, someone appointed an agent, then the partner established evidence specifically that his principal had received his share. Then this evidence will be accepted. And just as a buyer appointed an agent to return the sale due to a defect, and the seller established evidence that his principal had consented to that defect, then this evidence will be accepted. The same is the case of the agent for taking possession of debt. The author of Hidayah said that the agent for taking possession of debt is more similar to the agent for taking pre-emption than to the agent for purchase. Because the agent for taking possession of debt is considered a litigant against the debtor even before taking possession. As for the agent for purchase, he is not a litigant against the seller before making the purchase; rather, he becomes a litigant after purchase and buying. This is because exchange (mubadala) necessitates... from Imam Abu Hanifa's side, a point has been made on the original issue. The point is that when the principal appointed someone as an agent to take possession of debt while making him an owner, and in debt, the agent has the right to own the like of the original debt, then receiving the like of the debt is an exchange (mubadala). And exchange entails certain rights, i.e., delivery and taking delivery. And the agent of exchange is a principal in the rights of exchange, i.e., the rights of exchange refer back to him. And when the agent of exchange is a principal in the rights of exchange, then that agent will also be a litigant regarding those rights. Thus, it is established that the agent for taking possession of debt is also a litigant against the debtor, i.e., he is also an agent for litigation.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether an agent appointed to collect a debt (wakil bi qabd al-dayn) is also an agent for litigation (wakil bil khusuma). The passage opens by stating the agreed position from multiple Imams: from Imam Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad, Imam Shafi'i's later view, and Imam Ahmad according to Zahir al-Riwayah all hold that such an agent is indeed an agent for litigation. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, presenting two proofs: (1) There is a fundamental difference between taking possession of a debt and litigation, so one does not imply the other. (2) Trustworthiness in holding property does not imply ability to litigate; many honest people are poor litigators, so consent to possession does not imply consent to litigation. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is based on the nature of debt repayment. Since debts are paid by their like (mithl) and not by the specific item (ayn), taking possession of debt is essentially an exchange (mubadala) where the agent becomes owner of the like. This exchange gives him the rights of a principal, including the right to litigate. The passage then provides analogies: the agent for pre-emption (shuf'a), the agent for revoking a gift, and the agent for purchase all become litigants in their respective capacities. The author of Hidayah (al-Marghinani) strengthens the analogy with the pre-emption agent, noting that both become litigants before the actual transfer, unlike the purchase agent who only becomes a litigant after purchase. The passage concludes with a summary: because taking possession of debt is an exchange, the agent is a principal in that exchange and thus a litigant. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Imam Abu Hanifa, supported by the majority of later scholars.

Key Terms
وکیل بقبض الدین (wakil bi qabd al-dayn): An agent appointed to take possession of a debt from the debtor.
وکیل بالخصومت (wakil bil khusuma): An agent appointed to represent the principal in litigation or legal proceedings.
مبادلہ (mubadala): An exchange transaction involving delivery and receipt of countervalues.
خصم (khasm): A litigant or adversary in a legal dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa hold that an agent for debt collection is also an agent for litigation?
A) Because trustworthiness implies litigation capability.
B) Because taking possession of debt is an exchange (mubadala), making the agent a principal in the rights of exchange.
C) Because the agent personally owns the debt.
D) Because the Sahibayn agree.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an agent for debt collection is also an agent for litigation because debt collection is an exchange (mubadala) that makes the agent a principal in the rights of exchange.

Agent for Specific Property: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Ruling and istihsan reasoning for agent of specific property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that an agent for a specific item is not a litigation agent, and distinguish the qiyas argument from the istihsan exception.

Core Idea
An agent for taking possession of a specific item is a mere trustee, not a litigant.

Imagine you appoint someone to take physical possession of a specific slave you own. A third party claims the slave was sold to him and presents evidence. Can your agent litigate to keep the slave? The Hanafi school rules that he cannot, because he is only a trustee (amin) for taking possession. However, through istihsan (juristic preference), the handover of the slave is suspended until you return. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this ruling and the interplay between qiyas and istihsan.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling and Its Basis
Read the opening ruling: 'The agent for taking possession of a specific thing is not an agent for litigation.' Identify the reason given: the agent is a mere trustee (amin mahd) and taking possession is not an exchange (mubadala).
The agent resembles a messenger (rasul) who merely delivers, not a principal in exchange.
2
Analyze the Qiyas Argument
Qiyas would dictate that the slave be handed to the agent because the evidence presented by the third party is not against a litigant (the agent is not a litigant), so the evidence is disregarded. Understand the asl (original case) and the far' (new case).
The illa is that the agent is not a khasm.
3
Understand the Istihsan Rule
Istihsan overrides qiyas: the agent is considered a litigant regarding the restriction of his own possession. Because he stands in place of the principal for taking possession, his right to take possession is suspended if the third party's evidence suggests the principal sold the slave.
The result is that the matter is suspended (wuqif) until the absent principal appears.
4
Apply the Distinction to a Modern Scenario
Consider a bailee appointed to receive a specific car. A third party claims to have bought it from the owner. Can the bailee contest? No, but the car should not be delivered until the owner clarifies.
This illustrates the practical consequence of the ruling.

Source Text

عین پر قبضہ کا وکیل خصومت کا وکیل نہیں
قال والوكيل بقبض العين لا يكون وكيلا بالخصومة لانه امين محض والقبض ليس بمبادلة فاشبه الرسول حتى ان من وكل وكيلا بقبض عبدله فاقام الذي هو في يديه البينة على ان المؤكل باعه اياه وقف الأمر حتى يحضر الغائب فى هذا استحسان والقياس ان يدفع الى الوكيل لان البيئة قامت لا على خصم فلم تعتبر وجه الاستحسان انه خصم في قصر يده لقيام المؤكل فى القبض فيقتصر يده وان لم يثبت البيع حتى لو حضر الغائب تعاد البينة على البيع فصار كما اذا اقام البينة على ان المؤكل عزله عن ذالك فانها تقبل في قصر يده
گذارهنا
ترجمہ اور عین شی پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل خصومت کا وکیل نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ محض امین ہے اور قبضہ مبادلہ نہیں ہے پس وہ قاصد کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ حتی کہ اگر کسی نے کسی کو اپنا غلام وصول کرنے کا وکیل کیا پس وہ شخص جس کے قبضہ میں غلام ہے ۔ اس نے اس بات پر بینہ قائم کیا کہ مؤکل نے وہ غلام اس کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا ہے تو یہ معاملہ موقوف رہے گا یہاں تک کہ غائب حاضر ہو جائے اس میں استحسان ہے اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ غلام وکیل کو دیا جائے کیونکہ گواہی قائم ہوئی لیکن خصم پر نہیں لہذا یہ گواہی معتبر نہ ہوگی وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ دوکیل اپنا قبضہ کوتاہ ہونے میں خصم ہے اس لئے کہ قبضہ کرنے میں وہ موکل کا قائم مقام ہے ۔ پس اس کا قبضہ کوتاہ کیا جائے گا اگر بیچ ثابت نہ ہو۔
The agent for taking possession of a specific thing is not an agent for litigation, because he is a mere trustee, and taking possession is not an exchange, so he resembles a messenger. Hence, if someone appointed an agent to take possession of his slave, and the person in whose possession the slave is established evidence that the principal sold the slave to him, then the matter will be suspended until the absent one appears. In this, istihsan (juristic preference) is applied, and by qiyas (analogy), the slave should be handed over to the agent because the evidence was established but not against a litigant, so it is not considered. The reason for istihsan is that he (the agent) is a litigant regarding the restriction of his possession because he stands in place of the principal in taking possession. So his possession will be restricted, even if the sale is not proven. So much so that if the absent one returns, the evidence regarding the sale will be re-established. It becomes as if he had established evidence that the principal had dismissed him from that, then it will be accepted in restricting his possession.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (istihsan vs qiyas) regarding an agent appointed to take possession of a specific tangible item (wakil bi qabd al-ayn). It begins with the ruling: such an agent is not an agent for litigation. The reason is that the agent is a mere amin (trustee) and taking possession of a specific item is not an exchange (mubadala); it resembles a messenger (rasul) who simply delivers possession. An example: If someone appoints an agent to take possession of a slave, and the person holding the slave presents evidence that the principal sold the slave to him, the matter is suspended until the absent principal comes. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas (analogy) would require handing the slave to the agent because the evidence was not presented against a litigant (since the agent is not a litigant) and thus should be disregarded. However, istihsan prevails: the agent is considered a litigant in the limited sense of restricting his own possession, because he stands in place of the principal for the purpose of taking possession. Therefore, his right to take possession is restricted until the principal appears. If the principal later appears, the evidence regarding the sale is re-presented. This is analogous to a case where the holder proves that the principal dismissed the agent - such evidence is accepted to restrict the agent's possession. The key distinction from the debt collection agent is that taking possession of a specific item is not an exchange, so the agent does not become a principal in exchange rights and thus is not a full litigation agent.

Key Terms
وکیل بقبض العین (wakil bi qabd al-'ayn): An agent appointed to take physical possession of a specific, identifiable item (e.g., a slave).
امین محض (amin mahd): A pure trustee, someone entrusted with property but without authority to litigate or dispose.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a more equitable outcome. In this case, avoiding handing the slave to the agent when there is evidence of sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the agent for taking possession of a specific item (like a slave) not considered an agent for litigation?
A) Because specific items are always exchanged in a sale.
B) Because he is a mere trustee (amin) and taking possession is not an exchange (mubadala).
C) Because the Sahibayn said so.
D) Because the agent cannot be a litigant in any case.

Key Takeaway
An agent for specific property is not a litigation agent, but istihsan may suspend the handover if a third party claims ownership, until the principal appears.

Agent for Debt Collection as a Litigant
Explaining that the agent for collecting debt is a litigant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that an agent for debt collection is a litigant and explain the qiyas reasoning that supports this view.

Core Idea
An agent for taking possession of a debt is a litigant because debt collection is an exchange, making the agent principal in exchange rights.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that an agent appointed to collect a debt (wakeel bi qabd al-dayn) is considered a litigant (khasm) against the debtor. The ruling is derived through qiyas khafi, comparing the debt agent to the agent for pre-emption (shuf'ah) rather than the agent for purchase. Understanding this distinction clarifies when an agent can represent his principal in court without separate authorization.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State that the agent for debt collection is a litigant (khasm) against the debtor.
2
Review supporting analogies
The passage mentions three analogies: seller's evidence on non-payment, co-owner's evidence on receipt, and seller's evidence on defect consent.
These analogies show that evidence from the opposing party's agent is accepted, establishing a pattern.
3
Understand the key comparison
The author of Hidayah compares the debt agent to the pre-emption agent, not the purchase agent.
Pre-emption agent is a litigant before taking possession; purchase agent only becomes a litigant after purchase.
4
Follow the qiyas reasoning
Debt collection is an exchange (mubaadalah) requiring delivery and receipt. The agent becomes the principal in these exchange rights.
This is qiyas khafi: the effective cause (illa) is that both involve exchange where the agent holds the right to equivalent property.
5
Derive the consequence
Since the agent is principal in exchange rights, he is a litigant regarding those rights.
Thus, the agent can sue and be sued without separate litigation authorization.

اشرف الہدایہ جلد دہم حتی کہ اگر بائع نے بعینہ قائم کیا کہ وکیل بالشراء نے شمن ادا نہیں کیا تو یہ بینہ قبول ہوگا۔ اور جیسے مشترک چیز میں ہوارہ کیلئے کسی نے کسی کو وکیل بنا کر بھیجا پس شریک نے بعینہ قائم کیا کہ اسکے موکل نے اپنا حصہ وصول کر لیا ہے تو یہ بینہ قبول ہوگا اور جیسے مشتری نے عیب کی وجہ سے بیچ واپس کرنے کا وکیل کیا اور بائع نے بینہ قائم کیا کہ اس کا موکل اس عیب پر راضی ہو چکا ہے تو یہ بینہ قبول ہوگا یہی حال قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کے وکیل کا ہے۔
