Even if he gave him the loaned property, in this case too the debtor will have the right to take back the loaned property from the agent, provided that the creditor has demanded the debt from the debtor. The proof is the same as what has passed before: that the debtor had given it in hope of permission. But with the creditor's demand, this hope is cut off, so the debtor will have the right to return from the agent. The author of al-Hidayah says: In the case of denial, the permissibility of the debtor returning from the agent is more apparent compared to the first two cases which permit return, i.e., the debtor confirmed the agent and made him a guarantor, or the debtor remained silent. So when in both these cases the debtor has the right to return from the agent, then in the case of denial, he will have the right to return even more. The author of al-Hidayah says: In all four mentioned scenarios (confirmation without guarantee, silence, confirmation with guarantee, and denial), when the debtor has given the property to the agent, then before the absent (creditor) appears, the debtor will not have the right to take back the said property from the agent. Because the property that the debtor gave to the agent has become the right of the absent. If the debtor confirmed the agent in the claim, then it is absolutely clear that the property has become the right of the absent. And if the debtor remained silent or denied the agent, then in both these cases there is a possibility that the absent has become entitled to this property. In any case, when this property has become the right of the absent, then before the absent (creditor) appears, the debtor will not have the right to take it back from the agent. And this becomes like the debtor having given property to a fudhuli (unauthorized person) in hope that perhaps the creditor would permit. So due to the possibility of permission, the debtor does not have the right to take back that property. Similarly here, he will not have the right to take back the property. The second proof is: If someone did an act for some purpose, he does not have the right to break that disposition as long as he is not hopeless of his purpose. So the act the debtor did by giving the loan amount to the agent has the purpose that the debtor's liability be discharged and the creditor has no right to demand. So as long as he is not hopeless of this purpose being fulfilled, he will not have the right to take the loan back.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with two rulings concerning a debtor who has given the loaned amount to a wakil (agent) of the creditor. First: If the creditor has demanded the debt from the debtor, the debtor may reclaim the money from the wakil because the hope of the creditor's permission is cut off. Second: In four scenarios (confirmation without guarantee, silence, confirmation with guarantee, and denial), if the debtor gave the property to the wakil before the creditor appears, he cannot reclaim it because the property has effectively become the creditor's right. The text provides two proofs: the analogy of giving property to a fudhuli (unauthorized agent) in hope of ratification, and the principle that one cannot undo an act intended to discharge a liability until hopeless of that purpose.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakil): Agent appointed by one party (creditor) to receive the debt
قرض (qard): Loan of fungible property (money) that is repaid in kind
تصدیق (tasdiq): Confirmation/admission by the debtor that the agent is truly the creditor's agent
تکذیب (takdhīb): Denial by the debtor that the agent is the creditor's agent
فضولی (fudhūlī): An unauthorized person who acts on behalf of another without appointment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which situation does the debtor have the right to reclaim the loan amount from the wakil?
A) When the debtor confirmed the wakil and made him a guarantor.
B) When the debtor remained silent about the wakil's authority.
C) When the creditor has demanded the debt from the debtor.
D) When the creditor has not yet appeared.

Key Takeaway
The debtor's right to reclaim from the agent is extinguished once the money is given, unless the creditor has demanded the debt, and even then, once the creditor appears, the money becomes his and cannot be reclaimed.

Depositary's Duty When Claims of Agency, Inheritance, or Purchase Arise
Rulings on depositary's duty when claims arise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of the three scenarios (agency, inheritance, purchase) and explain why the ruling differs based on acknowledgment of another's property.

Core Idea
Delivery of deposit is only ordered when the acknowledgment does not implicate another's property rights.

Claims on a deposit can arise from agency, inheritance, or purchase. The Hanafi school provides a clear criterion: if confirming the claim would amount to acknowledging a right over another's property, the depositary is not ordered to deliver. If the acknowledgment is against oneself or the property's ownership has terminated, delivery is ordered. This lesson examines the reasoning behind each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three claims: (1) someone claims to be an agent of the owner to take the deposit, (2) someone claims the owner died and he is the sole heir, (3) someone claims he bought the deposit from the owner. Note the ruling for each.
2
Extract the 'illa (effective cause) for each
For each scenario, determine the reason ('illa) given in the text. The recurring phrase is 'acknowledgment of another's property' (iqrar bi mal al-ghayr). In the agency and purchase cases, the depositary's confirmation acknowledges a right over the owner's property, which is invalid. In the inheritance case, ownership ended with the owner's death.
Contrast with the debt case: in debt, the acknowledgment is against the debtor himself, not another.
3
Compare inheritance with agency and purchase
Why is inheritance different? Because the owner died, so the property no longer belongs to him. Both the depositary and claimant agree it belongs to the heir. Thus, acknowledging the heir's right is not acknowledging another's property since no other owner exists.
4
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Consider a case where the claimant says he is the owner (not agent/heir/purchaser). Would delivery be ordered? The text does not cover this, but the principle suggests: if the depositary confirms, it is an acknowledgment of ownership, but since the depositary is not the owner, his confirmation is not binding. The ruling would be similar to agency.
This step reinforces the concept that the depositary's confirmation alone is insufficient when it involves another's right.
5
Summarize the rule
A depositary is ordered to deliver only when his confirmation does not constitute an acknowledgment of another's property. This occurs only when the property's owner is dead (inheritance) or when the acknowledgment is against himself (debt).

Source Text

عبداللہ نے اپنا مال عبد الرحمن کے پاس ودیعت کے طور پر رکھا پھر ایک تیسرے شخص مثلاً شاہد نے مودع ( بفتح الدال ) پر دعوی کیا کہ میں مودع ( بكسر الدال) کی طرف سے اس مال ودیعت پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل ہوں اور مودَع (بفتح الدال ) نے اس کی تصدیق بھی کر دی تو مورع کو یہ حکم نہیں دیا جائے گا کہ وہ مدعی کو مال ودیعت سپر دکر دے۔ کیونکہ مودَع (الفتح الدال ) کے پاس جو مال ودیعت ہے وہ مودع ( بكسر الدال) کی ملک ہے اور مودع (بفتح الدال ) اس کا معترف بھی ہے پس مودع ( فتح الدال ) کا مدعی وکالت کی تصدیق کرنا در حقیقت غیر یعنی مودع ) بكسر الدال ) کے مال پر مدعی وکالت کے لئے قبضہ کے حق کا اقرار کرنا ہے اور غیر کے مال پر قبضہ کے حق کا اقرار کرنا درست نہ ہوگا اور جب یہ اقرار درست نہیں ہے تو مودع (بفتح الدال) کو یہ حکم بھی نہیں دیا جائے گا کہ وہ مال ودیعت مدعی وکالت کے حوالہ کر دے تو قرضدار کو حکم دیا جائے گا کہ مال قرض مدعی وکالت کو دیدے کیونکہ دیون اور قرضے با مثالها ادا کئے جاتے ہیں نہ کہ با عیا تھا ۔ لہذا قرضدار کا مدعی وکالت کیلئے قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کے حق کا اقرار کرنا ہوگا نہ کہ غیر یعنی قرض خواہ پر۔ پس جب قرضدار کا اقرار خود اس کی ذات پر ہے تو یہ اقرار درست ہوگا اور جب اس صورت میں اقرار درست ہے تو قرضدار کو یہ حکم دینا بھی درست ہوگا کہ وہ قرضہ کا مال مدعی وکالت کے سپر د کر دے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دعوی کیا کہ میرا باپ مر گیا ہے اور ودیعت کا مال جو فلاں مودع ( بفتح الدال ) کے پاس ہے اس کو میرے باپ نے میرے لئے میراث چھوڑا ہے اور حال یہ کہ میت کا اس مدعی کے علاوہ دوسرا کوئی وارث نہیں ہے اور مودع (بفتح الدال) نے مدعی میراث کے قول کی تصدیق بھی کر دی تو مودع (بفتح الدال ) کو حکم دیا جائے گا کہ وہ مال ودیعت اس مدعی کو دیدے کیونکہ مودع ( بكسر الدال ) کی وفات کے بعد مال ودیعت اس کا مال نہ رہا یعنی مرتے ہی اسکی ملک ختم ہو گئی۔
And whoever said, 'I am an agent for taking possession of the deposit,' and the depositary (mūda') confirms him, the depositary is not ordered to hand over to him because it is an acknowledgment of another's property, unlike the case of debt. And whoever claimed that his father died and left the deposit as inheritance for him, and he has no other heir, and the depositary confirms him, he is ordered to pay to him because after his death the property is no longer his; they have agreed that it is the property of the heir. And if he claimed that he bought the deposit from its owner, and the depositary confirmed him, he is not ordered to pay to him because as long as the owner is alive, it is an acknowledgment of ownership of another, because he is capable of ownership, so they are not believed in the claim of sale against him. Translation: If someone said, 'I am an agent for taking possession of the deposit,' and the depositary confirmed him, the depositary will not be ordered to hand over the deposit to him because this is an acknowledgment of another's property, unlike the case of debt. And if someone claimed that his father died and left the deposit as inheritance for him, and he has no other heir, and the depositary confirmed him, then the depositary will be ordered to hand it over to him because after the death of the depositor (owner), it is no longer his property. And both the depositary and the claimant agreed that it is the property of the heir. And if he claimed that he bought the deposit from its owner, and the depositary confirmed him, then the depositary will not be ordered to hand it over to him because as long as the owner is alive, this is an acknowledgment of ownership of another, because the owner is capable of ownership. So the depositary and the claimant are not believed in the claim of sale against him. Explanation: Mūda' (with fatha on the dal) is the person with whom the deposit is kept, i.e., the trustee (amin). Mūdi' (with kasra on the dal) is the one who deposits the property, i.e., the owner. The scenario is: A person, e.g., Abdullah, placed his property as a deposit with Abdur-Rahman. Then a third person, e.g., Shahid, claimed to the depositary (mūda') that he is an agent on behalf of the depositor (mūdi') to take possession of this deposit. And the depositary confirmed him. Then the depositary will not be ordered to hand over the deposit to the claimant because the deposit held by the depositary is the property of the depositor (mūdi'), and the depositary admits this. So the depositary's confirmation of the claimant's agency is in effect an acknowledgment of the claimant's right to possession over the property of another (the depositor). And acknowledging a right of possession over another's property is not valid. And when this acknowledgment is not valid, the depositary will not be ordered to hand over the deposit to the claimant. However, the debtor will be ordered to give the loan property to the claimant agent because debts and loans are paid by equivalents, not by specific items. Therefore, the debtor's acknowledgment of the claimant's right to possess the debt is an acknowledgment against himself, not against the creditor. So when the acknowledgment is against himself, it is valid. And when the acknowledgment is valid, it will be proper to order the debtor to hand over the loan property to the claimant agent. The author of al-Hidayah said: If a person claimed that his father died and the deposit with the depositary was left as inheritance for him, and the deceased has no other heir besides this claimant, and the depositary confirmed the claimant's statement, then the depositary will be ordered to give the deposit to this claimant because after the death of the depositor (mūdi'), the deposit is no longer his property; upon death, his ownership ends.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents three distinct rulings concerning claims on a deposit (wadi'ah) and the depositary's duty to deliver the property to the claimant. The rulings are based on whether the claim constitutes an acknowledgment of another's property. First, if a person claims to be an agent of the owner to take possession of the deposit, and the depositary confirms this, the depositary is not ordered to hand it over because the confirmation amounts to an acknowledgment of another's property (the owner's). This is contrasted with debts: in the case of a debt, the debtor can acknowledge an agent because the debtor's acknowledgment is against himself. Second, if the claimant asserts inheritance (owner has died and he is the sole heir), and the depositary confirms, then delivery is ordered because after the owner's death, the property no longer belongs to the owner, and both agree it belongs to the heir. Third, if the claimant asserts purchase from the owner while the owner is alive, and the depositary confirms, delivery is not ordered because it is still an acknowledgment of another's property, as the owner is alive and capable of ownership. The commentary elaborates on the terminology and reasoning, including the distinction between deposits (specific items) and debts (fungibles).

Key Terms
وديعت (wadi'ah): Deposit; property entrusted by owner (mūdi') to a trustee (mūda') for safekeeping
مودع (بفتح الدال) (mūda' (with fatha on dal)): The depositary or trustee; the person with whom the deposit is kept
مودع (بكسر الدال) (mūdi' (with kasra on dal)): The depositor or owner; the person who places the property on deposit
اقرار (iqrar): Admission or acknowledgment of a right or fact
دين (dayn): Debt; a liability that is paid by equivalent (mithli), not by a specific item

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a person claims to be an agent (wakil) to take possession of a deposit, and the depositary confirms, why is the depositary not ordered to hand over the deposit?
A) Because the depositary did not actually confirm
B) Because it amounts to an acknowledgment of another's property (the owner's)
C) Because the agent's claim is false
D) Because the owner has died

Key Takeaway
A depositary's confirmation of a claim only triggers a duty to deliver if the acknowledgment does not involve another's property rights, which occurs only when the owner's ownership has terminated (death) or the acknowledgment is against oneself (debt).

Agent Claiming Deposit: Depositee's Confirmation Not Binding
Ruling on a claimant alleging to be an agent for taking possession of a deposit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a claimant alleges to be an agent for taking possession of a deposit and the depositee confirms, and explain the distinction between deposits and debts in the validity of acknowledgment.

Core Idea
A depositee's confirmation of an agent's claim does not bind the owner; acknowledgment of another's right over specific property is invalid.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the Hanafi Book of Agency: a third party claims to be the depositor's agent for taking possession of a deposit, and the depositee confirms the claim. At first glance, the depositee's confirmation might seem sufficient to hand over the property. However, the Hanafi school rules that the depositee is not ordered to do so. The reasoning hinges on a fundamental distinction between specific property (ayn) and debt (dayn), and the validity of acknowledgment (iqrār) over the rights of a third party.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their roles
Understand the scenario: depositor (mūdi‘), depositee (mūda‘), and claimant agent. The depositor is absent and has not directly authorized the agent.
The depositee is a trustee (amin) of the specific property.
2
Identify the ruling
State that the depositee is not ordered (la yu'mar) to hand over the deposit to the claimant agent. This means it is not permissible for him to do so.
The ruling is from the judge's perspective; the depositee is prohibited from handing over.
3
Analyze the reason: acknowledgment of another's property
The depositee's confirmation would constitute an acknowledgment (iqrār) of the claimant's right to possession over property belonging to the absent depositor. Such acknowledgment regarding a third party's property is invalid in Hanafi law.
Iqrār is only valid when it binds the declarant himself, not a third party.
4
Contrast with debt
In a debt case, the debtor's acknowledgment of an agent to collect is valid. This is because the debt is a generic obligation (dayn) on the debtor himself; the acknowledgment binds the debtor, not the creditor.
Debts are discharged by equivalents, not specific items, so the debtor's acknowledgment is against himself.
5
Identify the dalil: istihsan
The distinction between deposit and debt is based on istihsan (juristic preference), which considers the nature of the right. The illa (effective cause) is that deposit involves specific property (ayn), while debt is a liability (dayn).
Istihsan overrides any analogical reasoning that might treat both cases alike.

Source Text

كتاب الوكالة

تشریح مودع بفتح الدال وہ آدمی جس کے پاس ودیعت کا مال رکھا گیا ہو یعنی امین اور مودع بكسر الدال مال ودیعت رکھنے والا یعنی مال کا مالک۔ مسئلہ کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص مثلاً عبداللہ نے اپنا مال عبد الرحمن کے پاس ودیعت کے طور پر رکھا پھر ایک تیسرے شخص مثلاً شاہد نے مودع ( بفتح الدال ) پر دعوی کیا کہ میں مودع ( بكسر الدال) کی طرف سے اس مال ودیعت پر قبضہ کرنے کا وکیل ہوں اور مودَع (بفتح الدال ) نے اس کی تصدیق بھی کر دی تو مورع کو یہ حکم نہیں دیا جائے گا کہ وہ مدعی کو مال ودیعت سپر دکر دے۔ کیونکہ مودَع (الفتح الدال ) کے پاس جو مال ودیعت ہے وہ مودع ( بكسر الدال) کی ملک ہے اور مودع (بفتح الدال ) اس کا معترف بھی ہے پس مودع ( فتح الدال ) کا مدعی وکالت کی تصدیق کرنا در حقیقت غیر یعنی مودع ) بكسر الدال ) کے مال پر مدعی وکالت کے لئے قبضہ کے حق کا اقرار کرنا ہے اور غیر کے مال پر قبضہ کے حق کا اقرار کرنا درست نہ ہوگا اور جب یہ اقرار درست نہیں ہے تو مودع (بفتح الدال) کو یہ حکم بھی نہیں دیا جائے گا کہ وہ مال ودیعت مدعی وکالت کے حوالہ کر دے تو قرضدار کو حکم دیا جائے گا کہ مال قرض مدعی وکالت کو دیدے کیونکہ دیون اور قرضے با مثالها ادا کئے جاتے ہیں نہ کہ با عیا تھا ۔ لہذا قرضدار کا مدعی وکالت کیلئے قرضہ پر قبضہ کرنے کے حق کا اقرار کرنا ہوگا نہ کہ غیر یعنی قرض خواہ پر۔ پس جب قرضدار کا اقرار خود اس کی ذات پر ہے تو یہ اقرار درست ہوگا اور جب اس صورت میں اقرار درست ہے تو قرضدار کو یہ حکم دینا بھی درست ہوگا کہ وہ قرضہ کا مال مدعی وکالت کے سپر د کر دے۔
Book of Agency: He is not ordered to hand it over to him because as long as he is alive, it is an acknowledgment of ownership of another, for he is among the people of eligibility, so they are not believed in the claim of sale against him. Translation: If a person said, 'I am an agent for taking possession of the deposit,' and the depositee confirmed him, then the depositee will not be ordered to hand the deposit over to that agent, because this is an acknowledgment of the property of another, unlike a debt. Explanation: Mūda‘ (with fatḥa on dāl) is the person with whom the deposit is placed, i.e., the trustee. Mūdi‘ (with kasra on dāl) is the one who places the deposit, i.e., the owner. The scenario is: A person, e.g., Abdullah, placed his property as a deposit with Abdur Rahman. Then a third person, e.g., Shahid, claimed to the depositee (Mūda‘) that he is the agent of the depositor (Mūdi‘) for taking possession of this deposit. The depositee confirmed him. Then the depositee will not be ordered to hand over the deposit to the claimant. Because the deposit with the depositee is the property of the depositor, and the depositee is also acknowledging that. So the depositee's confirmation of the claimant's agency is effectively an acknowledgment of the claimant's right to possession over the property of another, i.e., the depositor. Acknowledgment of the right to possession over another's property is not valid. When this acknowledgment is not valid, the depositee will not be ordered to hand over the deposit to the agent claimant. As for a debtor, he will be ordered to hand over the debt to the agent claimant because debts and loans are discharged by their equivalent, not by their specific items. Therefore, the debtor's acknowledgment of the claimant's right to take possession of the debt is an acknowledgment regarding himself, not regarding another (the creditor). So when the debtor's acknowledgment is upon himself, it is valid, and in that case it is valid to order the debtor to hand over the debt money to the agent claimant.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with legal reasoning from the Book of Agency. It addresses a scenario where a third party claims to be the agent of the depositor for taking possession of a deposit (wadi‘ah), and the depositee (the trustee) confirms the claim. The ruling is that the depositee is not ordered to hand over the deposit to the claimant. The reason is that the deposit is the property of the depositor, who is a living third party. The depositee's confirmation amounts to an acknowledgment of the claimant's right to possession over another's property, which is not valid because one cannot affect the rights of another without authorization. In contrast, if the matter were a debt, the debtor would be ordered to pay the agent claimant. The distinction is that debts are generic obligations, not linked to a specific object. When the debtor acknowledges the agent's right to collect, it is an acknowledgment against himself—he admits he owes the debt—and such an acknowledgment is valid. Therefore, the debtor must pay the agent, since the agent is acting for the creditor. The passage includes a detailed elucidation of the terms mūda‘ (depositee) and mūdi‘ (depositor), and uses an example with names to clarify the scenario. The key legal point is that a trustee cannot transfer possession of a deposit based solely on a third party's unsupported claim of agency, even if the trustee confirms it, because that would infringe on the rights of the absent owner.

Key Terms
مودع (بفتح الدال) (mūda‘): The person with whom the deposit is placed; the trustee or depositee.
مودع (بكسر الدال) (mūdi‘): The person who places the deposit; the depositor/owner.
ودیعت (wadī‘ah): A deposit; property left with another for safekeeping, which is a trust in the hands of the depositee.
وکالت (wakālah): Agency; the delegation of one's legal authority to another.
اقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment or confession; a legal admission that creates rights or obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a third party claims to be the depositor's agent to take possession of a deposit, and the depositee confirms, why is the depositee not ordered to hand over the deposit?
A) Because the depositee's confirmation is not valid evidence.
B) Because the deposit is a trust and the depositee cannot return it without the owner's direct order.
C) Because the confirmation would be an acknowledgment of another's right over the owner's property, which is invalid.
D) Because the claimant did not provide witnesses.

Key Takeaway
A depositee cannot transfer possession of a deposit based solely on a claimant's unsupported agency claim, even if the depositee confirms it, because such confirmation is an invalid acknowledgment of another's property.

Agent's Right to Collect Despite Debtor's Claim of Prior Payment
Ruling on agent for debt when debtor claims creditor already paid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a debtor claims prior payment after an agent is appointed, and explain the proof and the oath mechanism.

Core Idea
The debtor must pay the agent immediately despite claiming prior payment; the debtor's recourse is an oath from the creditor, not the agent.

This passage addresses a common dispute in debt collection: what happens when a debtor claims the creditor already received payment? The Hanafi school holds that the agency overrides the mere claim, so the agent collects immediately, but the debtor can later demand an oath from the creditor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The creditor appoints an agent to collect a debt. The debtor then claims that the creditor has already received payment. Understand the parties: creditor (principal), agent (wakil), debtor.
2
Understand the ruling
The debtor must pay the agent immediately. The agency is established, and the mere claim of prior payment does not suspend the agent's right.
The ruling is wajib: the debtor is obliged to pay the agent.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The agency is proven by mutual agreement or evidence. The debtor's claim is unproven; thus, it does not override the established agency. The ruling is based on qiyas: the agent's right is analogous to the principal's right, and a claim without proof does not defeat a proven right.
The proof is aqli (rational) – the principle that a mere assertion cannot invalidate an established right.
4
Examine the oath mechanism
To protect the debtor, he may demand an oath from the creditor (not the agent) that he did not receive payment. If the creditor swears, payment to agent is valid. If creditor refuses, debtor can take back the money from the agent.
Deputyship in oaths is not allowed in Hanafi law, so the agent cannot be sworn in place of the principal.

Source Text

قرضدار نے کسی آدمی کو قرضہ وصول کرنے کا وکیل کیا پھر قرضدار نے دعویٰ کیا کہ قرض خواہ اپنا مال وصول کر چکا ہے قرضدار قرضہ وکیل کو دے
قال فان وكل وكيلاً بقبض ماله فادعى الغريم ان صاحب المال قد استوفاه فانه يدفع المال اليه لان الوكالة قد يثبت بالتصادق والاستيفاء لم يثبت بمجرد دعواه فلا يؤخر الحق قال ويتبع رب المال فيستحلفه رعاية لجانبه ولا يستحلف الوكيل لانه نائبه
ترجمہ اگر کسی نے اپنا مال وصول کرنے کیلئے کسی کو کیا کیا پھر قرضدار نے کہا کہ صاحب مال نے اپنا مال وصول کر لیا ہے تو مال ، وکیل کو دیدیا جائے گا اسلئے کہ وکالت ان دونوں کے اتفاق سے ثابت ہو گئی اور مال کو وصول کرنا محض اس کے دعوا بی سے ثابت نہیں ہوا لہذا حق کو موخر نہ کیا جائیگا۔ اور قرضدار ، قرض خواہ کے پیچھے پڑ کر اس سے قسم لے گا تاکہ قرضدار کی جانب کا لحاظ رہے اور وکیل سے قسم نہیں لی جائے گی اس لئے کہ وہ اپنے موکل کا نائب ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر قرض خواہ نے کسی آدمی کو اس بات پر وکیل کیا کہ قرضدار سے میرے قرضہ کا مال وصول کر لے پھر قرضدار نے دعوی کیا کہ قرض خواہ اپنا مال وصول کر چکا ہے تو اس صورت میں قرضدار اس کا مکلف ہوگا کہ مال قرض وکیل کو دے دے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکالت وکیل اور قرضدار دونوں کے اتفاق کر لینے سے ثابت ہو گئی ہے۔ بعض نسخوں میں بالتصادق کا لفظ نہیں ہے الہذا ان نسخوں کے مطابق بقول صاحب عنایہ یہ مطلب ہوگا کہ وکالت ، بینہ سے ثابت ہو گئی ہے اس لئے کہ مسئلہ اس صورت میں فرض کیا گیا ہے کہ وکیل نے اپنی وکالت کو بعینہ کے ذریعہ ثابت کر دیا ہو بہر حال وکیل کی وکالت ثابت ہوگئی اور قرض خواہ کا مال قرض وصول کر نا محض قرضدار کے دعوی سے قرض وصول کرنا ثابت نہیں ہوا تو وکیل کو مال قرض پر قبضہ کرنے کا جو حق تھا اس کو قرض خواہ سے قسم کھلانے تک مؤخر نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ بلکہ وکیل کو مال قرض دیگر اس حق کو فوراً ادا کیا جائے گا البتہ قرضدار قرض خواہ کا دامن گیر ہو کر قرض خواہ سے قسم لے گا کیونکہ قرضدار کی رعایت کرنا بھی ضروری ہے اور اس قسم دلانے میں بلاشبہ قرضدار کی رعایت ہے بہرحا ل قرض خواہ اگر یہ قسم کھا گیا کہ میں نے قرضہ کا مال وصول نہیں کیا ہے تو قرضدار سے جو مال وکیل کو دلایا گیا ہے اس سے قرضہ کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی اور یہ اداء کرنا نافذ ہو جائیگا۔ اور اگر قرض خواہ نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو قرضدار ، قابض یعنی وکیل کا دامن گیر ہوگا اور دیا ہوا مال واپس لے گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قرض خواہ کے بدلے وکیل سے قسم نہیں لی جائے گی اس لئے کہ وکیل اسکا نائب ہے اور ایمان میں نیابت فرماتےہیں نہیں لی ارکان ہےاور جاری نہیں ہوتی ۔
A debtor appointed someone as an agent to collect a debt, then the debtor claimed that the creditor had already received his property. The debtor gives the debt to the agent. He said: If he appoints an agent to collect his property, and the debtor claims that the owner of the property has already received it, then he gives the property to him because the agency is established by mutual agreement, and the receipt is not established by mere claim, so the right is not delayed. He said: And he follows the owner of the property and makes him swear an oath out of consideration for his side, and the agent is not made to swear because he is his deputy. Translation: If someone appointed someone as an agent to collect his property, and then the debtor said that the owner of the property has already received his property, then the property will be given to the agent because the agency is established by the agreement of both, and receiving the property is not established by mere claim, so the right will not be delayed. And the debtor will follow the creditor and take an oath from him so that the debtor's side is considered, and the agent will not be made to take an oath because he is the deputy of his principal. Explanation: The scenario is that if a creditor appointed someone as an agent to collect the debt amount from the debtor, and then the debtor claimed that the creditor had already received his property, in this case the debtor will be obligated to give the debt amount to the agent. The proof is that the agency is established by the mutual agreement of the agent and the debtor. In some copies, the word 'bi al-tasāduq' is not present; therefore, according to those copies, per the author of 'Inayah, this meaning will be that the agency is established by evidence, because the case is assumed that the agent has proven his agency by evidence. In any case, the agent's agency is established, and the creditor's receipt of the debt is not established merely by the debtor's claim, so the agent's right to take possession of the debt will not be postponed until the oath of the creditor. Rather, the agent will be given the debt amount immediately. However, the debtor will follow the creditor and take an oath from him, because consideration for the debtor is also necessary, and in this oath-taking, undoubtedly there is consideration for the debtor. In any case, if the creditor swears that he did not receive the debt amount, then the debt that was delivered to the agent from the debtor will be considered as payment, and this payment will become effective. And if the creditor refuses to swear, then the debtor will follow the possessor, i.e., the agent, and take back the delivered property. The author of Hidayah says that the agent will not be made to swear in place of the creditor because the agent is his deputy, and deputyship in oaths is not established, it is not permissible, and it does not apply.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage covers a ruling on agency (wakalah) in debt collection. It begins with a scenario: a creditor appoints an agent to collect a debt from a debtor. The debtor then claims that the creditor has already received payment. The ruling is that the debtor must still pay the agent immediately. The reasoning is that the agency is established (either by mutual agreement or by evidence), while the debtor's claim of prior payment is a mere assertion that does not suspend the agent's right to collect. However, to protect the debtor's interests, the debtor is allowed to demand an oath from the creditor (not the agent) that he did not receive payment. If the creditor swears, the payment to the agent is valid. If the creditor refuses, the debtor can take back the money from the agent. The agent is not sworn because deputyship in oaths is not recognized; the oath must be from the principal. This ruling balances the rights of all parties: the agent's authority is honored, but the debtor is not left without recourse against a potential false claim.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakīl): Agent; a person appointed to act on behalf of another (the principal) in a specific matter, here debt collection.
موکل (muwakkil): Principal; the person who appoints an agent. Here, the creditor is the principal.
قسم (qasam): Oath; a sworn statement. Here, the debtor can demand an oath from the creditor regarding receipt of payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi law, if a debtor claims the creditor already received payment after an agent is appointed to collect, the agent must:
A) Wait until the creditor confirms the debtor's claim.
B) Collect the debt immediately, and the debtor can later demand an oath from the creditor.
C) Refuse to collect until the debtor proves the claim.
D) Collect only after the creditor takes an oath.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a valid agency allows immediate collection over a debtor's unsubstantiated claim of prior payment; the debtor's remedy is an oath from the creditor.

Agent Spending Own Money on Principal's Family: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling with proof: agency for spending

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent spending his own money for the principal's family and explain why istihsan is applied instead of qiyas.

Core Idea
An agent for spending is effectively an agent for purchase, so spending his own money is reimbursable by istihsan.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in Hanafi agency law. The central question: can an agent who is given money for his principal's family spend his own money and still recover from the principal? The text presents the Hanafi position, supported by istihsan (juristic preference), and contrasts it with a stricter qiyas (analogy) that would make the agent a volunteer. Understanding this distinction sharpens your appreciation of how Hanafi jurists balance textual analogy with equitable outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Ruling
Read the matn: a principal gives ten dirhams to an agent to spend on his family. The agent spends ten dirhams from his own pocket. The ruling: those ten become in exchange for the principal's ten.
The agent does not lose his money; he effectively buys the principal's dirhams.
2
Understand the Reasoning: Agency for Purchase
The commentary explains that an agent for spending (wakil bil-infaq) is in reality an agent for purchase (wakil bil-shira'), because spending on the family requires buying provisions. Hence the same rule applies: if the agent pays from his own pocket, he can recover from the principal.
This is the established ruling for wakil bil-shira'.
3
Examine the Qiyas Objection
Qiyas would say the agent cannot do this; he becomes a volunteer (mutabarri') and must return the principal's dirhams. The basis: spending is not exactly the same as purchasing.
This is the alternative view that istihsan overrides.
4
Apply Istihsan to Override Qiyas
The Hanafi position relies on istihsan because spending includes purchase (infaq yatadamman al-shira'). The effective cause (illa) of the original ruling (agent can recover) is present, so equity dictates the same outcome.
Istihsan avoids the harshness of qiyas that would penalize the agent.
5
Note the Distinction from Debt Repayment
Some scholars say that qiyas and istihsan apply only to paying debts (qada' al-dayn), not to spending that involves purchase. But here spending includes purchase, so istihsan is correctly applied.
This nuance shows the precision of Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شخص نے دوسرے کو دس درہم دیئے تا کہ وہ اس کے بچوں پر خرچ کرے اس نے اپنے پاس سے دس درہم ان پر خرچ کئے تو یہ دس ان دس کے عوض ہو جائیں گے
قال ومن دفع الى رجل عشرة دراهم لينفقها على اهله فانفق عشرة عليهم من عنده فالعشرة بالعشرة لان الوكيل بالاتفاق وكيل بالشراء والحكم فيه ما ذكرناه وقد قدرناه فهذا كذالك وقيل هذا استحسان و في القياس ليس له ذالك و يصير متبرعاً و قيل القياس والاستحسان في قضاء الدين لانه ليس بشراء واما الانفاق يتضمن الشراء فلا يدخلانه والله اعلم.
ترجمہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے شخص کو دس درہم دیے تا کہ وہ ان کو اس کے بچوں پر خرچ کرے۔ بس اس نے اپنے پاس سے دس درہم ان پر خرچ کئے تو یہ دس ان دس کے عوض ہو جائیں گے۔ اس لئے کہ خرچ کرنے کا وکیل خرید کرنے کا وکیل ہے اور وکیل بالشراء میں حکم وہی ہے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے اور اس کو ثابت کر چکے۔ پس اس کا حکم بھی ایسا ہی ہے اور کہا گیا کہ یہ استحسان ہے اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ اس کے لئے یہ جائز نہیں ہے اور یہ متبرع ہو جائے گا اور کہا گیا کہ قیاس و استحسان قرض ادا کرنے کی صورت میں ہے کیونکہ یہ خریداری نہیں ہے اور رہا خرچ کرنا تو وہ شراء کو تضمن ہے پس اس میں قیاس و استحسان داخل نہ ہوں گے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص مثلاً حامد نے دوسرے شخص مثلاً خالد کو دس درہم اس لئے دیئے تا کہ خالد ان دراہم کو حامد (موکل) کے اہل و عیال پر خرچ کرے پس خالد (وکیل) نے ان پر اپنے پاس سے خرچ کئے تو یہ دس درہم جن کو وکیل نے اپنے پاس سے خرچ کیا ہے ان دس دراہم کے مقابلہ میں ہو جائیں گے جن کو وکیل (خالد) نے موکل (حامد) سے لیا تھا حاصل یہ کہ وکیل ان دراہم کو خرچ کرنے میں تبرع کرنے والا نہیں ہوگا بلکہ جو درہم اس نے موکل سے لئے تھے ان کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس مسئلہ میں اتفاق اور خرچ کرنے کا وکیل در حقیقت شراء اور خرید کرنے کا وکیل ہے کیونکہ مؤکل کے اہل و عیال پر خرچ کرنے کے لئے وکیل ایسی چیز خریدنے پر مجبور ہوگا جو ان کا نفقہ بن سکتی ہو اور کبھی وکیل کے پاس موکل کے دیئے ہوئے دراہم موجود نہیں ہوتے تو وہ اس بات کا محتاج ہو گا خرید کردہ چیز کی قیمت اپنے مال سے ادا کرے اور موکل کے دیئے ہوئے دراہم اپنے پاس رکھ لے پس توکیل بالشراء میں اس طرح کے استبدال کی اجازت ہوتی ہے بہر حال وکیل بالانفاق در حقیقت وکیل بالشراء ہے اور وکیل بالشراء کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر وہ ثمن اپنے پاس سے ادا کر دے تو اس کو موکل سے رجوع کرنے کی اجازت ہوتی ہے جیسا کہ پہلے بیان کیا جا چکا ہے۔ پس اسی طرح وکیل بالانفاق نے جو در حقیقت وکیل بالشراء ہے اگر مؤکل کے اہل و عیال پر اپنے پاس سے خرچ کیا ہے تو وہ موکل کے مال سے وصول کر سکتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ بعض مشائخ کے قول کے مطابق مذکورہ حکم استحسان ہے ورنہ قیاس یہ ہے کہ وکیل کے لئے یہ بات جائز نہیں ہے کہ وکیل موکل کے دیئے ہوئے دس درہم کے مقابلہ میں اپنے پاس سے دس درہم خرچ کرے بلکہ اگر اس نے اپنے پاس سے دس درہم خرچ کئے تو وہ خرچ کردہ دراہم میں تبرع کرنے والا ہو گا اور جو دراہم اس نے مؤکل سے لئے ان کو واپس کرنا لازم ہوگا۔
A person gave ten dirhams to another to spend on his children. He spent ten dirhams from himself on them, so these ten are in exchange for those ten.
He said: And whoever gives ten dirhams to a man to spend on his family, and he spends ten from himself on them, then the ten are for the ten, because the agent is, by agreement, an agent for purchase, and the ruling therein is what we mentioned and we have established it. So this is like that. And it was said: This is istihsan, and in qiyas he does not have that and becomes a volunteer. And it was said: Qiyas and istihsan are in the case of paying a debt, because it is not a purchase. As for spending, it includes purchase, so they do not enter into it. And Allah knows best.
Translation: If a person gives ten dirhams to another person to spend on his children, and he spends ten dirhams from himself on them, then these ten become in exchange for those ten. Because the agent for spending is an agent for purchase, and the ruling for the agent for purchase is what we have mentioned and established. So his ruling is also similar. And it was said that this is istihsan, and qiyas is that it is not permissible for him and he becomes a volunteer. And it was said that qiyas and istihsan are in the case of paying a debt, because it is not a purchase. As for spending, it includes purchase, so qiyas and istihsan do not enter into it. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The scenario is that a person, for example Hamid, gave ten dirhams to another person, for example Khalid, so that Khalid would spend those dirhams on Hamid's (the principal's) family. Then Khalid (the agent) spent from his own pocket on them. So these ten dirhams that the agent spent from his own pocket will be in exchange for those ten dirhams that the agent (Khalid) had taken from the principal (Hamid). The result is that the agent will not be a volunteer in spending those dirhams; rather, he will become the owner of the dirhams he took from the principal. The evidence is that there is agreement in this matter, and the agent for spending is in reality an agent for purchase, because to spend on the principal's family, the agent will be compelled to buy something that can become their maintenance, and sometimes the agent does not have the dirhams given by the principal, so he needs to pay the price of the purchased item from his own wealth and keep the principal's dirhams with him. Thus, in agency for purchase, such substitution is permitted. In any case, the agent for spending is in reality an agent for purchase, and the ruling for the agent for purchase is that if he pays the price from his own pocket, he is allowed to seek reimbursement from the principal, as has been stated before. Similarly, the agent for spending, who is in reality an agent for purchase, if he has spent on the principal's family from his own pocket, then he can recover from the principal's wealth. Sahib al-Hidayah says that according to the saying of some mashayikh, the aforementioned ruling is istihsan; otherwise, qiyas is that it is not permissible for the agent to spend ten dirhams from his own pocket in exchange for the ten dirhams given by the principal; rather, if he spent ten dirhams from his own pocket, he becomes a volunteer in the spent dirhams, and he must return the dirhams he took from the principal.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on agency for expenditure (wakalah bil-infaaq). The matn states that if a principal gives ten dirhams to an agent to spend on the principal's family, and the agent instead spends ten dirhams from his own pocket, those ten dirhams become equivalent to the ten given by the principal. The commentary explains that this is because the agent for spending is effectively an agent for purchase (wakil bil-shira'), since spending on the family requires purchasing provisions. The established ruling for an agent for purchase is that if he pays the price from his own funds, he can recover from the principal. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas (analogy) would be that the agent cannot do this and becomes a volunteer (mutabarri'), but istihsan overrides qiyas. There is a further nuance: some scholars say that qiyas and istihsan apply only in the case of debt repayment (qada' al-dayn), not in spending that involves purchase. However, since spending here includes purchase, istihsan is applied. Sahib al-Hidayah notes that according to some mashayikh, the ruling is istihsan; otherwise, qiyas would require the agent to return the principal's dirhams and be a volunteer. The passage thus illustrates the Hanafi use of istihsan to achieve equity in agency relationships.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas to achieve a more equitable outcome.
وکیل بالشراء (wakil bil-shira'): Agent authorized to purchase on behalf of the principal.
وکیل بالانفاق (wakil bil-infaq): Agent authorized to spend on the principal's dependents.
متبرع (mutabarri'): One who acts voluntarily without expectation of compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason given in the text for treating an agent for spending as an agent for purchase?
A) Because spending on the family requires buying provisions.
B) Because the agent is always authorized to borrow.
C) Because the principal's money is not sufficient.
D) Because the agent has no choice.

Key Takeaway
An agent for spending is treated as an agent for purchase, allowing him to use his own money and recover from the principal under istihsan, overriding the stricter qiyas.

Agent Spending His Own Money: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Explains ruling and qiyas/istihsan dispute on agent's substitution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent substituting his own money for the principal's and explain how the dispute between qiyas and istihsan is resolved.

Core Idea
An agent spending on the principal's family is an agent for purchase, so using his own money is valid and he can recoup.

In this lesson, we examine a classic Hanafi dispute: when a principal gives specific dirhams to an agent to spend on his family, can the agent use his own dirhams instead and claim reimbursement? The passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explores both qiyas and istihsan reasoning, ultimately showing that both converge on permissibility.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the passage rules: the agent can recoup; the ten spent are exchanged for the ten received.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opposing view
Some mashayikh held that this is only istihsan; strict qiyas would make him a volunteer.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference.
3
Follow the strict qiyas reasoning
Strict analogy: the agent was given specific money to spend, so he must use that money; using his own is a deviation.
This view sees the agent as a mere conveyor of funds.
4
Analyse the istihsan reasoning
Spending on family necessarily involves purchase; thus the agent is effectively an agent for purchase, where substitution is allowed.
Istihsan considers practical need and implied authorization.
5
Determine the resolution
The author argues that even qiyas supports recoupment because spending entails purchase; thus both qiyas and istihsan agree.
The mufta bihi is the permissibility.

قال ومن دفع الى رجل عشرة دراهم لينفقها على اهله فانفق عشرة عليهم من عنده فالعشرة بالعشرة لان الوكيل بالاتفاق وكيل بالشراء والحكم فيه ما ذكرناه وقد قدرناه فهذا كذالك وقيل هذا استحسان و في القياس ليس له ذالك و يصير متبرعاً و قيل القياس والاستحسان في قضاء الدين لانه ليس بشراء واما الانفاق يتضمن الشراء فلا يدخلانه والله اعلم.
ترجمہ اگر ایک شخص نے دوسرے شخص کو دس درہم دیے تا کہ وہ ان کو اس کے بچوں پر خرچ کرے۔ بس اس نے اپنے پاس سے دس در ہم ان پر خرچ کئے تو یہ دس ان دس کے عوض ہو جائیں گے۔ اس لئے کہ خرچ کرنے کا وکیل خرید کرنے قرض کی صورت میں جاری ہیں یعنی اگر قرضدار نے اپنے وکیل کو ہزار درہم دیئے تا کہ اس کے قرض خواہ کو ادا کر دے لیکن وکیل نے ان دراہم کی جگہ اپنے پاس سے ہزار درہم ادا کر دیئے تو استحسان یہ ہے کہ وکیل کے لئے ایسا کرنا جائز ہے اور وہ ادا کردہ ہزار درہم، موکل کے مال سے وصول کرے گا اور قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ وکیل نے اپنے پاس سے ہزار درہم ادا کر کے تبرع کیا ہے اور وہ موکل کے مال سے واپس لینے کا مجاز نہیں ہے کیونکہ ادائے قرض ، خرید کرنے کے معنی میں نہیں ہے بلکہ جو درہم موکل سے لئے ہیں انہیں کو دینا لازم ہے پس جب وکیل کا اپنے پاس سے ادا کرنا مؤکل کی منشاء کے مطابق نہ ہوگا اور جب یہ ادائیگی مؤکل کی منشاء کے بھی ادا کردہ مال موکل کے مال سے وصول کرنے کا مجاز ہوگا۔ اور ہاں بال بچوں پر خرچ کرنا تو وہ خرید کرنے کو متضمن ہوتا ہے یعنی موکل کی طرف سے خرچ کرنے کا امر در حقیقت خرید کرنے کا امر ہوتا ہے اور خریداری متبرع نہ ہو گا اس کو مؤکل کے مال سے وصول کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب . جمیل احمد عفاه الله
He said: And if someone gave ten dirhams to a man to spend on his family, and he spent ten from himself on them, then the ten are exchanged for the ten, because the agent by agreement is an agent for purchase, and the ruling in that is what we mentioned and we have determined it, so this is like that. And it was said: this is istihsan, and in qiyas he does not have that and he becomes a volunteer. And it was said: qiyas and istihsan are in the repayment of debt because it is not a purchase, but spending entails purchase, so they do not enter it. And Allah knows best. Then the Urdu commentary explains the scenario with names Hammad and Khalid, states the ruling, provides the reason that the spending agent is effectively a purchasing agent, and discusses the opinions of some mashayikh that the ruling is istihsan, and that in qiyas it is not permissible. Also discusses the difference between debt repayment and spending on family. The author concludes that in the case of spending on family, qiyas and istihsan agree that the agent can recoup.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is a commentary on a ruling from al-Hidaya regarding an agent appointed to spend money on the principal's family. The passage begins by stating the ruling: if the principal gives 10 dirhams to the agent for spending, and the agent instead spends 10 dirhams from his own pocket, then the 10 he spent are considered in exchange for the 10 he received; he is not a volunteer. The reason is that an agent for spending is by agreement an agent for purchase, because spending on a family requires purchasing provisions. The ruling for an agent for purchase has already been established: if he pays the price from his own pocket, he can recoup from the principal. The same applies here. Then the passage notes that some scholars consider this ruling to be based on istihsan (juristic preference), while qiyas (analogy) would make the agent a volunteer and not allow recoupment. Another view is that the distinction between qiyas and istihsan applies only in the case of debt repayment, not spending, because spending involves purchase. However, the author then elaborates that in the case of spending on family, the stronger view is that qiyas also allows recoupment because spending necessarily entails purchase. Thus, the final position is that both qiyas and istihsan agree that the agent can recoup from the principal. This is a clear example of how Hanafi scholars resolve apparent conflicts between qiyas and istihsan by analyzing the underlying 'illa (effective cause).

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that departs from strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling based on need, custom, or implied authorization.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning that applies a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared effective cause ('illa).
وکالت (wakalah): A contract of agency where one person (principal) appoints another (agent) to perform a legal act on his behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, if a principal gives an agent 10 dirhams to spend on his family, and the agent spends 10 dirhams from his own pocket, what is the ruling?
A) The agent is a volunteer and cannot claim reimbursement.
B) The agent can recoup the 10 dirhams from the principal because spending entails purchase.
C) The agent must return the 10 dirhams he received and cannot claim anything.
D) The agent can only recoup if the principal explicitly agreed in advance.

Key Takeaway
The agent appointed to spend on family is effectively an agent for purchase, so using his own money is valid and he can claim reimbursement.

The Principal's Right to Dismiss the Agent and Its Exception
States the general rule of dismissal and exception for third-party rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a principal may dismiss an agent except when a third-party right is attached, and apply this rule to determine the validity of a dismissal in a given scenario.

Core Idea
The principal can dismiss the agent unless a third party's right is attached.

In this lesson, we examine the principal's power to dismiss his agent. While the agency contract gives the principal the right to revoke at will, this right is not absolute. When a third party's legitimate interest becomes attached to the agency, the principal loses his right to dismiss. We will explore the general rule, the key exception, and a paradigmatic example: the litigation agent appointed at the plaintiff's request.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
State the principal's default right: he may dismiss the agent at any time because agency is his right.
This is the starting point of the passage.
2
Recognize the exception
Note the condition that if a third party's right (ḥaqq al-ghayr) is attached to the agency, dismissal is not allowed.
The exception is introduced with 'except when' (illā idhā).
3
Understand the example
The passage gives the case of an agent appointed for litigation at the request of the plaintiff: dismissal would nullify the plaintiff's right to representation.
This shows a concrete application of the exception.
4
Compare with pledge analogy
The text likens the litigation agency to an agency included in a pledge contract, where the pledgee's right cannot be revoked by the pledgor.
This analogy strengthens the rule.

Source Text

باب عزل الوكيل
ترجمہ یہ باب وکیل کے معزول کرنے کے بیان میں ہے
مؤکل وکیل کو وکالت سے معزول کر سکتا ہے
قال وللمؤ كل ان يعزل الوكيل عن الوكالة لان الوكالة حقه فله ان يبطله الا اذا تعلق به حق الغير بان كان وكيلاً بالخصومة بطلب من جهة الطالب لما فيه من ابطال حق الغير وصار كالوكالة التي تضمنها عقد الرهن
ترجمہ موکل کو اختیار ہے کہ اپنے وکیل کو وکالت سے معزول کر دے کیونکہ وکالت موکل کا حق ہے لہذا اس کو حق باطل کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا مگر جب کہ اس کے ساتھ دوسرے کا حق متعلق ہو بایں طور کہ مدعی کی درخواست سے وکیل ہو اس لئے کہ اس میں غیر کے حق کو باطل کرنا ہے اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا کہ وہ وکالت جس کو عقد رہن متضمن ہو۔
Chapter on Dismissal of the Agent. Translation: This chapter is about dismissing the agent. The principal can dismiss the agent from the agency. He said: The principal may dismiss the agent from the agency because agency is his right, so he has the right to nullify it, except when a right of another person is attached to it, such as if he was an agent for litigation at the request of the plaintiff, because that would nullify the right of another, and it becomes like the agency that is included in a contract of pledge (rahn). Translation: The principal has the authority to dismiss his agent from the agency because agency is the principal's right, so he has the authority to nullify it, except when the right of another is attached to it, such as when the agent was appointed for litigation at the request of the plaintiff, because in that case nullifying would cancel the right of another, and it becomes like the agency that is included in a contract of pledge.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the dismissal of the agent (عزل الوكيل). It states the general rule: the principal has the right to dismiss his agent at any time, because the agency is the principal's right. He can revoke it as he wishes. However, there is a crucial exception: if a third party's right has become attached to the agency, the principal cannot unilaterally dismiss the agent. The example given is when the agent was appointed for litigation (وكيل بالخصومة) at the request of the plaintiff (المدعي). In such a case, the plaintiff has a right to have the agent represent the defendant. If the principal dismisses the agent, he would nullify the plaintiff's right. Therefore, dismissal is not allowed. This is similar to the agency that is encompassed in a contract of pledge (رهن), where the pledgee's right is attached and cannot be revoked by the pledgor. The Hanafi school holds that the principal's right to dismiss is generally absolute, but constrained by the rights of others. This ensures that agency contracts do not harm the legitimate interests of third parties who rely on the representation.

Key Terms
عزل ('azl): Dismissal of an agent by the principal, revoking the agency contract.
وكيل بالخصومة (wakīl bi al-khuṣūmah): An agent appointed for litigation, i.e., to represent the principal in court proceedings.
حق الغير (ḥaqq al-ghayr): Right of a third party that is attached to the agency contract, preventing dismissal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which case can the principal NOT dismiss the agent according to the Hanafi school?
A) When the agent was appointed for a limited time.
B) When the agent has not yet performed any act.
C) When the agent was appointed for litigation at the request of the plaintiff.
D) When the agent is a close relative of the principal.

Key Takeaway
The principal may dismiss his agent except when a third party's right is attached to the agency, such as in litigation representation requested by the plaintiff.

Istihsan in Agency: Agent Paying Debt from His Own Money
Explaining istihsan for debt payment agent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that an agent paying a debt from his own money can recover the amount from the principal, using istihsan, and distinguish it from the qiyas ruling.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas: an agent paying a debt from his own funds is treated like a purchase agent, so he recovers.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi case where an agent (wakil) entrusted with specific coins to pay a debt instead uses his own money. The apparent analogy (qiyas jali) suggests he is a donor. However, the Hanafi school prefers istihsan, analogizing debt payment to purchase, allowing recovery. We will trace the reasoning and see how later scholars expanded the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two rulings
The principal gives the agent 1000 dirhams to pay a debt. The agent pays from his own money instead. Qiyas says it's a donation (tabarru') – no recovery. Istihsan says it's permissible and the agent can recover.
This is the core conflict.
2
Understand the qiyas argument (jali)
Qiyas argues that debt payment is not purchase; the agent was ordered to use the specific dirhams. Using his own money deviates from the principal's order, so he is a donor.
Key premise: debt payment ≠ purchase.
3
Understand the istihsan argument (khafi)
Istihsan relies on a hidden analogy: the agent is effectively buying the debt (the principal's obligation) from the creditor. A purchase agent who pays from his own money always recovers. Therefore, the debt payment agent should also recover.
The illa is the meaning of purchase embedded in debt payment.
4
See the expansion to spending on children
The author extends the reasoning to another example: an agent ordered to spend on the principal's children. Here both qiyas and istihsan agree – the agent is not a donor because spending entails purchase.
This confirms the illa: any agency that involves a financial obligation similar to purchase allows recovery.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text adopts the istihsan view, which is the operative position in the later Hanafi school (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
The ruling is that the agent recovers the paid amount.

بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ یہ قیاس و استحسان ادائے قرض کی صورت میں جاری ہیں یعنی اگر قرضدار نے اپنے وکیل کو ہزار درہم دیئے تا کہ اس کے قرض خواہ کو ادا کر دے لیکن وکیل نے ان دراہم کی جگہ اپنے پاس سے ہزار درہم ادا کر دیئے تو استحسان یہ ہے کہ وکیل کے لئے ایسا کرنا جائز ہے اور وہ ادا کردہ ہزار درہم، موکل کے مال سے وصول کرے گا اور قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ وکیل نے اپنے پاس سے ہزار درہم ادا کر کے تبرع کیا ہے اور وہ موکل کے مال سے واپس لینے کا مجاز نہیں ہے کیونکہ ادائے قرض ، خرید کرنے کے معنی میں نہیں ہے بلکہ جو درہم موکل سے لئے ہیں انہیں کو دینا لازم ہے پس جب وکیل کا اپنے پاس سے ادا کرنا مؤکل کی منشاء کے مطابق نہ ہوگا اور جب یہ ادائیگی مؤکل کی منشاء کے مطابق نہیں ہے تو وکیل اس ادا کرنے میں متبرع ہوگا اور جب وکیل اس ادائیگی میں متبرع ہے تو وہ موکل کے مال سے وصول کرنے کا مجاز بھی نہ ہوگا۔ اور اس مسئلہ میں وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ ادائیگی قرض کا وکیل اس چیز کو جو موکل کے ذمہ میں ہوتی ہے دراہم کے عوض خریدنے کا وکیل ہوتا ہے اور وکیل بالشراء جب خریداری کرے اور شمن اپنے پاس سے ادا کر دے تو وہ متوکل سے رجوع با شمن کرنے کا مجاز ہے لہذا ادائے قرض کا وکیل بھی ادا کردہ مال موکل کے مال سے وصول کرنے کا مجاز ہوگا۔ اور ہاں بال بچوں پر خرچ کرنا تو وہ خرید کرنے کو متضمن ہوتا ہے یعنی موکل کی طرف سے خرچ کرنے کا امر در حقیقت خرید کرنے کا امر ہوتا ہے اور خریداری بعینہ ان دراہم کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہوتی جو دراہم مؤکل نے وکیل کو دیئے ہیں بلکہ خرید کرنے کی وجہ سے وکیل کے ذمدان در اہم کے مثل ثابت ہوتے ہیں پھر وکیل کے لئے ان دراہم کو رجوع کرنے کا اختیار ثابت ہوتا ہے اور جب ایسا ہو تو وکیل قیاسا بھی تبرع کرنے والا نہ ہو گا یعنی مسئلہ انفاق میں قیاس اور استحسان کا حکم یکساں ہوگا یعنی قیاس اور استحسان دونوں کے حکم کے مطابق وکیل بالا نفاق اپنے مال کو خرچ کرنے میں متبرع نہ ہو گا اس کو مؤکل کے مال سے وصول کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب . جمیل احمد عفاه الله
Some scholars said that this qiyas and istihsan apply in the case of debt payment. That is, if a debtor gave his wakil one thousand dirhams to pay his creditor, but the wakil paid one thousand dirhams from his own pocket instead of those dirhams, then istihsan is that it is permissible for the wakil to do so, and he will recover the one thousand dirhams he paid from the principal's wealth. Qiyas requires that the wakil, by paying one thousand dirhams from his own pocket, has made a gratuitous payment (tabarru'), and he is not authorized to recover it from the principal's wealth, because debt payment is not in the meaning of purchase; rather, it is necessary to give the very dirhams he received from the principal. So when the wakil pays from his own pocket, it does not conform to the principal's wish, and when it does not conform, the wakil is a donor in this payment, and thus he is not authorized to recover from the principal's wealth. The istihsan justification in this issue is that the wakil for debt payment is a wakil to purchase the obligation (that is, the debt) from the creditor with those dirhams, and a wakil for purchase, when he buys and pays the price from his own pocket, is authorized to recover the price from the principal. Hence, the wakil for debt payment is also authorized to recover the paid amount from the principal's wealth. As for spending on children, that entails purchase; the principal's order to spend is essentially an order to purchase, and purchase is not specifically tied to the exact dirhams given by the principal, but a similar amount becomes due in the wakil's liability, so the wakil has the option to recover those dirhams. When this is the case, the wakil, by qiyas as well, is not a donor; that is, in the spending issue, qiyas and istihsan have the same ruling: the wakil for spending is not a donor and has the right to recover from the principal's wealth. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, may Allah forgive him.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the Hanafi position on an agent (wakil) who pays off the principal's debt using his own money instead of the money given by the principal. The text presents both qiyas (analogical reasoning) and istihsan (juristic preference). According to qiyas, the agent is considered a donor (mutabarri') because he did not use the specific dirhams given by the principal, so he cannot recover the amount. However, istihsan permits the agent to recover because debt payment is analogous to purchase: the agent is effectively buying the debt from the creditor using his own funds, and a purchase agent is always allowed to recover the price he paid. The author strengthens this by comparing to spending on children (nafaqah), where qiyas and istihsan agree that the agent is not a donor. The weight of the ruling is that istihsan is the operative position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, as indicated by the text's adoption of istihsan. The authority comes from the later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) as stated by 'some scholars'. The proof mechanism is istihsan based on the meaning of purchase embedded in debt payment.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference based on a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) that overrides the apparent analogy (qiyas jali) to avoid hardship.
تبرع (tabarru'): A gratuitous act or donation done without expectation of compensation. In the text, the wakil paying from his own money without right of recovery is considered tabarru'.
وكيل بالشراء (wakil bi al-shira'): An agent appointed specifically to purchase something for the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the debt payment scenario, what is the istihsan justification for allowing the wakil to recover from the principal when he pays from his own money?
A) The wakil is considered a donor and the principal must repay him.
B) Debt payment is analogous to purchase, so the same rule of price recovery applies.
C) The wakil always has the right to change the payment method at his discretion.
D) The principal's order is void if the wakil uses his own money.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an agent paying a debt from his own funds can recover the amount from the principal because istihsan analogizes debt payment to purchase, overriding the apparent analogy of donation.

intermediate

Dismissal of the Agent: Conditions and Knowledge
Explains dismissal of agent and knowledge condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a principal may unilaterally dismiss an agent and explain why dismissal requires the agent's knowledge in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Dismissal of an agent is effective only upon the agent's knowledge; prior actions remain valid to prevent harm.

This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on dismissing an agent. While the principal generally has the right to terminate the agency at will, this right is limited when a third party's right is attached. Additionally, the dismissal itself only takes effect after the agent is informed, protecting him from unknowingly acting and incurring liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its exception
The principal may dismiss the agent because the agency is his right. However, if a third party's right (like a plaintiff's right in litigation or a mortgagee's right) is attached to the agency, the principal cannot dismiss without that party's consent.
This exception prevents harm to the third party whose right depends on the agency.
2
Explore the examples
In litigation, if the defendant appoints an agent at the plaintiff's request, the plaintiff's right to a representative is attached; the defendant cannot dismiss without consent. In a mortgage, an agent appointed to sell collateral upon default has the mortgagee's right attached; the mortgagor cannot dismiss unilaterally.
These examples show when a third-party right is considered attached.
3
Analyse the knowledge requirement
The dismissal is not effective until the agent learns of it. This is to prevent harm: the agent might continue acting, paying from his own money or delivering goods, and then become liable or suffer loss.
Until the agent knows, his actions are valid and bind the principal.
4
Note the inter-madhhab agreement
While some early scholars said dismissal is immediate regardless of knowledge, the Hanafi position (shared by Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad in one narration) is that knowledge is required.
The practical difference: if the agent acts after dismissal but before knowledge, the transaction is valid in Hanafi law.

Chapter: Dismissal of the Agent – Translation: This chapter is about the dismissal of the agent.
The principal may dismiss the agent from the agency.
He said: The principal has the right to dismiss the agent from the agency because the agency is his right, so he has the right to nullify it, unless a right of another person is attached to it, such as if he was an agent for litigation at the request of the plaintiff, because that would involve nullifying another's right, and it becomes like the agency that is included in a mortgage contract.
Translation: The principal has the option to dismiss his agent from the agency because agency is the principal's right, so he has the right to nullify his right. However, if another person's right is attached to the agency, then the principal does not have the right to terminate the agency without that other person's consent. For example, if in the judge's court, at the request of the plaintiff, the defendant appointed an agent for litigation, then without the plaintiff's consent, the defendant is not authorized to dismiss that agent, because the plaintiff's right is attached to this agency: the plaintiff will bring the agent to the court, litigate with him, and establish his right. So if the defendant dismisses the agent, the plaintiff's right would be nullified, and nullifying another's right without consent is not permissible. Thus in this case, the defendant's dismissal of the agent without the plaintiff's consent is not valid. And this is like the agency that is included in a mortgage contract. For example, Rashid borrowed 1000 rupees from Shahid and mortgaged his garden to him, but this garden, with the consent of both mortgagor and mortgagee, was placed in the custody of a third trustworthy person, say Qasim, with the condition that, at the request of the mortgagee, the mortgagor appointed this trustworthy (Qasim) as an agent: if the money is not paid within two years, you will sell this garden and pay the mortgagee his money. Now this agency is included in the mortgage contract, and the mortgagee's right is attached to it. So if the mortgagor wants to dismiss this agent without the mortgagee's consent, this agent will not be dismissed, and the mortgagor has no right to dismiss his agent.

If the news of dismissal has not reached the agent, he remains on his agency and his actions are valid until he learns.
He said: Then if the dismissal has not reached him, he remains on his agency, and his actions are valid until he knows, because in the dismissal there is harm to him, either in terms of nullifying his authority, or in terms of rights reverting to him; he pays the price from the principal's wealth and delivers the sold item, so he becomes liable and suffers harm. The agent for marriage and others are equal due to the first reason. We have already mentioned the condition of number or integrity in the informant, so we do not repeat it.

Commentary: The scenario is that if the principal dismissed his agent and the agent was not informed, he is not dismissed; rather, he remains on his agency and his actions are valid. However, when he becomes aware of his dismissal, he ceases to be an agent, and after that his actions are not valid. This is the Hanafi school, and Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad also have a saying to this effect. As for Imam Shafi'i's well-known saying...
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage covers two interrelated rulings on the dismissal of an agent (wakil). First, the principal's general right to dismiss: since agency is the principal's right, he can nullify it at will. However, this right is curtailed when a third party's right becomes attached to the agency. Two examples illustrate this: (1) In litigation, if the defendant appoints an agent at the plaintiff's request, the plaintiff has a right to the agent's presence for the lawsuit; thus the defendant cannot unilaterally dismiss him without the plaintiff's consent. (2) In a mortgage, an agent appointed to sell the collateral upon default has the mortgagee's right attached; the mortgagor cannot dismiss him unilaterally. The analogy (qiyas) is drawn to the mortgage contract where the agency is embedded within it. Second, the ruling that dismissal only becomes effective when the agent knows of it. This is to prevent harm to the agent who might unknowingly act after dismissal; until he learns, his actions are valid and binding on the principal. The text notes consensus among the major schools on this point, citing a saying from Imam Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad that aligns with the Hanafi position. The authority weight is from the matn of Quduri and its commentary, belonging to the Zahir al-Riwayah tradition.

Key Terms
عزل ('azl): Dismissal of an agent by the principal, terminating the agency relationship.
حق الغير (haqq al-ghayr): A right of a third party that becomes attached to the agency, preventing unilateral dismissal.
وكيل بالخصومة (wakil bi al-khusumah): An agent appointed for litigation, specifically to represent a party in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the mortgage example, why can the mortgagor not dismiss the agent appointed to sell the mortgaged property without the mortgagee's consent?
A) Because the mortgagor has no right to dismiss any agent.
B) Because the mortgagee's right is attached to the agency, as it was included in the mortgage contract.
C) Because the agent must be paid before dismissal.
D) Because the mortgagor is not the principal in this case.

Key Takeaway
Dismissal of an agent in Hanafi law is effective only upon the agent's knowledge, and it is restricted when a third-party right is attached to the agency.

beginner

Principal's Right to Dismiss Agent and Exception
Explains the principal's right to dismiss and the exception for attached third party rights.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule of agency termination in Hanafi fiqh and identify the exception when a third party's right is attached.

Core Idea
An agent may be dismissed unless a third party's right is attached.

In Hanafi law, agency is a contract that the principal can terminate at will. However, this right is not absolute; it is restricted when another person's right becomes bound to the agency. This lesson examines the rule and its application through two key examples from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
From the text, note that the principal (muwakkil) has full authority to dismiss the agent (wakil) because agency is the principal's right, and every right-owner can terminate their own right.
2
Note the exception
If another person's right is attached to the agency, the principal cannot terminate without the consent of that third party.
This exception protects the third party's vested right.
3
Analyze the litigation example
When a defendant appoints an agent upon the plaintiff's request, the plaintiff's right to confront the agent in court is attached. Dismissing the agent without the plaintiff's consent would nullify the plaintiff's right.
The plaintiff's right is to establish his claim against the agent.
4
Analyze the pledge example
In a pledge (rahn), if the pledgor appoints an agent to sell the pledged property upon the pledgee's request, the pledgee's right to receive payment through the sale is attached. The pledgor cannot dismiss the agent without the pledgee's consent.
The agency is part of the pledge contract.
5
Understand the underlying principle
The principle is that rights cannot be nullified without the consent of the right-holder. Therefore, when a third party has a right attached to the agency, the principal's right to dismiss is suspended.

تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ موکل کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اپنے وکیل کو وکالت سے معزول کر دیے کیونکہ وکالت مؤکل کا حق ہے اور ہر صاحب حق کو اپنا حق ختم کرنے کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا موکل کو بھی اپنا حق وکالت ختم اور باطل کرنے کا پورا پورا اختیار ہو گا ہاں وکالت کے ساتھ اگر کسی دوسرے کا حق متعلق ہو تو موکل کو بغیر اس دوسرے آدم کی رضا مندی کے وکالت ختم کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا مثلاً قاضی کی عدالت میں مدعی کی درخواست پر مدعی علیہ نے خصومت کا وکیل دیا ہو تو مدعی کی رضامندی کے بغیر مدعی علیہ اس وکیل کو معزول کرنے کا مجاز نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ اس وکالت کے ساتھ مدعی کا حق متعلق ہے اس طور پر کہ مدعی مجلس قاضی میں وکیل کو حاضر کر کے اس سے مخاصمہ کرے گا اور اس پر حق ثابت کرے گا پس اگر مدعلی علیہ نے اس وکیل کو معزول کر دیا تو مدعی کا حق باطل ہو جائے گا حالانکہ بغیر صاحب حق کی رضامندی کے اس کے حق کو باطل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا اس صورت میں مدعی علیہ کا اپنے وکیل کو بغیر مدعی کی رضامندی کے معزول کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ وہ وکالت جس کو عقد رہین متضمن ہوتا ہے مثلاً راشد نے شاہد سے ایک ہزار روپیہ قرض لے کر اپنا باغ اس کے پاس رہن رکھ دیا مگر یہ باغ راہن اور مرتہن دونوں کے اتفاق سے ایک تیسرے عادل آدمی مثلاً قاسم کے پاس رکھا گیا اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ مرتہن کی درخواست پر راہن نے اس عادل (قاسم) آدمی کو وکیل کیا اگر دو سال کے اندر روپے ادا نہ ہوں تو تم اس باغ کو فروخت کر کے مرتہن کا روپیا ادا کر دینا پس یہ وکالت عقد رہن کے ضمن میں ہے اور اس سے مرتہن کا حق متعلق ہے اب اگر راہن بغیر مرتہن کی رضا مندی کے اس وکیل کو معزول کرنا چاہے تو یہ وکیل معزول نہ ہوگا اور راہن کو یہ اختیار نہ ہوگا کہ وہ اپنے وکیل کو معزول کرے۔
Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that the principal has the right to dismiss his agent from the agency because agency is the principal's right, and every owner of a right has the authority to terminate his own right. Therefore, the principal has full authority to end and nullify his right of agency. However, if another person's right is attached to the agency, then the principal does not have the authority to terminate the agency without the consent of that other person. For example, if the defendant has appointed an agent for litigation in the judge's court upon the plaintiff's request, then the defendant is not authorized to dismiss that agent without the plaintiff's consent, because the plaintiff's right is attached to this agency in the sense that the plaintiff will confront the agent in the judge's court and establish his right against him. If the defendant dismisses the agent, then the plaintiff's right would be nullified, whereas it is not permissible to nullify a person's right without his consent. Therefore, in this case, the defendant's dismissal of his agent without the plaintiff's consent is not valid. This is similar to an agency that is included in a contract of pledge, for example: Rashid borrowed one thousand rupees from Shahid and pledged his garden to him as collateral, but the garden was placed with a third trustworthy person, e.g., Qasim, by mutual agreement of the pledgor and pledgee, with the condition that upon the pledgee's request, the pledgor appointed that trustworthy person (Qasim) as an agent to sell the garden and pay the pledgee's money if the debt is not paid within two years. Now this agency is included in the pledge contract, and the pledgee's right is attached to it. If the pledgor wants to dismiss this agent without the pledgee's consent, then this agent will not be dismissed, and the pledgor does not have the authority to dismiss his agent.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This is a ruling passage from a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The commentator explains that the principal (muwakkil) has the inherent right to dismiss the agent (wakil) because agency is a right belonging to the principal. However, this right is restricted when a third party's right becomes attached to the agency. The commentator provides two examples: first, in litigation, if the defendant appoints an agent upon the plaintiff's request, the plaintiff's right to confront that agent is attached; dismissing the agent without the plaintiff's consent would nullify his right, which is impermissible. Second, in a pledge (rahn), if the pledgor appoints an agent to sell the pledged property upon the pledgee's request, the pledgee's right is attached to this agency. The pledgor cannot dismiss the agent without the pledgee's consent. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that rights are respected and cannot be invalidated without the right-holder's consent.

Key Terms
وکالت (wakālah): A contract of agency where the principal authorizes the agent to perform a legal act on his behalf.
معزول (ma'zūl): The state of being dismissed from agency; the agent who has been removed from his position.
عقد رہن (ʿaqd al-rahn): A contract of pledge where property is given as security for a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can a principal not dismiss his agent without another person's consent?
A) When the agent is a close relative
B) When a third party's right is attached to the agency
C) When the agent has not yet started acting
D) When the agency is for marriage

Key Takeaway
A principal may dismiss an agent freely unless another's right is tied to the agency.
