Effect of Dismissal Without Knowledge of the Agent and Conditions of the Informant
Ruling and proof that dismissal requires knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that dismissal of an agent is ineffective until knowledge, explain the two harms (discrediting authority and personal liability), and apply the condition of number or reliability for the informant.

Core Idea
A principal's dismissal binds the agent only when known; unknown dismissal keeps the agency valid.

The agent's authority is a trust that cannot be silently revoked. The Hanafi school insists that dismissal is a binding address (khitab mulzim) that requires the agent's knowledge. This lesson unpacks the proof from harm and the conditions for notifying the agent, distinguishing the Hanafi view from the Shafi'i analogy to divorce.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Recite the main rule: if dismissal does not reach the agent, he remains on his agency and his dispositions are valid until he knows.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the two harms in dismissal
The text gives two reasons: (1) discrediting the agent's authority, (2) making him personally liable for transactions after dismissal. Both constitute harm (ḍarar) which Shari'ah removes.
The first harm applies to all agents; the second applies only where rights revert to the agent (e.g., sale, purchase).
3
Analyze the opposing view and Hanafi response
The opposing school analogizes dismissal to divorce and manumission, which do not require notification. The Hanafi response distinguishes: dismissal is a khitab mulzim (binding address), while divorce is simply dropping a right.
A binding address requires the addressee's knowledge to be effective, as shown by the Quba incident and wine prohibition (Quran 5:93).
4
Note the conditions for the informant
Imam Abu Hanifa states that the person informing the agent of dismissal must be either a single reliable person (adil) or two persons if not reliable.
This ensures certainty in notification.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Consider: principal dismisses agent without telling him; agent sells goods. Under Hanafi, the sale is valid and principal must deliver the goods. Under Shafi'i, the agent may be personally liable.
Thamarah al-khilaf: who bears the risk?

کے لئے واقع ہوگا اور ثمن ادا کرنے کی صورت میں ثمن کا ضامن ہو گا اور مبیع سپرد کرنے کی صورت میں مبیع کا ضامن ہوگا اور اس ضمان کی وجہ سے وکیل ضرر میں مبتلا ہوگا بہر حال وکیل کو اطلاع دیئے بغیر اگر وکیل کے معزول ہونے کا اعتبار کیا جائے تو وکیل دو وجہوں سے ضرر میں مبتلا ہوگا اور شرعا ضرر کو دور کیا جاتا ہے لہذا وکیل کے مذکورہ ضرر کو دور کرنے کے لئے بغیر وکیل کو اطلاع دیئے اس کو معزول کرنا معتبر نہ ہو اور موکل کی طرف نہیں لوٹتے ، جیسے بیع ، شراء ، یعنی وکیل کے بغیر علم ، معزول نہ ہونے میں وجہ اول کی وجہ سے نکاح ، طلاق ، اور بیع وغیرہ کے تمام وکیل برابر ہیں یعنی تمام کا حکم یہ ہے کہ وکیل کو اطلاع دیئے بغیر اگر اس کو معزول کیا گیا تو وہ معزول نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر وکیل کو معزول کیا گیا اور اس کو علم نہیں ہوا تو اب جو شخص اس کو معزول ہونے کی خبر دے گا حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس کے لئے عدد یا عدالت شرط ہے یعنی خبر دینے والا اگر ایک ہو تو عادل ہو اور اگر عادل نہ ہو تو پھر دو شخصوں کا ہونا
He said: If the dismissal did not reach him (the agent), then he remains upon his agency and his disposition is valid until he knows, because in dismissal there is harm to him, either from the perspective of nullifying his authority or from the perspective of rights returning to him. So he pays the price from the principal's wealth and delivers the sold item, thus becoming liable and suffering harm. The agent in marriage and others are equal due to the first reason. We have already mentioned the condition of number or reliability in the informant, so we will not repeat it. Translation: Then if the news of dismissal did not reach the agent, he will remain upon his agency and his disposition will be valid until he knows, because in dismissing him there is harm to the agent: either because his authority has become invalid, or because rights revert to him. So the agent pays the price from the principal's wealth and delivers the sold item; thus he becomes liable and suffers harm. Due to the first reason, the agent in marriage and others are equal. We have mentioned the condition of number or reliability in the informant, so we will not repeat it. Explanation: The issue is that if the principal dismisses his agent and the agent is not informed, then he is not dismissed; rather he remains on his agency and his disposition is valid. However, when he learns of his dismissal, he will no longer be an agent and after that his disposition is not valid. This is the madhhab of the Hanafis, and Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad also have one narration with this position. The evidence for the opposing view (that dismissal is effective without knowledge) is that implementing the agency is the principal's right, and by dismissing the agent he drops his own right, and a person is independent in dropping his own right; he does not need to inform the person from whom the right is dropped, just as a husband in giving divorce and a master in freeing a slave do not need to inform the wife or slave. Our response to this is that dismissal is a binding address (khitab mulzim) for the agent, meaning it is an address that imposes an obligation on the agent, in the sense that the principal restrains the agent from actions. The ruling of an address is only established for the addressee when he has knowledge of it. Before knowledge, the ruling of the address is not established for the addressee, as with the people of Quba: after the change of qibla, they continued praying towards Bayt al-Maqdis, but the Prophet ﷺ declared all their prayers valid until they learned of the change. Similarly, after the prohibition of wine, many Companions continued drinking wine due to not knowing, and no blame was placed on them. Indeed, Allah says: 'There is no sin upon those who believe and do righteous deeds concerning what they have eaten' (5:93). The reason is that action is intended from an address, and action without knowledge is not possible. Therefore, no person is obligated to act without knowledge and notification. The author of al-Hidayah, presenting the proof for his madhhab, said: In dismissing the agent, there is harm to the agent for two reasons: first, when the principal dismisses the agent, he nullifies his authority and thus discredits him; so the principal discredits the agent in his claim, saying that due to his dismissal the agent's authority has become invalid. Discrediting a person in his statement is clear harm. Thus, dismissing the agent without notification causes harm to the agent. Second, rights from the contract revert to the agent. For example, if the agent is an agent for purchase, he pays the price from the principal's wealth; if he is an agent for sale, he delivers the sold item. If the agent is dismissed and he is not aware of his dismissal, and the dismissal is considered effective, then any disposition after dismissal would be for the agent himself, and he would be liable for the price or the sold item, causing him harm due to this guarantee. In any case, if the dismissal is considered effective without informing the agent, the agent suffers harm for two reasons, and harm is removed by Shari'ah. Therefore, to remove the mentioned harm, dismissal without informing the agent is not effective. The author of al-Hidayah said: Among the two mentioned reasons, the first reason is general, applying to all dispositions such as marriage, divorce, sale, purchase, etc. The second reason is specific to those dispositions where rights revert to the agent and not to the principal, such as sale and purchase. So in the matter of the agent not being dismissed without knowledge, due to the first reason, all agents in marriage, divorce, sale, etc. are equal; the ruling for all is that if the agent is dismissed without information, he is not dismissed. The author of al-Hidayah said: If the agent is dismissed and he does not know, then the person who informs him of his dismissal, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, requires number or reliability: i.e., the informant must be either a single reliable person, or if not reliable, then two persons.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses a key question: Is the dismissal of an agent effective immediately upon the principal's decision, or only when the agent learns of it? The Hanafi ruling is clear: dismissal is ineffective until the agent receives knowledge of it. The passage provides the proof: the matn states that the agent remains on his agency and his actions are valid until he knows. The commentator elaborates with two arguments: first, that dismissal without knowledge harms the agent by discrediting his authority; second, it causes harm because after dismissal, any transactions he performs become his personal liability, not the principal's. The passage also addresses the opposing view attributed to al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad (in one narration) that dismissal is effective immediately. Their analogy to divorce and manumission is refuted by distinguishing dismissal as a khitab mulzim (binding address) that requires knowledge, similar to the change of qibla and prohibition of wine. The text also notes the condition for the informant: Imam Abu Hanifa requires either reliability (adala) if the informant is one person, or two persons if the informant is not reliable, for the dismissal to be effective after notification.

Key Terms
عزل (ʿazl): Dismissal of the agent by the principal, which is a legal act that removes the agent's authority.
خطاب ملزم (khiṭāb mulzim): A binding address that imposes an obligation on the addressee; here, the principal's dismissal is such an address that requires the agent to stop acting.
عدد یا عدالت (ʿadad aw ʿadālah): Condition for the informant: either two persons or one reliable person to notify the agent of his dismissal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what are the conditions for the person who informs the agent of his dismissal?
A) The informant must be a male
B) The informant must be either reliable if alone, or two persons if not reliable
C) The informant must be a relative of the agent
D) The informant must be the principal himself

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a principal's dismissal of an agent is ineffective until the agent is notified; otherwise, the agent's subsequent actions remain valid and binding on the principal.

Why an Agent Must Be Informed of Dismissal: The Hanafi Position
Evidence and counter-evidence on whether agent's dismissal requires knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires the agent's knowledge for dismissal and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) if the agent acts without knowledge.

Core Idea
Dismissal without knowledge harms the agent and fails as a binding address.

This lesson examines a key dispute in Hanafi agency law: does dismissing an agent require informing him? The opposing view analogizes dismissal to divorce and manumission, which need no notification. The Hanafi response, grounded in the concept of khatab mulzim (binding address) and harm prevention, explains why knowledge is essential. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi principles to real-world agency contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Opponent's Analogy
First, note the opponent's argument: the principal is independent in dropping his right to agency, just as a husband drops the marriage bond without telling his wife. This analogy claims that knowledge is irrelevant.
The opposing view is likely from non-Hanafi schools, but the passage does not name them specifically.
2
Analyze the Hanafi Refutation: Binding Address
The Hanafis classify dismissal as a khatab mulzim – an address that imposes a legal burden on the agent. For such an address to take effect, the addressee must be aware of it. This is supported by Quranic and Sunnah examples: the people of Quba and the Companions who drank wine before prohibition reached them were not held accountable.
The key principle: 'The ruling of an address is only established for the addressee when he has knowledge of it.'
3
Understand the Two Harms Preventing Dismissal Without Knowledge
The author of Al-Hidayah lists two harms: (1) Takdhib – contradicting the agent's claim to authority, which is a form of harm; (2) Liability – if the agent acts without knowing, he becomes personally liable for transactions (e.g., paying price or handing over goods), as rights revert to him. These harms are removed by Shari'ah, so the dismissal is invalid without notification.
The first harm applies universally; the second only when rights revert to the agent (e.g., sale, purchase).
4
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
If the agent is dismissed without knowledge and continues to act, his transactions are valid and binding on the principal until the agent learns of the dismissal. This is the operative ruling (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.
The effect of notification: once informed, the agent's authority ceases retroactively? Actually, it ceases from the moment he knows, not from the principal's declaration.
5
Note the Conditions for Informing
The passage ends with a detail from Imam Abu Hanifa: the person informing the agent must be either one upright (adil) witness or two persons if not upright. This echoes the rules of testimony in legal proceedings.
This condition ensures the agent receives reliable information, preventing further disputes.

یا عدالت شرط ہے یعنی خبر دینے والا اگر ایک ہو تو عادل ہو اور اگر عادل نہ ہو تو پھر دو شخصوں کا ہونا ضروری ہے تفصیل ادب القاضی میں گزر چکی ہے اس کے اعادہ کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
The proof is that the enforcement of agency is the right of the principal, and by dismissing the agent the principal drops his right, and a person is independent in dropping his right and does not need to inform the one from whom the right is dropped, like a husband in divorcing his wife and a master in freeing his slave does not need to inform the wife and slave. Our response to this is that dismissal is a binding address (khatab mulzim) for the agent, i.e., dismissal is an address that imposes a burden on the agent in that the principal restrains the agent from transactions, and the ruling of an address is only established for the addressee when he has knowledge of it, and before knowledge the ruling of the address is not established for the addressee, like the people of Quba continued praying towards Bayt al-Maqdis after the change of qibla, but the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) declared all their prayers valid until they knew of the change. Similarly, after the prohibition of drinking wine, many Companions continued drinking due to not knowing, and they were not held accountable. Allah Almighty says: 'There is no sin upon those who have believed and done righteous deeds concerning what they have eaten.' And the reason is that the address aims at action, and action is not possible without knowledge; therefore, no person is obligated to act without knowledge and information. The author of al-Hidayah, while adducing evidence for his school, said that in dismissing the agent there are two aspects causing harm to the agent: first, when the principal dismisses the agent, he nullifies his authority and contradicts him, so it is as if the principal contradicts the agent in his claim and says that due to his dismissal, the agent's authority has become void, and contradicting a person in his statement is a clear harm to him. Thus it is established that dismissing the agent without informing him causes harm to the agent. The second reason is that the rights of the contract revert to the agent. For example, if the agent is an agent for purchase, he pays the price from the principal's property; if the agent is an agent for sale, he hands over the sold item. Now, if the agent is dismissed and he is not aware of his dismissal, and the dismissal is considered effective, then any transaction he does after the dismissal will be for himself, and in case of paying the price, he will be liable for the price, and in case of handing over the sold item, he will be liable for the item, and due to this liability, the agent will suffer harm. In any case, if the agent's dismissal is considered effective without informing him, the agent will suffer harm in two ways, and harm is removed by Shari'ah. Therefore, to remove the aforementioned harm from the agent, dismissing him without informing him will not be considered effective. The author of al-Hidayah said that among the two mentioned aspects, the first is general, covering all transactions like marriage, divorce, sale, purchase, etc., and the second aspect is specific to transactions where rights revert to the agent and not to the principal, like sale and purchase. That is, regarding the non-effectiveness of dismissal without the agent's knowledge, based on the first reason, all agents in marriage, divorce, sale, etc., are equal, meaning the ruling for all is that if the agent is dismissed without being informed, he is not dismissed. The author of al-Hidayah said that if the agent is dismissed and he does not know, then the person who informs him of his dismissal must, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, satisfy a condition of number or uprightness: if the informant is one person, he must be upright (adil); if not upright, then two persons are necessary. The details have passed in Adab al-Qadi and there is no need to repeat them.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the effectiveness of dismissing an agent without informing him. The author presents the opponent's proof: the principal has the right to drop his right to agency, just as a husband can divorce without informing his wife. The Hanafi response is that dismissal is a binding address (khatab mulzim) that imposes harm on the agent. The ruling of an address only applies when the addressee knows it. Examples: the people of Quba and the Companions who drank wine before the prohibition reached them. The author of al-Hidayah provides two reasons why informing is necessary: (1) to avoid contradicting the agent's claim (takdhib), which is a clear harm; (2) because rights of the contract revert to the agent, so without knowledge, the agent may act and become liable for damages. The first reason applies to all types of agency, the second only to those where rights revert to the agent. Finally, the conditions for informing are given: according to Abu Hanifa, the informant must be either one adil person or two if not adil.

Key Terms
عزل (azl): Dismissal of an agent by the principal, removing his authority to act.
خطاب ملزم (khatab mulzim): An address that imposes a legal obligation or burden on the addressee.
تکذیب (takdhib): Contradicting someone's claim, which is considered a form of harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, why is dismissing an agent without informing him not effective?
A) Because the agent has a binding contract that cannot be terminated.
B) Because dismissal is a binding address that requires the agent's knowledge to take effect, and to avoid harm to the agent.
C) Because the principal must always inform the agent to maintain good relations.
D) Because the agency contract is a religious contract that cannot be revoked.

Key Takeaway
Dismissal of an agent is not effective without the agent's knowledge because it is a binding address that would cause harm.

Events That Invalidate Agency: Death, Insanity, Apostasy
Ruling on what nullifies a contract of agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three events that invalidate a contract of agency according to the Hanafi school and explain the intra-madhhab differences regarding the definition of continuous insanity and the effect of apostasy.

Core Idea
Agency is invalidated by death, continuous insanity, and apostasy with joining Dar al-Harb—but the definition of continuous insanity splits Abu Yusuf from Muhammad.

The contract of agency (wakalah) is a non-binding disposition that depends on the principal's capacity. When the principal loses capacity through death, continuous insanity, or apostasy combined with joining enemy territory, the agency is invalidated. However, the Hanafi school has internal differences on the precise limits of continuous insanity and on whether apostasy alone suspends or invalidates the contract. This lesson unpacks these rulings and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three invalidating events
From the passage, list the three events that invalidate agency: death, continuous insanity (junun mutabbah), and apostasy followed by joining Dar al-Harb.
Note that temporary insanity like fainting does not invalidate.
2
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
Agency is ghayr lazim (non-binding), so its continuation requires the principal's ongoing capacity. These events nullify that capacity, so the agency ends.
This is a qiyas argument: the continuation is like the initiation—both require the principal's command.
3
Analyze the intra-madhhab disagreement on continuous insanity
Abu Yusuf defines continuous insanity as one month (by analogy with fasting), also a narration of more than a day and night (by analogy with prayers). Muhammad defines it as one full year (by analogy with all acts of worship).
The difference affects when agency is actually invalidated.
4
Analyze the intra-madhhab disagreement on apostasy
Abu Hanifa holds that the apostate's dispositions are suspended (mawquf), so agency is suspended until he returns to Islam or dies/joins Dar al-Harb. The Sahibayn hold that his dispositions are effective, so agency remains valid until death or a ruling of joining Dar al-Harb.
The special case of a female principal: her apostasy does not affect her contracts, so agency continues until death or joining Dar al-Harb.
5
Apply the rulings to practical scenarios
Given a scenario with a specific duration of insanity or apostasy status, determine whether agency is valid, suspended, or invalidated based on each imam's view.
Consider the mufta bihi position (often Abu Yusuf's month).

قال ويبطل الوكالة بموت المؤكل وجنونه جنونا مطبقاً ولحانه بدار الحرب مرتدا لان التوكيل تصرف غير لازم فيكون لدوامه حكم ابتدائه فلابد من قيام الامر وقد بطل بهذه العوارض وشرط ان يكون الجنون مطبة لان قليله بمنزله الاغماء وحد المطبق شهر عند ابي يوسف اعتبارا بما تسقط به الصوم وعنه أكثر من يوم وليلة لانه يسقط به الصلواة الخمس فصار كالميت وقال محمد حول كامل لانه يسقط به جميع العبادات فقدر به احتياطا قالوا الحكم المذكور فى اللحاق قول أبي حنيفة لأن تصرفات المرتد موقوفة عنده فكذا وكالته فان أسلم نفذ وان قتل ولحق بدار الحرب بطلت الوكالة فاما عندهما تصرفاته نافذة فلا يبطل وكالته الا ان يموت أو يقتل على ردته او يحكم بلحاقه وقد مر في السير وان كان المؤكل امراة فارتدت فالوكيل على وكالته حتى تموت او تلحق بدار الحرب لأن ردتها لا تؤثر في عقودها على ما عرف

Agency becomes invalid due to the death of the principal, his continuous insanity, and his joining Dar al-Harb as an apostate. He said: Agency is invalidated by the death of the principal, by his insanity that is continuous (mutabbah), and by his joining the abode of war as an apostate, because agency is a non-binding (ghayr lazim) disposition; thus its continuation has the ruling of its initiation, so the existence of the command (of the principal) is necessary, and it has been nullified by these occurrences. It is stipulated that the insanity be continuous because a little insanity is like fainting. The limit of continuous insanity according to Abu Yusuf is one month, by analogy with that which invalidates fasting. According to another narration from him, it is more than a day and night because it invalidates the five prayers, so he becomes like a dead person. According to Muhammad, it is one full year because it invalidates all acts of worship, so it is estimated by that as a precaution. They said: The mentioned ruling regarding joining (Dar al-Harb) is the saying of Abu Hanifa because the dispositions of an apostate are suspended (mawquf) according to him, and so is his agency. If he becomes Muslim, it becomes effective; if he is killed or joins Dar al-Harb, the agency is invalidated. As for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), his dispositions are effective, so his agency is not invalidated unless he dies, is killed upon his apostasy, or a ruling is made of his joining Dar al-Harb. This has passed in al-Siyar. If the principal is a woman and she apostatizes, the agent remains upon his agency until she dies or joins Dar al-Harb, because her apostasy does not affect her contracts, as is known. Translation: Agency becomes invalid due to the death of the principal, his continuous insanity, and his becoming an apostate and joining Dar al-Harb, because agency is a non-binding disposition, so its continuation has the ruling of its initiation, and the existence of the principal's command is necessary, and it has been nullified by these occurrences. It is stipulated that insanity be continuous because a little insanity is like fainting. The limit of continuous insanity according to Imam Abu Yusuf is one month, by analogy with that which invalidates fasting. According to another narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, it is more than a day and night because it invalidates the five prayers, so he becomes like a dead person. Imam Muhammad said that continuous insanity is one full year because it invalidates all acts of worship, so it is estimated by that as a precaution. The scholars said that the mentioned ruling regarding joining Dar al-Harb is the saying of Abu Hanifa because according to him, the dispositions of an apostate are suspended, so similarly his agency is suspended. So if he becomes Muslim, it becomes effective; if he is killed or joins Dar al-Harb, the agency is invalidated. As for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the dispositions of an apostate are effective, so his agency is not invalidated unless he dies, is killed upon his apostasy, or a ruling is made of his joining Dar al-Harb. This difference has been mentioned in Kitab al-Siyar. If the principal is a woman and she apostatizes, the agent remains upon his agency until she dies or joins Dar al-Harb, because a woman's apostasy does not affect her contracts, as is known. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri says that agency becomes invalid in several cases.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that agency is invalidated by three events: death of the principal, continuous insanity (junun mutabbah), and apostasy followed by joining Dar al-Harb. The reasoning is that agency is a non-binding (ghayr lazim) contract, so its continuation depends on the principal's capacity, and these events nullify that. The definition of continuous insanity is disputed within the Hanafi school: Abu Yusuf says one month (by analogy with fasting), also a narration of more than a day and night (by analogy with prayers); Muhammad says one full year (by analogy with all acts of worship). For apostasy, Abu Hanifa's view is that the apostate's actions are suspended, so agency becomes suspended too; if he returns to Islam, it resumes; if he dies or joins Dar al-Harb, it is void. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the apostate's actions are effective, so agency remains valid until death or ruling of joining Dar al-Harb. A special case: if the principal is a woman and she apostatizes, agency remains valid because her apostasy does not affect her contracts (e.g., sale, purchase). This ruling is taken from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.

Key Terms
جنون مطبق (junun mutabbah): Continuous insanity that completely incapacitates the principal, as opposed to temporary insanity or fainting.
لحاق بدار الحرب (lihaq bil dār al-ḥarb): Joining the territory of non-Muslims as an apostate, which is considered a legal death for certain purposes.
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who renounces Islam. His dispositions are suspended according to Abu Hanifa, but effective according to the Sahibayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the duration of continuous insanity (junun mutabbah) that invalidates agency according to Imam Abu Yusuf?
A) One day and night
B) One month
C) One year
D) Indefinite

Key Takeaway
Agency is invalidated by death, continuous insanity, and apostasy joined with entering Dar al-Harb, but the definition of 'continuous' and the effect of apostasy alone are disputed within the Hanafi school.

intermediate
10 min
Invalidation of Agency by Death, Insanity, and Apostasy
Explains three causes that invalidate agency and intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three causes that invalidate agency (wakalah) and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreements regarding the duration of continuous insanity and the effect of apostasy.

Core Idea
Agency is invalidated by death, continuous insanity, and apostasy with joining Dar al-Harb; duration of insanity and status of apostate's acts are disputed among Hanafi imams.

You already know that agency (wakalah) is a non-binding contract. But when does it end? The classical Hanafi texts identify three clear events that automatically invalidate the agency: the principal's death, continuous insanity, and apostasy followed by joining enemy territory. However, the imams differed on the exact threshold for 'continuous' insanity and whether an apostate's agency remains effective. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah walks through these rulings and the proofs behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three invalidation events
Locate the three events stated at the beginning: death, continuous insanity (junoon mutbiq), and apostasy with joining Dar al-Harb. Note that apostasy alone is not enough; the principal must have physically joined the enemy territory.
The passage adds later that for a female apostate, the agency remains valid until death or joining Dar al-Harb.
2
Understand the underlying proof
The proof (dalil) is that agency is a non-binding transaction (tasarruf ghayr lazim). Its continuation requires the same conditions as its initiation—namely, the principal's command (amr). When the principal dies, becomes continuously insane, or apostatizes and leaves, the command is nullified, so the agency ends.
This is a rational (aqli) proof based on the nature of the contract.
3
Analyze the dispute on the duration of continuous insanity
Three views: Abu Yusuf (1 month, analogy to waiving fast), another narration from Abu Yusuf (more than a day and a night, analogy to waiving prayers), Muhammad (1 year, analogy to waiving all worship). Note that the passage does not explicitly prefer one, but later Hanafi practice tends toward the shorter duration.
The dispute is about the minimum length of insanity that removes legal capacity.
4
Analyze the dispute on apostasy and agency
Abu Hanifa holds that an apostate's transactions are suspended (mawquf) until he returns to Islam or dies/joins Dar al-Harb. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the apostate's transactions are effective (nafidh) during apostasy, so the agency remains valid unless the apostate actually dies or is executed.
The passage mentions that the ruling for a female apostate is milder: her agency remains valid even according to Abu Hanifa because her contracts are unaffected.
5
Determine the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
For insanity: if the principal becomes insane for less than a day, agency remains valid. If between a day and a month, a judge following Abu Yusuf's second narration would invalidate; following Muhammad, it would take a year. For apostasy: under Abu Hanifa, any transaction during apostasy is void if the principal dies; under Sahibayn, the agent can act until the principal's death.
These differences affect when an agent should stop acting to avoid liability.

حضرت امام ابو یوسف سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ جنون مطبق کی حد ایک دن رات ہے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ جنون مطبق کی حد ایک دن رات سے زائد ہے یعنی اگر مؤکل ایک دن رات سے زیادہ جنون میں مبتلا رہا تو اس کی وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے سر مسلسل ایک دن رات مجنون رہنے کی صورت میں پانچوں نمازیں اس کے ذمہ ساقط ہو جاتی ہیں لہذا اس مدت میں مجنون رہنے والا شخص میت کے مانند ہو گیا ہے اور جب یہ مجنون میت کے مانند ہو گیا تو وکالت کا اہل بھی نہ رہے گا اور جب وکالت کا اہل نہ رہا تو اس کی وکالت بھی باطل ہو جائے گی۔ اما محمد نے فرمایا کہ جنون مطبق کی حد ایک سال کی مدت ہے کیونکہ پورے ایک سال مجنون رہنے والے آدمی سے تمام عبادات نماز ، روزہ ، زکوۃ ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ لہذا جنون مطبق کی حد احتیاطاً ایک سال کی مدت کے ساتھ مقدر کی گئی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ مشائخ احناف نے فرمایا ہے کہ مرتد کے دارالحرب میں چلے جانے کا جو حکم متن میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے وہ امام ابوحنیفہ کا قول ہے کیونکہ حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک مرتد کے تمام تصرفات موقوف رہتے ہیں لہذا اس کی وکالت بھی موقوف رہے گی۔ موقوف رہنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مرتد اگر مسلمان ہو گیا تو اس کا وہ تصرف تو کیل جو اس نے ردت کے زمانہ میں کیا تھا نا فذ ہو جائے گا اور اگر مرتد قتل کر دیا گیا یا دار الحرب میں چلا گیا تو اس کی وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ مرتد کے تمام تصرفات نافذ ہیں۔ لہذا مرتد کی وکالت باطل نہ ہوگی ۔ ہاں اگر مرتد مر گیا یا اس کو ردت پر قتل کر دیا گیا تو بلاشبہ اس کی وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ اس
Book of Agency. It is necessary, its detail has passed in Adab al-Qadi; there is no need to repeat it. Agency becomes invalid by the death of the principal, his insanity (continuous insanity), and his apostasy joining Dar al-Harb. He said: Agency is invalidated by death of the principal, his continuous insanity, and his joining Dar al-Harb as an apostate, because agency is a non-binding transaction. Thus its continuance has the ruling of its initiation, so the command (of the principal) must exist, and it has been nullified by these impediments. The condition is that the insanity be continuous, because a little insanity is like fainting. The limit of continuous insanity according to Abu Yusuf is one month, analogy to what causes fasting to be waived. And from him (another narration): more than a day and a night, because it causes the five prayers to be waived, so he becomes like a corpse. Muhammad said: a complete year, because it causes all acts of worship to be waived, so it was estimated cautiously. They said: The mentioned ruling regarding joining (Dar al-Harb) is the statement of Abu Hanifa, because according to him the transactions of an apostate are suspended, and so is his agency. If he becomes Muslim, it is effective; if he is killed or joins Dar al-Harb, the agency is invalidated. As for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), his transactions are effective, so his agency is not invalidated unless he dies or is killed upon his apostasy or is judged to have joined Dar al-Harb, and this has passed in al-Siyar. If the principal is a woman and she apostatizes, the agent remains on his agency until she dies or joins Dar al-Harb, because her apostasy does not affect her contracts, as is known. Commentary: Al-Quduri says that agency becomes invalid in several cases: one, death occurs; two, the principal becomes continuously insane day and night; three, the principal apostatizes and resides in Dar al-Harb. The proof is that agency is a non-binding transaction, because binding is that whose existence depends on the consent of both parties, whereas in agency it is not so; rather both the principal and agent have the option to rescind. Thus the agent can prevent himself, and the principal can forbid the agent. In any case, agency is a non-binding transaction, and for its continuance and duration, all the conditions required for its initiation are necessary. For the initiation of agency, the command of the principal is necessary, so for its duration the continuous existence of the command is also necessary. Since due to the mentioned impediments (death, continuous insanity, apostasy) the principal's command becomes invalid, therefore the agency also becomes invalid. The author of al-Hidayah said: Al-Quduri restricted insanity to continuous insanity, i.e., madness that is present day and night, because a little madness that lasts for a short while and ends is of the rank of fainting, and the principal remains (capable) due to that, so the agency does not become invalid. The author of al-Hidayah said: The limit of continuous insanity according to Imam Abu Yusuf is one month, and he analogized it to this: if a person was insane for the month of Ramadan, the fast of Ramadan is waived from him, because when he is not qualified for divine address, he is also not qualified for worldly transactions. When his qualification ceases, his agency becomes invalid. From Imam Abu Yusuf is one narration that the limit of continuous insanity is a day and a night. Another narration is that it is more than a day and a night: if the principal suffers from madness for more than a day and a night, his agency becomes invalid. The reason is that when someone is continuously insane for a day and a night, the five prayers are waived from him, so such a person becomes like a corpse, and when he becomes like a corpse, he is no longer qualified for agency, so his agency becomes invalid. Muhammad said: The limit of continuous insanity is a period of one year, because from a person who is insane for a complete year, all acts of worship—prayer, fasting, zakat—are waived. Therefore, the limit of continuous insanity was conservatively set at a period of one year. The author of al-Hidayah said: The mashayikh of the Hanafis said that the ruling regarding the apostate joining Dar al-Harb mentioned in the text is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa, because according to Imam Sahib, all transactions of an apostate are suspended, so his agency is also suspended. The meaning of suspended is that if the apostate becomes Muslim, his transaction of agency made during apostasy becomes effective; if the apostate is killed or joins Dar al-Harb, his agency becomes invalid. The Sahibayn said: All transactions of an apostate are effective. Therefore the apostate's agency does not become invalid, unless the apostate dies or is killed upon apostasy, then undoubtedly his agency becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage from 'Ashraf al-Hidayah' is a detailed commentary on the rulings of invalidation of agency (wakalah). The author first states the three causes that invalidate agency: death of the principal, continuous insanity (junoonal-mutbiq), and apostasy with joining Dar al-Harb. The proof is that agency is a non-binding (ghayr lazim) contract; its continuation has the same requirements as its initiation. Since these three events destroy the legal capacity (ahliyyah) or the command (amr) of the principal, the agency ends. The passage then focuses on two intra-Hanafi disputes: (1) the definition and duration of continuous insanity, and (2) the effect of apostasy on agency.

Regarding insanity: The text distinguishes between minor (qalil) and continuous (mutbiq) insanity. Minor insanity is like fainting—it does not invalidate agency. For continuous insanity, there are three positions: (a) Abu Yusuf's well-known view: one month, based on analogy to the waiving of the Ramadan fast. (b) Another narration from Abu Yusuf: more than a day and a night, based on the waiving of the five daily prayers. (c) Muhammad al-Shaybani: a full year, because all acts of worship (prayer, fasting, zakat) are waived, so the limit is set conservatively.

Regarding apostasy: Abu Hanifa's position is that all transactions of an apostate, including agency, are suspended (mawquf). If the apostate returns to Islam, the transaction becomes effective; if he is killed or joins Dar al-Harb, it is invalidated. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the apostate's transactions are effective (nafidhah) during apostasy, so the agency remains valid unless the apostate dies or is executed. For a female apostate, her agency remains valid until she dies or joins Dar al-Harb, because a woman's apostasy does not affect her contracts (as her contract of marriage, for example, remains valid).

This passage is an expansion probe, explaining the matn of al-Quduri with additional reasoning and dispute resolution from al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
الوكالة (al-wakalah): A contract where one person (principal) appoints another (agent) to act on his behalf in a permissible matter.
تصرف غير لازم (tasarruf ghayr lazim): A transaction that is not binding; either party can unilaterally rescind it.
جنون مطبق (junoon mutbiq): Continuous insanity that lasts for a prolonged period, causing loss of legal capacity.
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who abandons Islam and joins enemy territory (Dar al-Harb).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the limit of continuous insanity according to Imam Muhammad?
A) One day and one night
B) One month
C) One year
D) More than a day and a night

Key Takeaway
Agency is invalidated by the principal's death, continuous insanity (duration disputed), and apostasy with joining Dar al-Harb; the Hanafi imams differ on thresholds but all agree on the underlying principle that agency requires the principal's legal capacity.

Nullification of Agency: Death, Continuous Madness, and Apostasy
Explains grounds for termination of agency due to loss of principal's capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the events that nullify a wakalah contract and explain the intra-Hanafi differences regarding the definition of continuous madness and the effect of apostasy.

Core Idea
Wakalah terminates when the principal loses capacity; disputes remain on madness duration and apostasy effect.

A wakalah contract is non-binding (ghayr lazim), meaning it depends on the continuous existence of the principal's command. Therefore, any event that destroys the principal's legal capacity to command also terminates the agency. This lesson explores three such events—death, continuous madness, and apostasy—and the nuanced differences within the Hanafi school on their precise definitions and effects.

Guided Path
1
Understand the nature of wakalah
Recognise that wakalah is a non-binding contract. Both parties have the right to revoke. The continuance of the contract requires the ongoing existence of the principal's command (amr).
This principle underpins why loss of capacity nullifies the contract.
2
Identify the capacity-nullifying events
Death, continuous madness (junun mutbiq), and apostasy (riddah) each destroy the principal's capacity to command, thus voiding wakalah. Note that the effect of apostasy is disputed.
Intermittent madness or temporary unconsciousness does not nullify wakalah.
3
Analyse the definition of junun mutbiq
The passage defines junun mutbiq as continuous, day-and-night madness. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the minimum duration: Abu Yusuf gives two opinions (one month or one day-night), while Muhammad holds it to be one year. Their reasoning is based on qiyas with dropped acts of worship.
The difference affects when wakalah becomes void: immediately upon reaching the threshold.
4
Examine the effect of apostasy
According to Abu Hanifa, the apostate's transactions are suspended (mawquf): if he returns to Islam, the wakalah becomes effective; if he dies or goes to Dar al-Harb, it becomes void. Sahibayn hold that the apostate's transactions are effective (nafidh) during apostasy, so wakalah remains valid until death or execution.
The thamarah al-khilaf: does wakalah revive upon return to Islam? Abu Hanifa: yes; Sahibayn: it never ceased, so it continues.
5
Note the exception for female apostates
By consensus, a female principal's apostasy does not nullify wakalah because a female apostate is not executed; her capacity is unaffected. However, if she dies or goes to Dar al-Harb, then wakalah becomes void.
This highlights the link between execution and loss of capacity.

Thirdly, that the principal apostatizes and goes to Dar al-Harb to reside. The proof is that wakalah is a non-binding contract because bindingness is the name for something whose existence depends on the mutual consent of both parties, whereas in wakalah it is not so; rather both the principal and agent have the option to revoke the agency. Thus the agent may withdraw himself from the agency, and the principal may prevent the agent. In any case, wakalah is a non-binding transaction, and for the continuance of a non-binding transaction, all those conditions are necessary which are necessary for its inception. For the inception of wakalah, the command of the principal is necessary, so for its continuance the existence of the principal's command at all times is necessary. Since the mentioned occurrences (death, continuous madness, and apostasy) invalidate the principal's command, therefore wakalah also becomes void. The author of al-Hidayah said that the author of al-Quduri restricted madness with the condition of being continuous, meaning such madness that persists day and night. Because slight madness that lasts for a short time and then ends is at the level of fainting and unconsciousness, and due to the principal's capacity, the wakalah does not become void. The author of al-Hidayah said that the limit of continuous madness according to Imam Abu Yusuf is one month, and he analogized it to the case that if a person remains insane for the month of Ramadan, the fast of Ramadan is dropped from his liability, because when he is not capable of divine worship, he will also not be capable of worldly transactions, and when his capacity ends, the wakalah becomes void. There is a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf that the limit of continuous madness is one day and night; another narration says it is more than one day and night, i.e., if the principal remains insane for more than a day and night, his wakalah becomes void, and the reason is that if someone remains continuously insane for a day and night, the five prayers are dropped from his liability, so the person who remains insane for this period has become like a corpse, and when he becomes like a corpse, he is no longer capable of wakalah, and when he is no longer capable, his wakalah becomes void. Imam Muhammad said that the limit of continuous madness is one year, because from a person who remains insane for a full year, all acts of worship (prayer, fasting, zakat) are dropped. Therefore, the limit of continuous madness has been determined cautiously as one year. The author of al-Hidayah said that the Hanafi scholars stated that the ruling mentioned in the text about the apostate going to Dar al-Harb is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa, because according to Imam Sahib, all transactions of an apostate are suspended; therefore his wakalah is also suspended. The meaning of suspension is that if the apostate becomes Muslim, that transaction of wakalah which he did during apostasy becomes effective; and if the apostate is killed or goes to Dar al-Harb, his wakalah becomes void. The two companions said that all transactions of an apostate are effective; therefore his wakalah does not become void. However, if the apostate dies or is killed for apostasy, then undoubtedly his wakalah becomes void. The detail of this difference has passed in the book of Siyar. If the principal is a woman and she apostatizes, then by consensus the agent remains on his agency, i.e., the wakalah does not become void due to the apostasy of the female principal. However, if the woman dies or goes to Dar al-Harb and joins them, then her wakalah undoubtedly becomes void. The reason is that a woman is not killed due to apostasy, so her apostasy does not affect her contracts; therefore her wakalah does not become void due to her apostasy. Rather, her wakalah remains as before, but if she dies, it becomes void due to death, and if she goes to Dar al-Harb, it becomes void due to joining the people of Dar al-Harb.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage discusses the factors that terminate an agency contract (wakalah) due to loss of the principal's legal capacity. The author first establishes the legal nature of wakalah: it is a non-binding (ghayr lazim) contract, meaning either party may revoke it at will. This non-bindingness implies that the continuance of the contract depends on the ongoing existence of the principal's command (amr). Therefore, any event that destroys the principal's capacity to command also terminates the wakalah. Three such events are identified: death, continuous madness (junun mutbiq), and apostasy (riddah) combined with going to Dar al-Harb. The author then discusses the definition of continuous madness, noting that al-Quduri restricted it to madness that persists day and night; intermittent madness does not nullify wakalah. A significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is presented: Imam Abu Yusuf gives two opinions on the minimum duration — one month (based on qiyas with Ramadan fasting) or one day and night (based on dropping of prayers), while Imam Muhammad holds it to be one year (based on dropping of all annual obligations). The passage then addresses apostasy. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that an apostate's contracts are suspended (mawquf): if he returns to Islam, the wakalah becomes effective; if he dies or goes to Dar al-Harb, it becomes void. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the apostate's transactions remain effective (nafidh) during apostasy, so the wakalah continues unless the apostate dies or is executed. Finally, the passage notes an exception for a female principal: if a woman apostatizes, her wakalah remains valid by consensus because a female apostate is not executed; her capacity is deemed unaffected. The passage thus provides a detailed exposition of the limits of agency termination within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ردت (riddah): Apostasy; abandonment of Islam. In this context, it is one of the events that may nullify the wakalah contract.
جنون مطبق (junun mutbiq): Continuous madness that lasts without interruption. The text discusses its definition and minimum duration according to different Hanafi imams.
وکالت (wakalah): Agency; a contract where one person appoints another to perform a legal act on their behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens to the wakalah if the principal apostatizes and then returns to Islam?
A) The wakalah becomes batil permanently.
B) The wakalah is revived and becomes effective.
C) The wakalah remains suspended until the principal's death.
D) The wakalah is unaffected by apostasy.

Key Takeaway
Wakalah terminates upon death, continuous madness, and apostasy, but the Hanafi school has internal differences on the definition of continuous madness and the immediate effect of apostasy.

Constructive Dismissal of Agency
Ruling statements on three specific cases of automatic termination of wakalah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Hanafi cases where wakalah becomes void automatically and explain the concept of azl hukmi (constructive dismissal) contrasting it with intentional dismissal.

Core Idea
Agency terminates automatically when the principal's command ceases – knowledge of the event is irrelevant.

In Hanafi law, agency (wakalah) is built on the principal's authority (amr). When that authority vanishes due to a change in the principal's status, the agency must end. This lesson presents three specific situations where the agency becomes void without any explicit revocation and without requiring the agent's knowledge. Understanding these cases clarifies a fundamental principle: the agent's authority is derivative and dissolves when the principal's legal capacity to command is lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Events
Read the Arabic text and list the three principal-side events that cause the wakalah to become void: incapacity of a mukatib, restriction of a ma'dhun lahu, and separation of partners. Note that these events happen to the principal, not the agent.
These are changes in the principal's legal capacity or status.
2
Understand the Principle Behind Automatic Termination
The text states that the continuance of wakalah depends on the existence of the principal's command (amr). In each of the three events, the principal's command ceases to exist legally. For example, when a mukatib becomes incapable, he no longer has the authority to command an agent. The agency therefore cannot survive.
The principle is: 'بقاء الوكالة يعتمد قيام الأمر'.
3
Distinguish Between Constructive and Intentional Dismissal
The text introduces the term 'azl hukmi' (constructive dismissal). In constructive dismissal, the agent is removed without the principal's active revocation, and the agent's knowledge is not required. In intentional dismissal (azl qasdi), the principal actively revokes, and the agent must know for the revocation to take effect.
The analogy: if a principal sells the item the agent was appointed to sell, the agent's authority ends even without knowledge.
4
Apply the Ruling to the Cases
For each of the three cases, confirm that the wakalah becomes batil (void) regardless of whether the agent knew. Consider a scenario: a mukatib appoints an agent to sell his business, then becomes insolvent. The agency ends immediately even if the agent sells later – the sale is invalid.
This prevents transactions from being made under an authority that no longer exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مکاتب نے وکیل کیا پھر عاجز آ گیا یا ماذون لہ نے وکیل کیا پھر وہ مجبور ہو گیا یا دوشریکوں نے وکیل کیا پھر وہ جدا ہو گئے تو یہ وجوہ وکالت کو باطل کر دیتی ہیں۔
قال واذا وكل المكاتب ثم عجز او الماذون له ثم حجر عليه او الشريكان فافترقا فهذه الوجوه تبطل الوكالة على الوكيل علم او لم يعلم لما ذكرنا ان بقاء الوكالة يعتمد قيام الامر وقد بطل بالحجر والعجز والافتراق ولا فرق بين العلم وعدمه لأن هذا عزل حكمى فلايتوقف على العلم كالوكيل بالبيع اذا باعه المؤكل.
ترجمہ اور جب مکاتب نے وکیل کیا پھر وہ عاجز ہوگیا یا ماذون لہ نے وکیل کیا پھر وہ مجبور ہوگیا یا دوشریکوں نے وکیل کیا پھر وہ جدا ہو گئے تو یہ وجوہ وکیل پر وکالت کو باطل کر دیتی ہیں ۔ وکیل کو علم ہو یا نہ ہو کیونکہ ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ وکالت کی بقا قیام امر پر موقوف ہے اور مؤکل کا امر حجر، عجز، اور افتراق سے باطل ہو گیا اور علم اور عدم علم کے درمیان فرق اس لئے نہیں کہ یہ عزل حکمی ہے لہذا یہ وکیل کے جاننے پر موقوف نہ ہوگا ۔ جیسے وکیل بالصبح جب مؤکل نے مبیع کو فروخت کیا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مکاتب نے کسی کو وکیل کیا اور پھر مکاتب، بدل کتابت ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہو گیا یعنی پھر رفیق ہو گیا۔ یا عبد ماذون لہ نے کسی کو وکیل کیا پھر مولی نے اس کو تجارت کرنے سے روک دیا یا دو شریکوں میں سے ایک نے کسی تیسرے آدمی کو وکیل کیا پھر وہ دونوں جدا ہو گئے یعنی شرکت باقی نہ رہی تو ان تمام صورتوں میں وکالت باطل ہو جائے گی وکیل کو ان چیزوں کا علم ہو یا نہ ہو کیونکہ ہم پہلے ذکر کر چکے ہیں کہ وکالت کی بقاء موکل کے حکم کی بنا پر موقوف ہے اور مذکورہ صورتوں میں موکل کا حکم باطل ہو جاتا ہے یعنی عبد ماذون لہ کا حکم حجر کی وجہ سے اور مکاتب کا حکم عجز کی وجہ سے اور شریکین میں سے کسی ایک کا حکم افتراق کی وجہ سے باطل ہو جاتا ہے اور ان صورتوں میں وکیل کے علم اور عدم علم میں فرق اس لئے نہیں کیا گیا کہ ان صورتوں میں وکیل کا معزول ہونا امر حکمی اور غیر اختیاری ہے یعنی ان صورتوں میں معزول کئے بغیر وکیل معزول ہو جاتا ہے اور وکیل کا جاننا عزل قصدی اور ارادی کے لئے شرط ہے نہ کہ عزل حکمی کے لئے یعنی اگر مؤکل بالقصد اور بالاختیار اپنے وکیل کو معزول کرے تو معزول ہونے کے لئے وکیل کا جاننا ضروری ہے اور اگر موکل کے اختیار و ارادہ کے بغیر ہی وکیل معزول ہوا تو وکیل کا جاننا ضروری نہیں ہے بہر حال مذکورہ صورتوں میں وکیل کا عزل حکمی اور غیر اختیاری ہے تو یہ معزول ہونا وکیل کے علم پر موقوف نہ ہوگا بلکہ وکیل بہر حال معزول ہو جائے گا خواہ اس کو علم ہو یا نہ ہو۔
If a mukatib appointed an agent and then became incapable, or a ma'dhun lahu appointed an agent and then was restricted, or two partners (one of them) appointed an agent and then they separated—these causes invalidate the agency on the agent, whether he knows or not. He (the author) said: And if the mukatib appointed an agent and then became incapable, or the ma'dhun lahu then he was restricted, or the two partners then they separated, these causes invalidate the agency on the agent, whether he knows or not, because we have mentioned that the continuance of the agency depends on the existence of the command, and the command has become invalid due to restriction, incapacity, and separation. And there is no difference between knowledge and ignorance because this is a constructive dismissal ('azl hukmi), so it does not depend on knowledge, just as when the principal sells the sold item (while the agent is appointed to sell). Explanation of the case: If a mukatib appointed someone as agent and then the mukatib became incapable of paying the kitabah, i.e., he became destitute; or a ma'dhun slave appointed an agent and then the master prevented him from trading; or one of two partners appointed a third person as agent and then the two partners separated, i.e., the partnership ceased to exist—in all these cases the agency becomes void, whether the agent knows of these events or not. Because we have previously mentioned that the continuance of the agency depends on the principal's command, and in the mentioned cases the principal's command becomes invalid: the command of the ma'dhun slave becomes invalid due to restriction (hajr), the command of the mukatib due to incapacity, and the command of one of the two partners due to separation. And in these cases, no distinction is made between the agent's knowledge and ignorance because in these cases the agent's dismissal is a constructive (hukmi) and involuntary matter; that is, in these cases the agent is dismissed without an explicit dismissal, and the agent's knowledge is a condition for intentional and voluntary dismissal, not for constructive dismissal. That is, if the principal intentionally and voluntarily dismisses his agent, then the agent's knowledge is necessary for the dismissal to take effect; but if the agent is dismissed without the principal's intention and will, then the agent's knowledge is not necessary. In any case, in the mentioned cases the agent's dismissal is constructive and involuntary, so this dismissal does not depend on the agent's knowledge; rather, the agent is dismissed in any case, whether he knows or not.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage presents three specific cases where an agency contract (wakalah) becomes void due to changes in the principal's legal capacity, and it introduces the important concept of 'constructive dismissal' (azl hukmi). The three cases are: (1) a mukatib (a slave under a contract of manumission) who appointed an agent and then becomes incapable of paying the kitabah installments; (2) a ma'dhun lahu (a slave permitted to trade) who appointed an agent and then his master places a restriction (hajr) on him, revoking the permission; (3) one of two partners who appointed an agent and then the partnership dissolves. In all these cases, the agency is terminated automatically (batil) regardless of whether the agent knows about the event. The reason is that the continuance of wakalah depends on the ongoing existence of the principal's command (amr). When the principal's command ceases—due to incapacity, restriction, or dissolution of partnership—the legal basis for the agency vanishes. The author distinguishes this 'constructive dismissal' from 'intentional dismissal' (azl qasdi). In intentional dismissal, the principal explicitly revokes the agency, and that revocation only takes effect when the agent learns of it. But in constructive dismissal, the termination occurs by operation of law, and no knowledge is required. The analogy given is that of an agent appointed to sell a specific item: if the principal sells the item himself, the agent's authority is extinguished even if the agent does not know. Thus, these cases reinforce the principle that wakalah is inherently dependent on the principal's capacity and command.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatib): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission (kitabah) with his master, agreeing to pay a sum for his freedom. In this context, his incapacity to pay nullifies the agency he appointed.
ماذون لہ (ma'dhun lahu): A slave who has been given permission by his master to engage in trade. In this context, if the master restricts him (hajr), the slave's command ceases and his agency appointment becomes void.
عزل حکمی (azl hukmi): Constructive dismissal; termination of agency by operation of law due to a change in the principal's status, without requiring the agent's knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following events does NOT cause a constructive dismissal (azl hukmi) of an agent according to this passage?
A) The principal (mukatib) becomes incapable of paying kitabah
B) The principal (ma'dhun lahu) is restricted by his master
C) The agent becomes insane
D) Two partners separate after one appointed an agent

Key Takeaway
Wakalah terminates automatically without agent knowledge in three Hanafi cases: mukatib's incapacity, ma'dhun lahu's restriction, and partnership dissolution – all instances of constructive dismissal (azl hukmi).

Invalidation of Agency Due to Agent's Death or Continuous Insanity
Clear ruling on agency invalidation due to agent's death or insanity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that an agent's death or continuous insanity voids the agency and explain the reason based on the agent's loss of legal capacity to be commanded.

Core Idea
Death or permanent insanity voids agency — the agent can no longer be validly commanded.

This lesson covers two clear, undisputed cases from the Hanafi school: when the agent dies or becomes permanently insane (junun mutbiq), the agency contract becomes void immediately. The reason is straightforward: the agent must be a legally capable person for the principal's command (amr) to be valid. These rulings are foundational for understanding the more complex issues of agency termination.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two events
Death or continuous insanity of the agent.
Continuous insanity (junun mutbiq) means no lucid intervals.
2
State the legal consequence
Agency becomes void (batalat).
The contract terminates immediately.
3
Explain the legal cause
The agent's capacity to be commanded (amr) ceases upon death or insanity.
Validity of agency requires the agent to be capable of receiving and executing commands.
4
Confirm the ruling's status
This is an agreed-upon ruling within the Hanafi school.
No dispute among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

كتاب الوكالة
ہو یا نہ ہو۔
جیسے اگر کوئی شخص وکیل بالبیع ہو اور پھر مؤکل اس شی کو خود فروخت کر دے جس کو فروخت کرنے کا وکیل کیا تھا تو وکیل معزول ہو جائے گا خواہ اس کو معلوم ہو یا نہ معلوم ہو ۔ کیونکہ موکل کے اس شی کو فروخت کرنے کے بعد وکیل کے تصرفات کا محل باقی نہیں رہا تو وکیل کی وکالت بھی باقی نہ رہے گی۔
وکیل فوت ہو جائے یا جنون مطبق ہو جائے تو وکالت باطل ہے
قال واذا مات الوكيل او جن جنونا مطبقاً بطلت الوكالة لانه لا يصح امره بعد جنونه وموته وان لحق بدار الحرب مرتدا لم يجز التصرف الا ان يعود مسلما قال وهذا عند محمد فاما عند ابي يوسف لا يعود الوكالة لمحمد ان الوكالة اطلاق لانه رفع المانع اما الوكيل يتصرف بمعان قائمة به وانما عجز بعارض اللحاق لتباين الدارين فاذا زال العجز والاطلاق باق عاد وكيلا ولابي يوسف انه اثبات ولاية التنفيذ لانه ولاية أصل التصرف باهلية وولاية التنفيذ بالملك وباللحاق لحق بالأموات وبطلت الولاية فلا تعود كملكه في ام الولد والمدبر ولو عاد المؤكل مسلما وقد لحق بدار الحرب مرتدا الا تعود الوكالة في الظاهر وعن محمد انها تعود كما قال فى الوكيل والفرق له على الظاهر ان مبنى الوكالة فى حق المؤكل على الملك وقد زال حــق الـــوكـيـــل عــلــى عنی ق قــــائـــم بــــــه ولـم يـــــزل بــــــالـــلـــحــــــاق
ترجمہ اور جب وکیل مر گیا یا اس کو جنون مطبق ہو گیا تو وکالت باطل ہوگئی اس لئے وکیل کا مامور ہونا اس کے مجنون ہونے اور مر جانے کے بعد صحیح نہیں ہے اور اگر وکیل مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب میں مل گیا تو اس کا تصرف جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ وہ مسلمان ہو کر واپس آئے ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ یہ امام محمد کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اسکی وکالت عود نہیں کرے گی ۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکالت تو اطلاق ہے کیونکہ وہ مانع دور کرنا ہے اور رہا وکیل تو وہ ایسے معانی کی وجہ سے تصرف کرتا ہے جو اس کے ساتھ قائم ہوتے ہیں اور وکیل تباین دارین کی وجہ سے عارض طاق کے سبب عاجز ہو گیا پھر جب عجز زائل ہو گیا اور اطلاق باقی ہے تو وہ وکیل ہو کر عود کر آیا اور ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ توکیل، ولایت تنفیذ کا ثابت ہونا ہے کیونکہ وکیل کو اصل تصرف کی ولایت تو اپنی لیاقت سے حاصل ہے اور نافذ کرنے کی ولایت ملک سے حاصل ہے اور دارالحرب میں جانے سے مردہ لوگوں کے ساتھ مل گیا ہے اور ولایت باطل ہوگئی تو وہ عود نہ کرے گی جیسے ام ولد اور مدبر میں اس کی ملکیت عود نہیں کراتی ہے اور اگر موکل مسلمان ہو کر واپس آیا حالانکہ وہ مرتد ہو کر دارالحرب کے ساتھ مل گیا تھا تو ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق وکالت عود نہیں کرے گی اور امام محمد سے روایت ہے کہ وکالت عود کرے گی جیسا کہ امام محمد نے ولیاں کے بارے میں کہا ہے اور ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق امام محمد کے قول پر فرق یہ ہے کہ وکالت کی بنیاد موکل کے حق میں ایسے معنی پر ہے جو اس کے ساتھ قائم ہیں اور دار الحرب میں چلے جانے سے وہ معنی زائل نہیں ہوئے ۔ تشریح گذشته صفحات میں ان عوارض کو بیان کیا گیا ہے جو موکل کی جانب سے وکالت کو باطل کرنے والے ہیں۔ اب یہاں ان عوائش کا بیان ہے جو وکیل کی جانب سے وکالت باطل کرنے والے ہیں۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ اگر وکیل مرگیا یا اس کو جنون مطبق ہو گیا تو وکات باطل ہو جائے گی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکیل کے مجنون ہونے اور مر جانے کے بعد اس کا مامور اور وکیل ہونا درست نہیں ہے حالانکہ صحت وکالت کے لئے یہ بات ضروری ہے کہ وکیل کا نامور ہونا برابر مسیح رہے۔ پس جب جنون مطبق اور مر جانے کے بعد وکیل کا مامور ہونا صحیح نہ رہا تو وکالت بھی باقی نہ رہے گی بلکہ باطل ہو جائے گی تو بحکم وکالت اس کا تصرف کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ الا یہ کہ وہ دارالحرب سے دار الاسلام میں مسلمان ہو کر لوٹے یعنی اگر وکیل مرتد مسلمان ہو کر دار الحرب سے دارالاسلام میں واپس آ گیا تو محکم وکالت اس کا تصرف جائز ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ مسلمان ہو کر واپس ہونے کی صورت میں وکیل کے تصرف کا جائز ہونا حضرت امام محمد کا مذہب ہے ورنہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک باطل شدہ وکالت عود نہ کرے گی اگر چہ وکیل مسلمان ہو کر واپس آئے۔ حضرت امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکالت تصرف کے اطلاق اور اجازت کا نام ہے کیونکہ وکالت مانع اور رکاوٹ کو دور کرنے کا نام ہے یعنی وکیل کو موکل کے معاملات میں تصرف کرنے سے شرعا ممانعت تھی لیکن جب مؤکل نے وکیل بنا کر ممانعت دور کر دی تو وکیل کے لئے اجازت حاصل ہو گئی اور تصرف کرنے کے لئے وکیل کا ہاتھ کھل گیا۔ اور رہا کیل تو وہ ایسے معانی کی وجہ سے تصرف کرتا ہے۔ جو معانی اس کی ذات کے ساتھ قائم ہیں یعنی اس کا آزاد، عاقل، بالغ ہونا حاصل یہ کہ بذریعہ وکالت موکل کی طرف سے وکیل کو تصرف کرنے کی اجازت بھی حاصل ہو گئی اور وکیل، حریت عقل اور بلوغ کی وجہ سے تصرف کرنے کا اہل بھی ہے لیکن وکیل ایک عارض کی وجہ سے تصرف کرنے سے عاجز ہو گیا اور وہ عارض وکیل کا دارالحرب میں چلا جانا ہے کیونکہ دارالاسلام اور دارالحرب میں تبائین ہے۔ پس تائین دار کیوجہ سے وکیل تصرف کرنے سے عاجز ہو گیا لیکن جب مرتد وکیل مسلمان ہو کر دار الاسلام میں واپس آ گیا تو بجر عن التصرف زائل ہو گیا اور مؤکل کی طرف سے اجازت برابر قائم ہے پس جب مؤکل کی طرف سے اجازت قائم ہے اور عجز زائل ہو گیا تو وکیل سابقہ وکالت پر عود کر آئے گا اور بحیثیت موکل کے لئے تصرف کرنے کا مجاز ہو گا۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وکالت ، تصرف کا نام نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ تصرف نافذ کرنے کی ولایت کا نام وکالت ہے کیونکہ وکیل کو اصل تصرف کی لیاقت حاصل ہے پس وکیل کل کے مال میں تصرف کی لیاقت تو رکھتا ہے لیکن اس کو یہ تصرف جائز نہیں ہے اور تصرف نافذ کرنے کی ولایت اس وقت حاصل ہوتی ہے جب وہ اس تصرف کا مالک ہو پس جب مؤکل نے کسی کو وکیل کیا تو وکیل اس تصرف کا مالک ہو گیا پھر جب وکیل دار الحرب میں مل گیا تو وہ مردہ آدمیوں کے ساتھ مل گیا اور جب وکیل مردہ آدمیوں کے ساتھ مل گیا تو اس کی ملک باطل ہو گئی۔ کیونکہ مردہ آدمی، مالک ہونے کی اہلیت نہیں رکھتا ہے اور جب وکیل کی ملک باطل ہوگئی تو اس کی ولایت بھی باطل ہو گئی۔ یعنی تصرف نافذ کرنے کی ولایت نہیں رہی اور باطل شدہ چیز چونکہ عود نہیں کرتی اس لئے تصرف نافذ کرنے کی ولایت عود نہیں کریگی ۔ اور مسلمان ہو کر دار الاسلام میں واپس آنے سے وکیل کی سابقہ وکالت حاصل نہ ہو گی۔ جیسے ام ولد اور مدبر میں اس کی ملکیت عود نہیں کرتی ہے یعنی اگر وکیل مذکور مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب میں مل گیا یعنی قاضی نے اس کے حربی ہونے کا حکم دیدیا تو اس کی ام ولد باندی اور مد بر غلام آزاد ہو گئے کیونکہ مدبر اور ام ولد ، مولی کے مرنے سے آزاد ہو جاتے ہیں اور مولی کا دارالحرب میں مل جانا بھی مرنے کے برابر ہے اس لئے یہ دونوں آزاد ہو جائیں گے اب اگر وکیل مذکور مسلمان ہو کر واپس آیا تو اس کی ام ولد اور مد بر دوبارہ اس کی ملکیت میں نہیں آئیں گے اسی طرح اس کی وکالت بھی عود نہ کرے گی یعنی اس کو تصرف نافذ کرنے کی ولایت حاصل نہ ہوگی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مؤکل مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب میں مل جائے اور پھر مسلمان ہو کر دار الاسلام میں واپس آ جائے تو
And when the agent dies or becomes insane with continuous insanity, the agency becomes void, because his being commanded is not valid after his insanity and death. And if he joins the abode of war as an apostate, his disposition is not permissible unless he returns as a Muslim. He (al-Marghinani) said: 'This is according to Muhammad. As for Abu Yusuf, the agency does not return.' For Muhammad, agency is release (itlaq) because it is removal of an obstacle; as for the agent, he acts by meanings subsisting in him, and he is only incapacitated by the obstacle of joining due to the difference of the two abodes. So when the incapacity is removed and the release remains, he returns as an agent. For Abu Yusuf, agency is the establishment of executive authority (wilayat al-tanfidh), because he has the authority of original disposition by eligibility, and the authority of execution by ownership. By joining (the dar al-harb) he joined the dead, and the authority becomes void, so it does not return, like his ownership in umm walad and mudabbar. And if the principal returns as a Muslim after having joined dar al-harb as an apostate, the agency does not return in the apparent ruling (zahir al-riwaya). And from Muhammad it is narrated that it does return, as he said regarding the agent. And the distinction for him according to the apparent ruling is that the basis of agency with respect to the principal is upon ownership, and the right of the agent upon [؟] subsisting in him has not ceased by joining.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya discusses the invalidation of agency (wakalah) due to events affecting the agent. It begins by stating a clear ruling: if the agent dies or becomes permanently insane (junun mutbiq), the agency becomes void. The reason is that the agent's capacity to be commanded (amr) ceases upon death or insanity. The agent must remain a legally capable person for the agency to continue. The text then addresses a more nuanced case: if the agent apostatizes and joins dar al-harb (non-Muslim territory), his disposition is not permissible unless he returns as a Muslim. At this point, the author presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad holds that the agency is merely a release (itlaq) — a removal of the prohibition preventing the agent from acting. The agent's personal capacity (qualifications of freedom, sanity, adulthood) remains intact; he is only temporarily incapacitated by the practical obstacle of being in dar al-harb where Islamic jurisdiction does not apply. When he returns as a Muslim, the incapacity is removed and the original permission (itlaq) remains, so the agency revives. Imam Abu Yusuf, by contrast, views agency as the establishment of executive authority (wilayat al-tanfidh). According to him, the agent has natural capacity for original disposition (ahliyyat al-tasarruf), but the executive authority comes from ownership (milk) — i.e., the principal's grant of authority makes the agent 'owner' of the right to execute the transaction. When the apostate agent joins dar al-harb, he is legally considered like the dead; his ownership and thus his executive authority are void. Since a void thing does not return, the agency does not revive even if he returns as a Muslim. Abu Yusuf draws an analogy to umm walad and mudabbar slaves: when the master dies or joins dar al-harb, they are freed and do not revert to his ownership upon his return. The text notes that the relied-upon position in zahir al-riwaya (the six core books of Imam Muhammad) is that the agency does not return when the principal returns, but there is a narration from Imam Muhammad that it does return, similar to his view on the agent. The commentary explains the reasoning in detail, using analogies and clarifying the conceptual difference between 'itlaq' (release/permission) and 'wilayat al-tanfidh' (executive authority).

Key Terms
وکالت (wakalah): A contract by which one person (principal) authorizes another (agent) to perform a legal act on his behalf.
جنون مطبق (junun mutbiq): Continuous insanity without lucid intervals, as opposed to intermittent insanity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of the agent's permanent insanity on the agency contract?
A) The agency becomes suspended until the agent recovers
B) The agency becomes void immediately
C) The principal must revoke the agency for it to be void
D) The agency continues but the agent's actions are not binding

Key Takeaway
An agent's death or continuous insanity voids the agency because the agent loses the legal capacity to be commanded.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Does Agency Revive After an Apostate Agent Returns from Dar al-Harb?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on revival of agency after apostate agent's return from dar al-harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi positions on whether agency revives when an apostate agent returns from dar al-harb as a Muslim, and identify the practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
Imam Muhammad says agency revives upon return; Abu Yusuf says it does not — each based on a distinct conception of agency (itlaq vs. wilayat al-tanfidh).

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf. The case: an agent apostatizes and joins dar al-harb, then later returns as a Muslim. Does his agency revive automatically, or must the principal re-appoint him? The answer depends on how we conceptualize agency: as a mere permission (itlaq) or as a grant of executive authority (wilayat al-tanfidh). Understanding this dispute sharpens one's grasp of the nature of agency in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
State the case
An apostate agent joins dar al-harb, then returns as a Muslim. Does the agency revive?
2
Identify Imam Muhammad's position
Agency revives. Proof: wakalah is itlaq (release/permission); the agent's capacity remains; only the obstacle of dar al-harb is removed upon return.
3
Identify Imam Abu Yusuf's position
Agency does not revive. Proof: wakalah is wilayat al-tanfidh (executive authority) based on ownership; joining dar al-harb voids ownership and authority, and void things do not return.
4
Compare the proofs
Muhammad focuses on persistence of permission; Abu Yusuf draws analogy to umm walad and mudabbar.
5
State the practical thamarah al-khilaf
If agency revives, agent can act without new appointment; if not, principal must re-appoint.

محمد کے قول پر فرق یہ ہے کہ وکالت کی بنیاد موکل کے حق میں ایسے معنی پر ہے جو اس کے ساتھ قائم ہیں اور دار الحرب میں چلے جانے سے وہ معنی زائل نہیں ہوئے ۔ تشریح گذشته صفحات میں ان عوارض کو بیان کیا گیا ہے جو موکل کی جانب سے وکالت کو باطل کرنے والے ہیں۔ اب یہاں ان عوائش کا بیان ہے جو وکیل کی جانب سے وکالت باطل کرنے والے ہیں۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ اگر وکیل مرگیا یا اس کو جنون مطبق ہو گیا تو وکات باطل ہو
