Oath Refusal in Financial Claims with Incidental Lineage
Hanafi ruling with reasoning on oath refusal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that in a financial claim where lineage is incidental, the defendant's refusal of the oath establishes the financial right but not the lineage, and explain the rationale.

Core Idea
Oath refusal establishes financial rights but not lineage, because lineage requires stronger proof.

Imagine you claim maintenance from someone because they are your brother, but you have no evidence. If the defendant denies and then refuses to take an oath, does a judge rule that he is your brother? No. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rule that the financial claim is accepted, but the lineage is not proven. We will explore the reasoning and two concrete examples from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of claim
Recognize that the claim has two components: a financial right (e.g., maintenance, right to revoke a gift) and a lineage basis (brotherhood). The primary purpose is financial.
The lineage is 'incidental' (tabi') to the financial claim.
2
Apply the rule of istikhlaaf
Since the claimant lacks evidence, the judge administers an oath to the defendant by consensus. If the defendant swears, he is absolved. If he refuses (nukul), the claim is considered admitted.
Istikhlaaf is valid in financial matters (umur maliyyah).
3
Distinguish between financial right and lineage
The oath refusal only establishes the financial claim, not the lineage. The text explicitly states that maintenance is decreed but brotherhood is not established.
This is because lineage (nasab) is a personal status matter that requires more stringent proof (e.g., bayyinah or acknowledgment without affecting third parties).
4
Identify the rationale (talil)
The rationale given: 'Because the purpose of these rights is financial' – i.e., the claim revolves around money, not lineage. Since istikhlaaf is valid for financial rights, it applies. The lineage is not the intended objective.
This reasoning (talil) underpins the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت کی طرف بچہ کومنتقل کرنے کا حکم دیدیا جائے گا لیکن نسب ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ یعنی مدعیہ عورت کا اس بچہ سے رشتہ اخوت ثابت نہ ہوگا یا مثلا نفقہ کا دعوی کیا اس طور پر کہ ایک شخص نے دعوی کیا کہ فلاں یعنی شاہد میرا بھائی ہے اور مالدار ہے لہذا میر ا نفقہ اس پر واجب ہے مدعی یعنی شاہد نے اخوت کا انکار کیا اب اگر مدعی بینہ پیش نہ کر سکا تو مدعی علیہ یعنی شاہد سے بالاجماع قسم لی جائے گی ۔ چنانچہ اگر وہ قسم کھا گیا تو نفقہ سے بری ہو جائے گا اور اگر قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو مدعی کے لئے نفقہ کا فیصلہ تو کر دیا جائے گا لیکن نسب کا فیصلہ نہ ہوگا یعنی رشتہ اخوت ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ یا مثلاً قرابت کی وجہ سے ہبہ میں رجوع کے ممتنع ہونے کا دعوی کیا اس طور پر کہ اگر واہب نے شی موہوب کو رجوع کرنا چاہا اور موہوب لہ نے کہا تو تو میرا بھائی ہے اور منشاء یہ ہے کہ تجھ کو رجوع کرنے کا حق نہیں رہتا ہے۔ پس اگر مدعی علیہ یعنی واہب نے اس کا انکار کیا اور مدعی یعنی موہوب لہ کے پاس بینہ نہ ہوا تو مدعی علیہ ( واہب ) سے بالاجماع قسم لی جائے گی پس اگر اس نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو رجوع فی الہبہ کا متمتع ہونا ثابت ہو جائے گا لیکن نسب یعنی رشتہ اخوت ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ لان المقصود لهذه الحقوق سے صاحب ہدایہ نے مذکورہ تمام مسائل کی دلیل بیان کی ہے یعنی مسائل مذکورہ میں نسب مقصود نہیں ہے بلکہ مذکورہ مالی حقوق مقصود ہیں اور مالی حقوق میں استخلاف جاری ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا مذکورہ مسائل میں بھی استخلاف جاری ہوگا۔
The ruling will be given to transfer the child to the woman, but lineage will not be established. That is, the woman's relationship of brotherhood with this child will not be established, or for example a claim of maintenance in such a way that a person claimed that so-and-so (the witness) is my brother and is wealthy, therefore maintenance is obligatory upon him. The claimant (the witness) denied the brotherhood. Now if the claimant could not produce evidence, then the oath will be administered to the defendant (the witness) by consensus. Thus, if he takes the oath, he will be absolved of maintenance, and if he refuses to take the oath, then maintenance will be decreed for the claimant, but the lineage will not be decreed, i.e., the relationship of brotherhood will not be established. Or for example, a claim of prevention of ruju' in hibah due to kinship, in such a way that if the donor wished to revoke the gifted property and the donee said, 'You are my brother,' meaning that you no longer have the right to revoke. Then if the defendant (the donor) denied this, and the claimant (the donee) had no evidence, then the oath will be administered to the defendant (the donor) by consensus. Then if he refuses to take the oath, the entitlement to ruju' in hibah will be established, but the lineage (i.e., the relationship of brotherhood) will not be established. Because the purpose of these rights: the author of Hidayah has explained the proof for all the mentioned cases, i.e., in these cases lineage is not intended, rather the mentioned financial rights are intended, and istikhlaaf (administering the oath) is valid in financial rights. Therefore, in these cases istikhlaaf will also be valid.
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding claims where the primary objective is a financial right, but lineage (nasab) is incidentally mentioned as a basis. The commentator uses two examples: a claim for nafaqah (maintenance) based on brotherhood, and a claim that a donor cannot revoke a gift (ruju' fi al-hibah) because the donee is a brother. In both cases, if the claimant cannot produce evidence and the defendant denies the claim, an oath is administered to the defendant by consensus. If the defendant takes the oath, he is free of the financial obligation. If he refuses, the financial right is established in favor of the claimant, but the lineage (brotherhood) is not legally established. The reasoning given is that the purpose of these claims is financial rights, not lineage. Since istikhlaaf (administering the oath) is valid in financial matters, it is applied here. However, lineage is only established through proper evidence or acknowledgment that does not involve third parties, and oath refusal does not establish lineage in such cases. Thus, the ruling distinguishes between establishing a financial right and establishing lineage.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlaaf): The process of administering an oath to the defendant in a claim when the claimant lacks evidence.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or familial relationship, such as brotherhood, fatherhood, etc.
نکول (nukul): Refusal to take an oath after it has been offered to the defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a claim for maintenance based on brotherhood, if the defendant refuses the oath, what is established according to the Hanafi ruling?
A) Both maintenance and brotherhood
B) Only maintenance, not brotherhood
C) Only brotherhood, not maintenance
D) Neither maintenance nor brotherhood

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a financial claim is based on an incidental lineage, the defendant's oath refusal establishes only the financial right, not the lineage, because istikhlaaf is limited to financial matters.
